O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the latest work of the science of medicine, embracing its employment in its entirety, and I have finished it through its expositions and pronouncements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to pass that I realized I must accomplish this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely surgery
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is far-flung in our region and is rare in all, if it is not learned and practiced, and if it is not refreshed, the science and art of it are lost, and nothing remains of it but the little descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have moved
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And this is the source of error and idleness, and the minds are closed and the science is confused.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I can make it live together the ordination of this practitioner according to the way of exposure and declaration and the abbreviation; and I will come together the forms of the fire cautery instruments and other things of the work with the agreement of the declaration and preparation of the patient, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or it seems to me that I can give life to this treatment in its entirety according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of the cautery instruments, and other implements of the work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary. And because none of our masters of hands can be found in our time, the art of medicine is prolonged
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary that he who undertakes this should be well versed in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he understands the structure of the limbs, the shapes and joints and separations of bones, and knows the bones and nerves and muscles and joints, and the number of bones, and the movement and rest of them, and their issues.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And thus Ipocras said that one should not go about it without the non and with the work it is thus;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We say in the beginning of this book that whoever is not learned in the things that are before said, if he dares to speak in error and to blame the homes;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Therefore, many times I have seen more of these things which intervene in this science and abandon its science and sense for experiment.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I have seen fools who coppied I apostume of scrofula or a woman’s neck, and coppied the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood flows out that the woman dies between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I have seen another fool who treated a stone of a wound, and the stone was great
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	if he carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and was dead for three days
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And thus I am already being called to deal with it, and see the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and know well if one should cut deeply into it, for it would surely kill him.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	and I have seen another fool who treated the duke of our land who had a broken limb, and with the treatment made him worse.
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	And the sight of ignorance hinders the bursting forth upon the wound as it is held fast by a strong ligament, and does not allow the wound to bleed at all, and leaves it unclosed at the end.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	It commands that it should not be detached from me.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And thus, when the limb has fled and the bone has gone astray, it has perished
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I call for help to come and I hasten to unfasten the limb
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	And when I see it dislocated, if it is quiet and causes no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But every way corruption is already confirmed or the limb is ruined, and it will not heal;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And it continues to corrupt the limb as long as the limb is entirely lost
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus another wrinkle that undermines the flesh, enflames and burns from the malice of its lord
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a wound caused by melancholy humours does not suffice except for touching it with iron when it is not in any other part of the body where it can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this reason, very skillful physician, you must know that the hand is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, thumb or there is peril in several positions.
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each chapter where there is doubt and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For you must always bear this in mind, so that the fools do not speak badly of you
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your arms in custody, and undertake your patients gently and firmly, and use the better way, then by the grace of God you will come to health and be praised
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the contagious diseases far behind with sobriety and sanitation
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and keep your arms from that which makes you doubt, and have faith that you will pass from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	The hairs grow long and even: if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady until they grow.
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take me in charge of any bad ailment, for I am not called a fool by chance.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise in three chapters
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter deals with fire cautery and the treatment of acute diseases, and this chapter commands from the head down to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the forms of instruments, and forceps for cautery, and everything that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter deals with drawing out and piercing, and abscesses, and wound treatment, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; or where there is doubt and fear, many die
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and this chapter commands and the forms of instruments
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	And it is ordained from the lords above to hold the head of the shoulder up to the wrist, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	When we remember our works, it is clear that I must say the quality of the help and the danger of neglecting certain complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of the helper, and the doubt, are the longest words and the subtlest science and the greatest secret response.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and about these things they speak many times in this book, and agree with this.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I am overcome by them because of their words, for I am reducing the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that the cautery helps universally in every complexion or where there is matter, for it is two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say complexion hot with matter, and complexion dry with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In complexion hot and dry together with matter, they do not say that there is no benefit, and they say that the cautery is a great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	And the others say the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	And the others say the opposite: that cautery is of no use in diseases that arise from heat and drought.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and must not be used to cure heat-related diseases by heat, nor by drought;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and they say that indeed it does great help in dry and heat-related diseases that arise in summer in the houses.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you compare the body of a man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never seen such a thing happen before in experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in all ways, fire should not be used except for those who have experience in it, and who know by long experience the chapter of cautery, and the variety of complexions of houses, and the causes and dispositions of their diseases, and the issues and the space of tension
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	of other complexions we have no fear, even in cold and moist diseases
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And you must all understand and agree to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know that fire cautery is more effective for certain secrets than burning cautery.</start_of_turn>
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The healing medicines of fire come from one member to another in aligning, and cause the sick limb to regain health from grief.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and sometimes cause the patient great pain.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its height and for the goodness of its substance, does not make this worse, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have learned through experience and by the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and it is confirmed by the truth of things
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and because of this I excuse myself for the length of the speech, for it does not please me to keep secret the secret which is reported or the fire, and the quality of the work, as it expels the diseases of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Or leSuivez en vos pensées.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know then, child, that it is fitting in what way the cauteries should be performed and when they are urgent.</start_of_turn>
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	Or I say that cautery is permissible in all cases, for the harmful things that follow are driven away by the aid of the cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and even if the cautery is for necessary pains that are urgent and cannot wait until the greater harm has passed from the limb
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not think, my son, as the foolish people do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cautery does not come back
et il le dient ensi;	thus it is said.
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not so that they would care for it, for the cautery is only medicine that changes the complexion, and dries up the humors that cause pain, and is worth more than medicine for its haste, and for the value of its work and its lordship
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is known that disease does not come about at any time according to the complexion of the patient and the nature of the disease and its virtue.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	And it is assembled in him the superfluous humors by the acquisition of foods and similar things, if these are not cauterized when administered in place or if there is much superfluous humors and moisture, as with cauteries of fat due to pain, and similar things, and part of the pain does not return again.</start_of_turn>
mais ce avient poc.	But this is often the case.</start_of_turn>
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand that the cauteries are called behind medicine, and it is seen.</start_of_turn
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that the cauteries are worth after medicine, but their understanding is false, and it is the cauteries that are behind medicine because whenever we administer other treatments for any disease and they do not work, we then administer the cautery, and it is worth.</start_of_turn
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Although the cautery is often used as the last resort in medicine, it does not suit the understanding of the fools.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The old men say that gold cauteries are more discreet than those of iron, and they do not say that of other fires except for the quality of the gold and the fineness of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	They say that the smell of the cautery does not remain in the air, but this I do not believe, for I have proved it, and I have seen it in many men
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Gold cauteries are more valuable than those of iron, as they say
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	Whenever you burn an instrument of gold, you do not know whether it is golden by the color of the gold, and when it has cooled down.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	And if you burn it too much
si font au feu;	It becomes red hot
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our fire cautery, as we have observed it to be useful for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have commanded this chapter from head to foot, for this reason that they may be more easily found.</start_of_turn>
dou cautere olivaire	olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are useful for moisture and cold on the skull, and there are two methods to use them because of the disease called “soda,” and because of the many humors that descend from the head to the ears, and for many dreams and pain of the teeth and throat, and even for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	And thus the form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by medicine that changes the head three or four times, according to what is useful and agreeable and to the custom of the patient; for the patient can endure it.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	Then make the head of the patient well again.</start_of_turn>
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit comfortably between your hands, and put his hands under his feet;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	Then put the root of your thumb on the root of his nail between his two eyes.</start_of_turn
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And there you will find your two middle fingers, if it bleeds from the nail then withdraw the cautery which is called "olivare", for this is its form.</start_of_turn
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And take out the limb that shows the sign of ink, and make it descend and extract your hand back and forth, alternating.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then keep your hand steady, and rejoin the limb if you see the bone slightly out of place;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	Then take hold of it a little, put on gloves and cotton wool inside, take out the limb, and leave it for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	Then put on soft wool outside.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it on until the swelling has gone down
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound of the swelling which is called “tetrafarmaçon,” until it is healed
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And they say the old folks, the more time passes over a wound, the more it purges.
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason, if the wound is treated early, it helps quickly.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say none of these that we must leave the cautery on for so long that part of the bone is scorched, and then we must renew that which is scorched from the bone, and be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And they say that if the fire cautery is delayed too long, the swelling will burst out as large as a woman’s girdle.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	And the wound must be left open for a long time
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	then it must be cured and dressed
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good for all cases, for in some people or where there is fear of pain;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	I believe that moisture must be left there
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	For the head of the shoulder is often loosened by continuous solutions of the same kind, as we have seen in other limbs.
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And thus when the head of the shoulder is weak by nature, the first sign of the fire cautery is more soothing and limp than before, and for this reason I will abstain from it.</start_of_turn>
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From ancient times pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When there is chronic pain lasting a long time, one must use for the patient herbs, pills which are called "cochices", and vomiting of the head and oils and poultices.</start_of_turn
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	And if we do the cautery as we have said, it is of no use.</start_of_turn
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Beware if the head of the shoulder is of great strength and is not too cold.</start_of_turn
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	When the cautery is finished, then cauterize as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	When the burn is done on the limb from the shoulder down to the bone, as we have said before, and do the burn or bruise which is called a "vessel".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and put on a bandage in place.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	align your hand so that you do not see me until the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much greater pain in this burn than in others, and I will speak of it later.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	it must be understood that the cauteries of the horns must be finer than those which we cauterize the moisture of the shoulder, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When pain suddenly arises in a part of the head, and it spreads throughout the illness, the head of the shoulder is expelled by medicines that alter the body, and other treatments have been made as mentioned in the division of diseases; but all this has been to no avail.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Therefore, make incisions according to two methods, namely with water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The water cautery is when you grasp a fleshy tumor with tweezers and expose the bone underneath, and then make the temple or the part where the pain persists until you can restore the tumor under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is restored, if you bind and strain it well and leave it for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	then take off the bandage and treat the tumor with fire, and leave the wound for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then put upon the shoulder a cushion plunged into the bore as long as the shoulder blade is stiff.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then the treatment of the inflammation until it is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that you must do something of those medicines that I have written or dose treat with other medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is as it is taught in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Leave the hairs long and even on the patient.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a cup or there is little curvature, and in the middle has a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and put it outside the painful limb, and hold your hand and rest the fire a little while, until half of the thickness of the limb is burned over
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and keep your hand that the artery does not burn, that is withdrawn, and there is abundant blood

de emigraine	After having put on cotton wool around the limb for two days, and having taken it out; then I put on moist cotton wool in the hole, and finally treat the limb for swelling until it is healed; and if you cauterize this embolism with the cautery called “cultellare,” at its tip, and keep the artery in this embolism from being cut that is not ancient.

et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	If he seizes the limb with a hand's breadth of length, and grasps the hand once, and strains so that he does not cover the artery and does not live up to the bone.

de l’epilempsie	It must be that the head of the shoulder is loosened from the socket and the things we have said before; after that, raise the patient’s arm, then perform cautery on the head and shoulders, that is, behind and in front of the collarbone; and if you must do more, and the limb is moist and the patient is drowsy, and the disease is urgent, make three cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave them until the pain is gone, and keep your hand steady; after that, cure as long as it is necessary, and the cautery which is called “olive” that we have said before.

de la cure de fistule par cautere	And know that the ears of men are diverse in size, and according to that, their constraints are different; and do not be answered by the straight way to him who studies this art.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cure does not profit, then you must cauterize according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in its rightful place.
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, do not let go of his head

et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and let it rest on the head if it forms like a pine cone, gather so that it is the cautery

mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	But nevertheless, the head of the shoulder is worth moving for your work.

et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the cautery in the fat of the oil and corrupt it.

dou movement des dens	When the root of the tooth comes loose in the gums or in the socket, or in the palace, or has the root of the teeth, after that it makes pus and becomes rancid and is filled with pus and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in division, and it does no good: therefore you must cauterize it according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or perforate the fistula, and keep your hand over it until life returns to its original place; and do so once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, if you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you must do in its chapter.

de la dolor des dens	And in part therefore it remains moving if confirmed, and the joint softens restrains, and the moisture corrupts dries.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When there is pain in the tooth from cold, or if there is cold or heat, and the medical treatments do not help, then there must be recourse to cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	cautery of soot and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cautere of burn if it is such that you grasp burn of barley, and the end in a spoonful of iron or of raisin;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Cautery of burn if it is such that you grasp burn of barley, and the end in a spoonful of iron or of raisin; after take cotton and wrap over the tip of a tent, and the boil in burn built, and put on the painful tooth immediately and hold until it is cooled.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do it often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see so much moisture of wool and cotton in burn frothed, and put on the painful tooth, and put on the burn iron until the fire comes to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The burn cauteries together fire if it is such that you grasp one can of iron or raisin, and be large if the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient.

de la toust	When the lymph nodes are full of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not subject to digestion by medicines, then evacuate the fire cautery from the chest immediately, for otherwise there will be swelling. de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	De la dislocation de l’ajutoire.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement. Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.
