et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and this would be the last remedy after the treatment of wounds as long as it is healthy
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	and if the pain has spread as far as the thigh or as far as the leg, make an instrument that will hold the hair according to what you have done in the hair bundle;
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	It is the way of the learned men of our time, and I have written or treated of the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	or if there is a slight loss of blood, that the point of a knife can enter;
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and put that vessel in another vessel well plumped, and put lime, salt, and soft wax upon it, until there is one-third of an inch of powder remaining that you can easily grasp with your hand
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and leave it until it descends with water and blood or vessel plumped, then take away all that wax and pour it upon salt and lime as before
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And thus if there is much water and it is administered in the mouth of works of medicine and in cauteries of other members.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For indeed, the ointment of saffron with fumus, and if there are other medicines which we cauterize well, such as mastication of gum and honey and beeswax with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galiens tells us of a cure by which some honourees were cured of the pain of the groin and sciatic nerve, and he says that no other cure was done for them, and that they were healed at once when they had made this cure, and he bathed as he is taught afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And thus take two handfuls of green and dry comfrey, and grind them with a little fat, and put on the loin and thigh and leg where the pain persists, and bind it
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and leave it for three hours and as much as the patient does not feel the burning sensation
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter or bathe as much as the limb is relaxed, and when he has entered or washed, the pain will go away and be healed
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And ointments that no one must use with such medicines, except after the evacuation of pus.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with a piece of chaff, if there is pain it helps with honey.
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and must be done carefully.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in oil, and put it on the pit that is between the thumb and the great toe and the other that is called the fossilemma
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After taking strong pliers dry, and pressing the fire until it is charcoal, and putting it on the wool, and leaving it until it is stained.
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and repeat the cautery until the hair has grown back, and do not stop until you think it is enough, until the pain is gone;
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	This method of cautery is called "pliers cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from sitting or from percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar things like cold spreading matter, of none of these signs is the cautery useful, for it is only for what comes from the infusion of cold matter
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is advisable after this that the patient be free from foul pus or other things, that we make it on the back, loin or where the pain is, three lines marked with an indent, and five vertical lines cauterized or more according to the virtue and the amount that the patient can endure
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	And let the cautery be done according to the cautery which is called "poins.
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	And if you see, make three cauteries or four at the middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this disease comes as a small wound, and the sign of its beginning is that if it is injured, it swells and swells up; fear not
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	And you will find at the back of the spine in the loin and in us the appearance that comes after the others spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it healed, if you cauterize with the fire according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery burns some part of the spine excessively.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	If you see that the cautery has burned two or three lines deep on the spine, and that the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the wound until it is healed according to what we have said, take care that you do not cause further damage to the nerve in haste.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When the pain of joints is from moisture that is spread throughout the limb of bone, and when the pain comes from the heel, call it "podagre" properly; and when it is from cold and is cured by medicine, it cannot be cured; if it is cured by cautery in part:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the bone, if you cauterize with the whole cautery, we call that a “point”.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	Make the mouth of the cautery around the joint of the limb, and let the cautery be olive oil in this form: if there are pains that reach the knee and other joints, and this happens many times, make the cautery on each knee three cauteries or four of each part, with all the olive oil.
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you must proceed further, if you do more, but do not hold your hand firmly until the thickness of the thumb is as wide as an ass.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend down to the groin and back, administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, if you make points around the nail two lines.
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	And if there remains no pain in this area, if you make points on some joint and on the hair of the hand.
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	If the pains come up to the shoulders or up to the collarbones, if you cauterize some part, and make the patient take good care of himself and prescribe medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make him well-governed and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	If the vessel does not lose its nourishment by the incision of the veins, and if it dries and does not yield assistance.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When the fever breaks, and the bile descends like coals and is new, if you think that when you see it cured, that it will not return again;
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and that it uses things that release the belly, so that the pains descend from the belly
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	then you must make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm tight until the bile is repaired, and hold it at your sides, and mark on the skin the fever above the collarbone, and at all signs that it resembles half of a circle below the ears
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then he grasps the fire cautery; thus is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is soft and he sweats sensationless.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then he grasps the fire cautery; thus is the form: then he grasps the hair at their root.
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and he holds his hand over so that they do not move back;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and he gives well the blows to the patient, and puts a cushion and a dressing on the wounds, and another on the hand that holds the instrument; and he holds the patient’s hands firmly
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then he places the cautery on the sign at all your hand, and holds it straight and holds it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, if you do it again as many times as you live until you reach the bone
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and take care that the hair does not burn when you are doing the cautery.
que tu ne le brulasses;	Do not burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Do not burn it; and let the patient not suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And soaks that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And you must know that the cauterization of veins must be subtle in accordance with the measure of the person, and of great people also in accordance with their measure
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	After three days of treatment with the cautery of a burn, until the scab is ossified
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	After the treatment of other wounds, until they are healed, and keep the patient lying down for forty days on his back until the wound is well healed.
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And you must know that his movements must be quiet and slow, so that the fluid does not flow out when he moves from the bed to the bedroom
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wants to rise, there appears a well-made wound, and bears it for forty days.
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and has good rest, that he works little and guards against too great repletion of drink and eating, and of too high a diet;
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he has learned this, if he is sane throughout
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall tell you afterwards the treatment of the tail in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the route of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When wounds come to other parts and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow further, then you must make cautery of cautery according to their quantity, and take a third of the dose
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the cure as we have said
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with cautery at three angles according to this shape
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the limb and make a line over the belly of the wound, and another at the bottom, and hold your hand firmly over the entire cautery needle.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and softer.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	There is no ancient pain in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, or to the hip or to wound, and this pain lasts a long time, and the medical treatment is not worth it, then it is recommended to cauterize with the cautery called "pins", and to cauterize according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its toughness and its swelling and its pain
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	If he is sane after the first cautery, that is well.
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If so, repeat the cautery on that limb, for it is customary to burn the parts that are nearby, so that you can make the cauteries while the patient is still sane.</start_of_turn>
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, whether from sitting or injury, and the pain persists for a long time, the remedy of medicine is not sufficient; therefore it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "points," or with the cautery in accordance with the length of the limb, its smallness and its weakness and its toughness and its twisting and its pain. If it is cured with the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the cautery again. Indeed, it is customary that it must be burned towards the adjacent limb, for it is believed that in this way one can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The disease does not yield to cautery at any time, and even the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	Can you see that it is being cauterized? Take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured as we have said in the division, and do not linger, for you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the patient, so make five cauteries on the head.</start_of_turn
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I hold the head anew, and the other towards the front towards the end of the beard.</start_of_turn
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	And on the two corners, and one behind the heel;
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	And I leave the hand as long as the cautery approaches the bone, and as long as the scabs come out forcefully so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape.</start_of_turn>
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	And I perform the cautery on the mouse according to what is in front of me.</start_of_turn>
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if there is moisture everywhere;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	then I cauterize from these cauteries which we have mentioned before. I cauterize under the jaw and the cheek, and six on the spine of the shoulder, and one on the shoulderblade and one at the hip, and two on the two elbows.</start_of_turn
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	And upon the shoulders, and upon the tendons of the hand, and on one side of the wrist of the hands, and on the hollows of the hands.
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	And beware of the nerves that are behind the heel, that you do not burn them.
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And never perform cautery upon the bone of the heel, or upon the bone of the stomach, or upon the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And the more you do cautery, the more you will do good, and the more you will benefit from it.
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And the patients do not feel pain from the cautery if they feel it when they are well, because the flesh is already corrupted
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be known that the cautery must be great and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the handling of things.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating the wound several times with flour and honey and other cures until it is healed
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not serious, then you must perform cautery on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb;
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	Or let the cautery be made at a distance from the skin like a thumb in the thickness of the flesh.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then hold the wound steady until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	Never do we make the cautery on the hand, the arm, or the back, at the outlet of a nerve that makes the limb numb, and if so it swells the bone;
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	otherwise no one should interfere except those who are knowledgeable about the limbs and the movements of the nerves from the bone
de albaras	When swelling arises in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not completely healed, then it must be cauterized on the limb according to the size and degree of the swelling; and either the cautery should be applied once in the middle of the swelling or several times at the edge. Then it must be dressed with ointment until it is healed. And under no circumstances should cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the site of a nerve that makes the limb immobile. And if it is a bony swelling, all these things must be known about the limb and the course of the moving nerves and bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the ailment called "albaras" is inflamed, and the means of medicine are of no avail, then make a cautery of the thumb at a distance from the skin according to the thickness of the flesh until the bone is bled and its color is changed
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	Then sometimes for the cure, wheat flour with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alder, each a part.
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then mix them all together, or bind them with a cloth, and keep them warm until they are healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil starts to form, and you see it stop growing, if you cauterize at the level of the circle that appears around it, all around the boil.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And all these things say that the fire cautery is done in the middle of the abscess.
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	And I do not think that is good, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen several times that it does not work;
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And the most right thing is to cauterize around the circumference, which is called the circle, as we have said previously concerning the cautery
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When anyone has an ailment which is called "adubelati", and it delays in healing or through excessive swelling that it makes or through the hardness of the patient when decrepit (that is to say too old) and there is much blood, or for fear;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you must see it haste to heal.
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	therefore cauterize around the mouth of little cauteries by pricking.
aprés le laisse ensi.	leave it like that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see that it is perishing throughout the entire cautery, if it is hot, make the cautery smaller; for this is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this ailment which is called "adubelati" until the cauteries perceive the pain, and be such cauteries that the patient feels relief in parts as the process of decay advances.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then leave it be until it is perfectly healed
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another disease of this kind is called "corrodens," and is nothing other than a swelling of a limb, for it swells the limbs just as the fires swell the lines of dry things.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this ailment in which you can suffer cautery all together with fire, then remove the large and small cauteries quickly, as much as it is convenient for the limb or the ailment is;
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	Then cauterize all over until you have eradicated all the corruption, and nothing remains except the bone itself
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it rest for three days, and put on the cauterized limbs a bandage soaked in oil until the cauterized parts are ossified, and all the corruption is gone
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of wounds caused by these embers.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if after three days the hair does not grow back, it is well.
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if it does not, repeat the cautery on that which is left corrupt
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this swelling has never been cured by any medicine except for the fire cautery
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but every fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of the medicine that is in the section
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	take as much as you need
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	portions that come as pieces.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that when hairs grow back, a disease called “clos” appears according to our understanding, and is a great burdensome burden that causes great pain
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	The fire cautery is if you are ashamed of one cautery is like a pin of wool, and is made of good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the clot of all parts, and that there be subtle margins;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After the meat is put on the cloud, and bend your hand all the way into the cloud until it reaches the front of the cloud.
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and leave it there for three days until it starts to smell rotten.</start_of_turn>
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Then make an ointment of wild mallow broth with salt, and leave the ointment on all night, and it will be loosened from its roots.</start_of_turn>
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the swelling by applying pressure until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if it is softened by discharges of urine, and many times comes out in hands and feet, if you can, bring a hot water cautery.</start_of_turn
et est en teil maniere:	It is partly like this.</start_of_turn
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	Take a flax or iron bowl or a needle of gut, and put on the cloud and the underside, that is to say, with bumps.</start_of_turn
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	And put the bandage upon so that it covers all around, then put on a little pot of warm wax, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand as you are turning so that the edge of the bandage comes to the root of the wound, and you will find the warm water way down to the root.
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	And offer the patient a little the warmth of the warm water for an hour.
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	Then leave it like that, and it will spread all through its roots
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So do another, until you have scraped away all that is on the bone, then cure the wounds that remain and discharge the carbuncles that have formed.
li cure dou trembler	it cures trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When there are tremors of cold from nerves, or from a quartan fever or from something else, if you must do two or three cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one on the side, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If you leave it trembling, and hasten the healing of the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	When some shiver from cold or from a quartan fever or from another, if you order them to undergo three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach just below the naval; if you leave them thus, they will stop shivering and the disease will be overcome.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes from wounds appear bones bathed in pus, or boils filled with pus, which come from corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	When you see it at first that we are making cautery upon each head of the pustule.
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	A subtle cautery of mustard seed, or that which has its point grasped by the fire, or of long aristolochic root, or the lenticular cautery
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And never do the cauteries commence until they see it according to this manner, and it does not cause them to swell forward, but is broken by the excess of which they come, and they are healed;
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it must be done after the evacuation of blood
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes to the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It is a great grief to extend [oneself].
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And thus when this happens to anyone, if you are hasty to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and you strain too much without calming your thumb, and that there is no more bleeding;
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then put the olive cautery on fire several small and large ones until they are all red;
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then I take hold of it, great or small according to the wound and the limb in which the artery is blocked, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as it is not restrained
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out fiercely when you take your thumb away from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take hold of another cautery that is in the fire immediately.</start_of_turn
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	and do not cease to do this one after the other until the bleeding is stopped
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	And beware that you do not cut away the nerve which is below, and that no other evil come upon the patient.
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And so that without cutting the artery, you cannot well fill it again by itself when it is large, except in three ways that we have said.
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not otherwise treated, or by strong stitching with thread, or by medicines placed upon which have power to fill blood;
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And be bound and strained immediately thereafter.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about a rest of the limb by tightly draping it or by putting on hot things upon it, or other similar things, if this does not prove helpful in no way.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to him at no time and there is no remedy or medicine at hand, you must put two fingers upon the wound of the vein as we have said, and hold them in place until they are completely closed over the wound and the vein
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	And do not move it [the shoulder], but moisten it with cold water often so that it becomes cold as much as when it is without ice and freezes and thickens;
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	Make incisions in front of the place where the cautery and medicines are to be applied.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This sentence translates as:
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have already said in the first chapter that in all diseases where it is necessary to apply cautery or burning medicine, we must apply the cautery and medicine, and we must examine the wound and its cause and its form
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	I have placed this chapter among the others because it is more convenient for me to discuss it in this way
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, I must tell you, dear sir, that there is more danger and fear in this chapter than in all the previous cautery, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	Where there is doubt and fear, and in comes death.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you should not be rash.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in many ways people come to harm in treating.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	When such things come to pass, they bring with them such fear and anxiety that their limbs move carelessly from the violence of the disease, and from the greatness of their suffering;
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and from these things we must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And from these things one must have sense, and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am gone;
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the disease is terrible.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	I can only advise you to leave these things to those who have this custom, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not do anything rashly but prudently concerning that of which you are certain, and which you can take and leave as you please
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	And use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health is either preserved or restored;
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you to achieve lasting fame, glory, and lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our lords, you must understand and be skilled, and if you turn to the inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I vos ai ordonné ce chapitre en divisant par Chapitre, selon ce qu’il est devant ou Chapitre des cauteries, que j’vous ai devisé de chef jusques à pied, pour ce qu’il vous trouve plus facilement ce qu’il vous avez mérité.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have commanded you this chapter by dividing into chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have commanded from head to foot, because it will be easier for you to find what you have desired.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	When this disease comes from repeated assaults in childhood, and when the bail is too strong for the head of the child;
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	it does not come from any known cause that we are aware of.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	I have never seen this disease except in infants, and in all those that I have seen, it has been fatal
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	because of this, I believe it is better to leave the work in parts for treatment.</start_of_turn>
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose arm was completely filled with water, and the head swelling so much that he could not support it.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the moisture was so great that it became blood, and this blood if it is gathered under the bone above the socket, between the marrow and the bone
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and if the moisture is between the marrow and the bone, and the abscess is small, you must make a wide incision at the head of the bone
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and as long as the moisture is corrected
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and you will see the limb return to its normal shape:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the abscess is larger, if you make two incisions like a cross, following this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	and if the moisture is under the bone, and you see that the head of the bone is displaced from some part, and there is pain that increases when you press with your hand from inside, and this does not go away:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If it seems that you have made three incisions around the head of the shoulder according to this method:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, drain out the moisture with all your might.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After that, strain the edges of the incisions and remove the clots, and put in wine and oil, and leave for five days.
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Then take out the dressing, and cure the wound with stitches and ointments, and leave the head of the shoulder well drained, and give the patient dry food until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	Or another method of incision is that you look or open the greater tubercle, and gather the fluid.
car aucune fois est elle devant;	For it never appears before;
aucune fois derrier;	Never behind;
aucune fois en destre;	Nevermore in distress;
et aucune fois en senestre.	Nevermore in distress; nevermore in distress.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and beware that you do not cover the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and blood flows freely, so that the patient dies from excessive bleeding and the evacuation of moisture
de reume	When the shoulder or the armpit is open, and the filling of the liquid, and you do according to what you can bear; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and let the vein flow blood, if the patient dies from excessive bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no known disease which is called a "catarrh" of the eyes or the ear, and the disease is old, and the medical cure does not help, then the only remaining cure is to cauterize with the fire, since this will cover the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	You must therefore take care, not to cover them, that the patient makes a second dislocation
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	after you have rubbed the limb with a rough cloth until the arteries open, then straighten the patient’s neck with all your might
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look whether the vein is bleeding, and the blood from one and the other side is behind the ears, and they are returned;
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then see the bloodstained wound, then close one and the other with a sharp needle of two parts, as long as the vein is wide up to the bone, and that is as far as the large pulp of the head
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	If you see that, withdraw the sponge from the artery and tie it below, cutting as much as .ij. inches across the vein.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is tied, if blood spurts without stopping, continue to bleed upwards.</start_of_turn
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not bleed on inspection, if you must measure the amount of the space of three fingers, then close with a needle and do so until the bone is reached
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and what must be done with the blood is to put force if it is six fingers, and sometimes more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the refilling of the artery
puis regarde la plaie:	Then look at the wound.
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If it remains on the bone with a swelling, if the wound gapes widely, then strain the wound and hold it still, and cure it with oil until it is healed.
de emigrainne	If the artery does not open upon feeling, if it is thought that two fingerbreadths suffice, mark the spot and hold it firm until bone is reached; for what is to be done with blood that will be shed if more than two fingerbreadths are needed, or less, as the patient can bear, and the refilling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains over the bone point where the stitches were placed, if the wound edges do not meet, then strain the wound and tie it off, and cure it until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient dropsy comes, and acute swelling, because of the moisture of tears and the choleric humours in the temples and the ancient saliva is lost, and similar things, and it is cured by means of medical treatments and all that does not help, if the arteries of the temples are extracted and cauterized, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And as for the extraction of hair if the patient has repeated the growth of hair on his temples, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well with its beating, and is not closed like in some people who are too hairy;
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	And if it is closed, strain the patient’s neck with some cloths, then rub the limb of no rough hair, and raise the limb of warm water until the artery opens clearly
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then take the sponge which is like this:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	Then hold the skin loosely until you reach the artery, then pull it up with hooks, and remove the nails that are below the fleshy part.
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	And if the artery is thin, if the vein has its tip at the root of the bone, then cut off that part as much as necessary.</start_of_turn>
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not fixed, if it leaps out without hesitation.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And take out six ounces of blood, up to three.</start_of_turn
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	And if the artery is large, it is sufficient to ligate it twice with a strong silk thread, so that no blood flows in front of the healing of the wound, and let the blood drain out naturally.</start_of_turn
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then cut off the surplus that is between the two lines in that hour, and then if you see that the bleeding has stopped, if you burn with the cautery needle until the wound is closed.</start_of_turn
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And it is known that the malady is dull and languid, when the patient has no fever and is of fair complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the cautery is useful for finishing off moisture:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	because it is more effective for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	or it is useful for extracting arteries that are filled with much blood and put on good tension;
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are released, if they are cured by dry medicines that cause new blood to grow, and by tension, until they are healed;
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if without stopping the artery as much is said above, if you rush to cover it with cautery, or if you use the substance of vitriol and strain your hand, it will be stained
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	If you do not have this [present] on hand, put out the limb you must until it is relaxed; and raise the limb with cold water until it stops, and hold it strained as it should be.
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And that which is more rigid and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting through two parts, but the cutting must be well spaced in order to keep it longer lasting.</start_of_turn>
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too tight, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And must have between the two cuts one must have of great spacing, and then when you have signed the two bones, and you must let the burn the flesh burning over until it comes up to the bone, and close the vein in two bones.</start_of_turn
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	And must be pushed away between the two bones because it is not firmly soldered from this cautery at all.</start_of_turn
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And thus is the form of fire cautery:
des larmes	The fire cautery must have between the joints a space of one inch. Then, when you have marked the area with ink, let the loop of the instrument rest burning over until it reaches the bone, and press the skin in one inch of the loop. Let the loops be spaced between the joints because they are not soldered by this cautery in any way. This is the form of the fire cautery.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	And thus is the form of fire cautery: when the tears of the eyes descend from the veins that are above the root of the head, and it does not avail much of medical treatment in this case, you see the patient's face grimacing, and he feels pain or fear of walking as if with fear.
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and if they are tense and moist if the hair of the paper is cut, and they are scorched by the tears, if there is any hope of this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they call it the old "contusion cure," and you must make the patient who has this disease let the hair grow out over his face, and then make three incisions or equal front according to the length of the face;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	And it may be that one of the wounds has swallowed all the fat from the front as far as the jaw, and the others two have two ribs under the papers, and you must avoid incisions of the arteries that are under the papers.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	And hold your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and if there is a wound there, take hold of the amount of three thumbs to cross joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And provide a piece of sponge and cloth there to soak up the blood, and then bind the sponge tightly with two fingers of the hand that is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	of the incision which is over the temple up to the second incision.
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	And stretch out all the nerve that is between the two wounds to all the surface that is over the bone, then do the rest of the wound up to the other second, and then take out this bandage.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first fissure the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and is very well cut on one side, and on the other side is soft, do not cut deeply, for that is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge of the scalpel towards the outer side of the shoulder at the joint, and hold the cutting edge towards the bone, and hold the handle until it reaches the middle fracture line.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And take all the vessels that descend from the head as far as the incision is continuous until it reaches the opening of the vein, and then the rest make in the middle fissure until the other side of the wound.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	Then take out the blood equally, and express the limb for the blood taken out.</start_of_turn>
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	Then put in the wound a piece of cotton cloth and put on wet cloths soaked in wine and oil and in herbs, and keep that the wound does not bleed.</start_of_turn
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after three days remove the limb, and bring great healing plants of aquatint, then cure the wound basally with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.</start_of_turn
dou reume des eulz	because of the return of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When no acute burning comes, you see the pupils fixed and dilated, vomiting, and paper turning brown.
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	the hair grows thick and curly, and when they prick at their root, they cause pain that is like fire, and the patient spits out blood.</start_of_turn>
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	therefore these matters and the burning cause these evacuations, which are not due to other veins, and they bring relief rather than harm.</start_of_turn
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to recline his face, then make a great incision from ear to ear, and another one wide here below.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	From the left temple to the right temple, and from the incision up to the bone.</start_of_turn
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and hold your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move with swaying.</start_of_turn
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is discovered, empty all the blood out with a sponge, and then loosen between the two layers of the incision and put in cotton wool, and try to hold it in place.</start_of_turn
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	Then lie down under the damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, and keep your posterior warm.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When it is stiff, if you must, rub the bone until it begins to grow, and then treat it with drying things, which makes it swell up.</start_of_turn>
En teil maniere:	Part of this manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of barley flower and three parts of colophony, and make a poultice.</start_of_turn>
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	And apply it to these wounds to make them swell up throughout.</start_of_turn>
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding the ear swelling,
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that is heard in the ear is one of the three things:</start_of_turn
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or barley, or barley chaff, or stone, or other things like iron.</start_of_turn
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or semen, if like seeds, fever, pois;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or things that flow freely if like water and ease and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When he pricks in the earlobe or any other way that does not fit with the ear, do not believe in the ear, but put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, if it distills no purple oil or sesame oil, then mix in extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make it spit out the contents, and hold the nose when it spits, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and extend the ear downwards
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times comes forth from this cure;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come forth, mix in extraction as subtle as possible, for this is the form
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If the fire burns too fiercely, it causes wounds; it is good.
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	Otherwise, if it does not consume the base of the hair, it necessitates excision of the hair follicle of small double curvature.
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not burn at the base, make a mark at the root of the hair or pluck out the hair from the earlobe, and press that which is around the root of the hair so that it does not go inside with the hair
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then the fire will burn further, because many times it comes out as we have said
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out completely, take hold of the limb and put on no instrument that will cause damage, and put a pad of cotton around it
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the buttocks against the stone or whatever it may be, and pull forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	If it does not happen from all these things that we have said, if you rush to cut the ear immediately as we have said, there will be spasm.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of the incision is that if you do it first for the well-being of the head, and draw blood according to the measure of its virtue, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear downwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear at the fat or bone depending
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	or so that the incision be like the moon, as long as you reach the bone, and the bone according to your will, and suck the blood profusely from your mouth
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is as long as he is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is grains that are bruised and swell, if you administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot be cured, if you must give an emetic according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	mix in incision of that grain.</start_of_turn>
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this until you believe the grains are moistened by the moisture of the ear, until you have made many attempts;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	When the ear aches, then the patient must put on a condensor at first, and fill the ear with much cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And be it without on that ear or the pain is there already.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it is burst through that, that is good
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if this is not the case, take many pieces according to the length of your desire and hold them tensed and limp, and burn them all in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	And put the patient's ear in his hand, and take his jaw from the other side, and hold his cheek with the other hand on the cheek that is in the ear.
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	Do not cease to do this movement from thumb to thumb until the pain has passed, and when it leaps it will be all gone.</start_of_turn>
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	And if you see, take hold of the joint, and hold one of the heads in the ear, and the other head press with fire until the pain in the joint is gone.</start_of_turn
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then do the rest of the joints until the pain has passed, as we have said concerning the thumb.</start_of_turn>
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the stone, if it is of little bulk, if like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division.</start_of_turn
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	But if it is of great size, it can be felt, and necessitates the extraction of teeth.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	And this is the lighter thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	When extracting worms from the ear, when you have cured as we have said in the division, or when treating distillations, the cure does not benefit me, if you do not look at the ear in the sun:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if there are no worms, if you have extracted subtle teeth, and if they do not appear, take the tweezers accordingly, for this is the shape
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let the wound be broad and deep.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And keep the most subtle head in the ear according to the quantity of the patient’s suffering, then succeed with all the tweezers;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Leave the hair long and even; if you prick at its root, keep your eyes steady until they grow.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey by this, if you press into the cotton wool as I have said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not come out with force as we have said, if you administer distillations that the former have experienced in the incision of worms, and you will find them or treat them with distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	Or of silver or gold, these are the little ones that are lost, and over these you must distill;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and for pressing within the distillation to these instruments of gold well made for this, and if you see me take a scraper and wrap it around the tip immediately with cotton wool;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	Then I pour out my oil or juice, and whatever you see of your medicines in the can, and the can should be in the ear.

et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	And when you feel the patient is relieved, and the distillation is finished, do not leave the fire until it has cooled in the ear
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And keep it from getting too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding the ear swelling,
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without some hole in their ear
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and the same thing happens at home by bursting of wounds, or of hair growing in the ear, and these bursts never come without leaving a mark in the ear if we do not see them
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	And never has there been a time when I did not fear for my life, and I saw them all well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	When the cause of the patient’s pain comes to light, if we are unable to see it, it is a sign of serious illness in many cases; and in this case, it is clear that you put your ear close to the patient’s ailment in order to hear it.
et regarde dedens:	Look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	If you see the swelling apparent, if the limb has become completely limp and rigid, this is its form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	So be vigilant from front to back, so that it does not burst open; for if you do not heed it, your ear will bleed
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the swelling is of cartilage or bone of the ear, if you hold it tightly with slight pressure, while that bone is still fleshy.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operations are embedded in the ear, take a sharp scraper of the finer kind and burnish a little at the fire, then put in or remove the earwax.</start_of_turn
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the tingling which the patient feels at the ear, prick slightly, and keep your fingers from the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then put in the ear a plug according to the size of the hole, and the wool in an Egyptian position.
