puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If blood vessels swell, immerse a sponge and wring it out in cold water, place it on the ear, and apply other treatments that are useful for stopping blood flow which is causing the swelling.
de la char des papieres	De la char des papiers.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	Thus all these things come out of paper when the eyes are moist and dry; if you can extend them with nails and pins, and press with a spatula from their roots
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Then take out the glass vial filled with broth.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if there is no change, if the burn is done with a lenticular caustic substance and the burner does it after the incision is worth moving the limb immediately.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often it is repeated, cannot anything remain from its root;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	When they are burned by fire, if they are burnt to the root, they do not return again
de la gresle	From the grease.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Often come out on paper scraps things that seem greasy in their form and in their hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "granule", and is an accumulation of large moisture in the substance of the skin and bones;
li ovraiges est telz:	The work is like this:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take care if the great swelling moves from one side to the other, for it is an easy matter to know.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Make the great swelling swell up completely, then gently massage the chest piece, then take hold of it firmly with your fingers and hold it steady.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you do not perceive any improvement in the patient, do not grieve; for nothing is more grievous to the patient
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the fracture is great, if you assemble with a bandage, and keep it until it is healed;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not use force, for it will soon restore itself and bring relief
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	If the great swelling is descending into the ear towards the upper part, reverse the blood flow, and stretch the swelling with one finger, and hold and press from one side to the other
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	And if the marrow is loosened by the incision, it matters not.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And when the marrow is cut, let the oily liquid of the wound flow out, and heal the limb of that which engulfs hair until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the tears
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Pus is a greasy substance which is enclosed in layers of paper, and this happens more often to those who are poor, and causes great pain to their eyes, and they come to have a discharge of tears in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because of this
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And because of this, they lie with their faces downwards, and sleep on their backs, and their papers are wet with moisture which causes them to swell and appear covered in pus
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb towards your chest and feel the wax between the bones.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And thus the work is such that the patient places his head in his throat.
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then takes a fold of linen, and makes a loop in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains the excess of flesh from the chest, and puts it on it.
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and presses from both sides, so that the excess is assembled in the circle
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then makes in the middle of the moisture at the trenching of a large wound, and is not to be greater than the wound made to the vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and makes the skin in a wound as long as you see the excess;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many cases comes excess from the wound, according to the shape of a piece of white fat
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Remove the thumb completely at a right angle between your two thumbs, and bend your hand to the left and to the right as much as possible.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	And keep your fingers from being cramped in the crease, that you do not move them at all until the thumb has grown to the tip of your finger, that you do not bleed.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	If it does not emerge from the base of the crease, if you see a little piece of bone at the base of the crease, gently open the crease again until it emerges.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then remove it as we have said, then moisten the bandage and the surrounding area, and put on the limb, and support it.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if in such houses where they bruise themselves and put on to corrupt the moisture which is remaining
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure as long as it is healthy
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to the vein being cut, if the cure of closing wounds is applied as soon as it is sane.
des poilz des papieres	paper hair
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When paper nails grow long, do not clip them except as nature dictates, and keep them clean; for if you clip them, the blood will clot, and brings on various diseases like tears that are usually associated with inflammation and softening of the nails and glue, as much as this is the cause of the clotting of the blood
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And it is the cure in three ways:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	Or by whole-body cautery, or by water-medicine as it is before or alongside the fire cautery, and is done by incision and suture or by ligatures, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	You must put the patient’s hand on your left side, then turn the palm of the hand towards you;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is bent, that is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	If not, if you see a splinter under all its threads;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	then either pull out the margin of the palm or the hair will be born from these hairs, and pull out the thread from under all of it, and turn the palm up again.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	Then make in the armpit the papier, the hairs close together, at all the expanse encompassing, from the great to the small;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then draw out the thread, and put under the paper a little attempt of cotton and bandage, then mark on the paper a figure like a nail, as if like the head of a nail, and thus it is known that the figure is as much as you see elevate the paper that is destined for you.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if in a part that has suffered much, you must hold great quantity of the paper according to that which the paper is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then make at all the expanse on the two lines that you have marked, from the great to the small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And if it be one of the wounds near the hair root in the thickness of a radish, then one should apply the ointment to one of the two angles downwards, and then cover all.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	Then assemble the two layers with a staple of a needle at every thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make air the excess of threads over the two edges to all corners, as you see me do;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if this does not suffice, if there is no remedy, then leave the staple and the threads until three days or four;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then cure the wound with a bandage of dry and constricting things, for the moisture recedes at the wound heals and the reunion of the parts, but the staple is mute (as they say the old ones), and this is work with fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	And if in another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if in another way: if you mark the mark of a figure which is like the foot of a myrtle, as we have said, at three inches distance from each other according to the shape that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then hold back what is above with small forces evenly according to the form which is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you do not have the nails to hold it, and the thing is not quite equal, if you take a needle or there is a thread, and the thread will be in the mark;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and join the other thread with great loop, and the second thread with a small loop, and assemble between these two the threads equally.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then hold your hand equally, and hold all the leather over which you have marked, as we have said, and assemble the two layers of the wound by stitching, and cure until it is healed
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if the incision comes to your wound, if the surrounding area is apposed with certain cerotes and similar oily substances, it will be soothed.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	And never has it happened that the hairs of the patient have been converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	since you must use what we have said about the incision.
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the costure in one and the other is more artificial
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The cure for these wounds is in this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and that you convert the hair and the root according to what I have said, and then make two incisions by art, and two sutures as long as the hair and the surrounding area is wide;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and grasp as two cuts of two parts or hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	Then assemble one with the other smoothly above what rests on the marrow of the oil, and strain the two thumbs of the two parts forming.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	And leave it in place for a while, and the skin which is strained will tear and fester and swell, until it recovers by itself.</start_of_turn>
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it is delayed, if the pain has become great, then cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound is closed and the marrow is raised, and the hairs do not prick, they will not grow again.</start_of_turn
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two thumbs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and breadth.</start_of_turn
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The work is such that you grasp a subtle needle, and there is a thread of silk subtle.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then gather the threads and knot them together subtly, and if the length of the threads is long enough, make a palm of length
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then order in the chase another thread of silk briefly, and do not let the thread slip through the needle
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then put the patient’s hand in its right place;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and if the work is delicate, if the work is delicate, because it is a subtle and fine work, then leave the sun out so that the work is not spoiled, for this is a subtle and fine work, and put the needle at the root of the hair and make it pierce in the tissue until you bring it out in the natural way
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then withdraw the hair until above the chase, and remain in the chase that hair, if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then withdraw your hand as much as the hairs vanish from the entire chase to the tip of the palm with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the chase is treated and the hairs no longer prick with it, if you draw the chase to the outside as you have commanded, until the chase vein bursts through and you see it through the oil sight;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then you must draw the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair returns to its place and the mark disappears from above
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is little, if accompany one long hair naturally, and leave it with that or leave it alone, until it is elongated and then retain it
de la porriture de l’oil	from the putrefaction of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes into the oil, if there are two methods:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes into the oil, if there are two methods: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And comes from the wound, or from a burn or from cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way of working in this case is that you make that suture, dry the flesh of it, put in linen threads, and leave it until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and do not do anything except use dry and restrictive things in the treatment of it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do that, the disease will return worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but you must give it soft things, such as fennel
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	The acute rose or thistle and flaxseed should be boiled, and aquilon oil melted in none of the oils, and it should be wrapped around a bandage, and it should cure this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	If you take care of your wound, it will not swell as before
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And these works that we have mentioned are not fierce except in addressing this disease, for they do not regress beyond their former form.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the burn that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is of sudden onset and which truly is called "axacrati", is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	Accidents arise from wounds, cuts, cautery, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the way of this work if you take an awl, if it has two threads, and the hook in the flesh, and it makes the liquid of the armpit so that the thread of the vein is split in two at the root.</start_of_turn
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then the head of the shoulder is extended upwards to the highest point, and the scapula is abducted to a wide span.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the limb returns to its normal position as it should, that is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	otherwise, take hold and put it into the socket, and turn the limb, and make two incisions or break the bone within the limb
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and make two incisions at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make an angle so that when they are reunited, the limb should have the same shape as the letter that has not been split
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then fix the head of the shoulder, according to the quantity of its bones and cartilages, of that which sustains the limb, then join the two separated parts with a silk thread.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then comes the treatment of what we have said of soft medicines and patches, as long as he is sane.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a fracture or sprain or burn, if you must make a full incision from the hair to the skin, and as described above.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then remove between two fingers of a bandage, as I have said before.
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	And you must make the work according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the wise men appear to be of all sorts as to how to return the limb to its natural shape
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what is convenient in the work and the instruments in various arrangements
dou soudement de la papiere	And if the disease comes from a fracture or a sprain or a cautery, if you must make a full incision along the hairs of paper, as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the surgeons know best how to make it return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is convenient for him in more diverse circumstances.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When the suture comes loose at the fingers in such a manner that the thumb above is soldered with the white of an oil, and cannot move or perform its natural works, if you must, then bite the tip of a needle with your teeth and hold it high.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	And extend as pinches, as much as you can cope with the thing which is at the edge of the sensitive area, which should not be too tight nor too loose, so that the patient does not suffer too much and does not spit out the oil
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	Or make your incision, which you must loosen, gently, so that the thumb returns to its natural position
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	And is cleansed entirely of the surrounding area, and do not put in any salt or vinegar, and lift up the fresh water, and of vinegar;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then put between the paper and the oil a lint cloth, and put on the oil wool soaked in abundance of eggs.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And afterwards, use a bandage doucovered with cloths and other soft things until it is healed
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the root of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	The nails are according to two methods:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	One is nervous and seems like I soft scab, and another which is not nervous, but seems like white moisture frozen, which when touched with iron and warmed up, as if by a burn, it cannot endure;
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both of them seem to commence towards the great marrow, and cross back and forth so that they cover all the eye and the light and the movement of the oil
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And if the patient puts his head in his side, then hold the eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and keep the hand steady, then grasp the pupil as if it had small double vision, and stretch it upwards.
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put in hair of horse, or ox, or beef, and tie it firmly;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and pierce through the pupil, and tie the pupil with a thread and stretch it upwards, and scratch all around the pupil the costae of the pupil that lies under the edge of the iris, and leave the natural discharge or mucus, if in the incision there is no discharge of tears usually
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And never has the nail extended at the cuticle alone, but gradually, as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then the swelling engulfs all the surrounding soft tissue, as in this shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And keep that the soft tissue does not touch the tough membrane and breaks it, and that the pulp is not perceived;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, pour into an oil a little bit of bruised silk, and soaked in cold water, and leave it until the other evening
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure what is causing the pain until it is healed
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push out the awl, and the bone does not enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured by medicine;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And they grow as I have said in the division, and if you see them covered, if you smear oil on the patient, and take the sponge slightly moist according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And they grow as I have said in the division, and if you see them covered, if you smear oil on the patient, and take the sponge slightly moist according to this form: immediately pull out the hair gently, and if you see that it has ceased and the root is pressing, if you distill from your mouth into the oil of the coliers make of litharge and red coliers and it boils, and stamp the oil until the other side is reached.
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then repeat the work according to this same form, until it is entirely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez. de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the seed that grows on the plum tree.

des voines des eulz	des voines des eulz

de la fistule de l’oil	And if you are unable to collect everything in that hour, make a poultice upon the oil of soothing things to relieve the pain of the eyes, and leave it in place until the pain is relieved and is assured after the burn is complete; then resume in the same manner as before until it is healed; and this is the way of action.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	Moisture is called "arissati" and forms a fistula:
