Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If it does not bleed and moisture comes up to the palate, the patient is sane;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	if moisture does not flow as it should, the patient has fractured bones beneath the skin, for the instruments do not pass through without breaking them.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Therefore it is advised that you take a broad thread and loop it around the limb, and grasp it firmly with your hands, and keep between each knot no space greater than or less.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient’s hand over the dislocated limb at its root, and keep smelling until it comes out through the mouth of the limb.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times make the child do as they are taught, and it is a light matter for one who has seen it done;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes from the root with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and grasp one after the other with your thumbs as we do with a needle and thread.</start_of_turn>
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you are certain that the knot has not been damaged, then pull out the thread, dry the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian balsam, and reset the limb as before.</start_of_turn
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	Do so for three days or more, until the swelling has subsided throughout. Then apply or remove a sponge soaked in wine for several days until it has healed, and if there is need for sedative medicines, use them as well.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	This is the shape of the instrument for drawing out the head, from which we extract oils and medicines or not
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	Be of silver or gold, like an overspread lamp, like a sponge, and guide accordingly.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	And if you see, make a closed sponge, and let the instrument be flat for purging the head
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And he has one hand clasped at the head to hold it when we burn oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint on the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times there arises at the head no disease which is called "telul", and grows and becomes large again, so that it is seen like a thing;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore you must take hold at the beginning, and break the bone, then put out the fire or the burning medicine
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you delay to take hold when it is large, if you take hold too tightly, of poor color, of faintness:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if you do not touch it with iron because it is a swelling abscess, for when you take hold of it once, there comes great harm to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	And if the abscess bursts with a soft touch, not of a harsh color, you see that you can cover everything; if you see the patient vomiting and groaning in fear, cure the limb of dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and bound.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Do not leave the hairy growth for too long, but take out the hair at its root, wipe the blood, and moisten the hair with Egyptian balsam, and reinsert it as before; do this for three days or more, until the hair has eaten away everything that is left of the carbuncle; then put on or take off a cautery every other day until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them as well. This is the form of the instrument for purging the head, from which we distil oils and medicines or nothing.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary that this does not happen at all, if you observe that the wound is fresh throughout its entirety
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then immediately join the two levers to a suture, and then cure until it is healed
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the levers are already detached from one side and the other, if you can cover all the parts of their curvature until they bleed, then assemble the two levers to a suture, and tighten, and sprinkle with powdered dragon's blood and incense powder
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put upon the wound a piece of dressing of great or other dressing which sticks, and leave it until it bleeds by itself, then cure it of swelling as it becomes healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The method of stitching is as follows: if you assemble the solution.
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	from the armpits of the arms.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	At home, there is in the veins a dense paste like mustard seeds, sometimes minor and sometimes greater
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Therefore you must tear open the veins, and make incisions upon each knot, and take hold with tweezers and grasp in the middle part
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	Then apply the poultice after the incision of the vitriol, until the wound is closed.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave it [poultice] easily, and cure the wound of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the heel of the jaw.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times there appears on the gums charcoal-black spots which the old people call "albules.
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	If you support it [toothache], and hold the root, and let the blood flow out, or the blood clot;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then put out the broiling vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if it comes back after the incision, and comes many times, if the root comes out a second time, and cauterize it
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	If it does not return by itself after the cautery.
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	And these are the forms of the instruments for covering
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Never are they assembled at the head of the dens, between the teeth in the mouth, escorces that are burdensome and rough
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	Never are the teeth black and yellow and towards, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are biting;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	If you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head is in your hand, and open the teeth or the escorces wide, until nothing remains to be removed
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And thus make blackness and greenness, and yellowness and other impurities, until they are washed away
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if the bone that is at the first cause is good, it is well.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not, if it starts to slip again the second time and the third, until you have all failed;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and the teeth that they have must move in various ways, as it shows in their work, for the root of the teeth that we remove to drive out has other forms than those that remain between the teeth
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others are seen with you
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	You must know that when you cure the tooth of its pain, you must leave it alone as much as possible, for it must not be made worse
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a thing of great moisture so that we have no excuse for making it worse
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained to endure, if you wish to be certain that he will endure.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the patient complains of pain, whether it is acute or chronic, and causes the limb to tremble.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and never does the pain depart from him except when the evil is removed, for we have already wished to do it to these scoundrels.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well sure that it is the bone causing the pain, if you can, escort the limb to its root at all costs; keep it firm to prevent the bone from shifting from all sides
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then the muscle has to be pressed towards the shoulder or the scapulae at the first moment and the second time, until they are well loosened, and then firmly bind them again
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and if the head of the shoulder is in its place between your shoulders, and you keep it well still if it does not move
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, stretch the tooth outwards along the ridge; and if it does not yield, take no instruments and hold it loosely within the gum, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the wound is seen and bleeding, if it is possible, cover it with a cloth, otherwise let it bleed out.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	If the wound is bleeding slightly, do not strain too much, for it will break
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	It is necessary to keep the wound moist around the limb by using a swab to absorb the blood that escapes from it.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be careful not to break it, and leave some of the root intact, and return to the patient with the greatest pain of the first.</start_of_turn>
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	Beware that you do not do anything rash as the ignorant do, who without haste and without courage break the limb every time and bring nothing but what we have told you
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but often cause greater pain and damage to the limb due to the root of the disease or the fracture that breaks, as we have often seen
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	And when the disease is severe, if you bathe the limb in wine or vinegar and oil,
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and the blood comes away often; so often do we see it, if you use strong vinegar, it is enough to clot the blood.</start_of_turn>
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	If this does not suffice, if you cauterize.</start_of_turn
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments, which must be silent at first, must have long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you draw the tooth.</start_of_turn
et ce sont les formes:	These are the shapes.</start_of_turn
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great size if they do not bend when drawing, and be of iron well made, and be toothed so that they may hold firmly.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains when you pull, if you must put out the soft cotton wool in the wound I or II, as long as the wound is bleeding, because it holds the teeth that are loosened “algrophi”, so that the head of the shoulder seems like a beak of a rooster.</start_of_turn
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	And let the incisions be made as with a lime, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not yield to all these tensions, if you can, uncover the bark entirely around the root, and put the instrument which is called the «althali», which is to say a palanche, because of this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And be strong and wide so that if it does not break me, and if the root leaps over this, that is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	Otherwise, if you aid all the instruments, so that the forms come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has just rain, because of this form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And be these instruments strong that they cannot break, and nails that are as much as teeth of the jaws are
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	And so of other instruments, which are not counted here;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And so the master surgeon will find by himself the instrument that suits his work and the patient's disease, for there are many diseases where the old ones did not teach an instrument for the variety of things; and if it breaks not from bone or from other parts, or if it is necessary, if you seek other instruments, as I have said, and if you help with gestures, so that this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and firm to hold the bone, that it does not slip away, but can be held and grasped.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Then restore the limb with the appropriate medicines suitable for this case, and if there is decay in the bone, even if it is small, if the wound has all these instruments at hand.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear contrary to their natural course, and the form is bad, and even in women of gentle birth, if you suspect that they are decayed inside and cannot be seen externally, and are not in their proper place, they cannot be treated or comforted
adonques lou raie;	Therefore, extract it;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if it is mixed with the tooth, take this instrument which has a small beak-like shape, and be like a little spear:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	When the tooth persists too long in the gums and in the hands, for the duration of the tooth's hardness, and because you do not move the others, if it appears, it can be limed, if you use a file that has the same shape as the tooth
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	And it is also like when we make needles.
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	And like when we bite teeth together without gloves, if they do not move until they are pricked
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the face at the end has no relief, and if the tooth is too deep and bites the tongue, you must keep the biting teeth even until they are even, so that they do not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front tooth is loosened, by percussion or biting, and the patient cannot press on anything that hurts them except biting, you must treat them with restrictive medicines, which is not worth
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if you must restrain them with a gold thread, because the silver thread becomes green and corrupts, but the pain never goes away
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And let the hair be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you see the teeth leaning, if you take hold of the hair and double it between the two front teeth, then put the thumbs between the teeth next to each other, if there are one or more, until you see clearly up to the tooth opposite;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then repeat the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and cautiously, until it does not move at all.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let the suture be at the root of the tooth if it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then grasp the thumbs with pincers, assemble them, and put them between the tooth and the tongue, and hold them there so that it does not bite the tongue
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then let him hold his limb firmly as much as he can, and if it slips or the thread breaks, if the strain of another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if he should remain and serve his hold firmly, and this is the form of the teeth and the setting of the two teeth above, and the two teeth below, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	When the tooth bites, if we reset it in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and no other thing should intervene except moisture and ointment, and never make it the shape of a tooth of ivory, and put it in its place or withdraw it where it is wanting, and strain it as we have said, and remain and serve firmly long tension
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Never is this life which comes from God or nature, that we are born without.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by the sudden blow of a deep wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you must offer the mouth of the patient, and take his head in your hand, and hold the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cope the nerves of the large intestine, so that the tongue is freed from its bed, and if there is duration or it does not go away, and it is a consequence of a wound, if you see blood and cope the large intestine again
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and keep that the wound is not too deep, for the artery which comes from there
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, if you lift the limb of water-rose and easily, or cold water, then put the tongue back in its place with a little thread.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	And the patient groans in his sleep, that his limbs cannot rest.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	When blood spills forth, if you take out the glass vessel that is bleeding,
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	If it does not stop, if you cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then you must cure it with other means until it is healed
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see black or red or hard pus, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is an abscess.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is drooping with moisture, if there is moisture in it, if it bursts, and there comes out a white spittle, and you deliver from a part and from the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	If it does not go well at your work, if you put on a glass of broth that is stained, then return to your work until you have finished everything.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then lift your head easily and cautiously, and cure it of other ailments until it is healed
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Never comes from the throat boils that are called “Godath,” and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if they are hard abscesses of little size and color of rust, do not touch them with iron
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, even though it may burst blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	But leave it as long as it is whole, and then you will take it away, or it will break by itself.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is pale in colour and the root is fragile, if you have brought the instrument to cover it, but look first to see if the swelling has subsided and is calmed.</start_of_turn>
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and his limbs be in their normal position, and cover his mouth and take hold of his hands, and press the tongue down towards the instrument, for this is the form.</start_of_turn
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And be of silver or gold as thin as nails.</start_of_turn
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Can you press the tongue down towards the instrument, and you see the swelling, if you take the ointment and put it in the hollow, and draw it out more than you wish.</start_of_turn
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And do nothing with the towels, then take hold of the instrument, for this is its shape, that seems like a powerful force.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And behold, the head of the sufferer is bent, one part over the other, and is very acute, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can manage with pincers, know that this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	Or that it be split on one side, and on the other side whole;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have grasped one of the angles, if you grasp the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and remove the blood that comes out, if you gargle the patient with hot water, or if there are pomegranate seeds or wormwood leaves, or similar things, until the wound is clean;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then the remedy must be such that it is effective while the patient is still sane;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Then never arise in the throat other abscesses than the two amanduses, if the nails are thrust in like the two amanduses always.</start_of_turn>
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was not in the throat, namely one abscess of small size.</start_of_turn
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had her close the throat well so that she could neither breathe through the choked passage nor eat or drink, and died because of that.</start_of_turn
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had forced two grains out of the two holes of the nose
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I had already seen so many, and in one I had made an incision, then the fire went up, and in the going up took a great portion of the bow.</start_of_turn
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then stretch out the other limb in the opposite direction of where it hurts, and cover the mouth and press the tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After applying ointment to the abscesses, and pressing down a portion, only a little blood should escape
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	Then grasp the tongue of the woman beside the neck and make her drink water and wine, and do not cease pressing on this abscess for a long time
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	The abscesses would recede at the same time as the swelling in the body would go down, as long as I avoided vomiting, and until the great swelling disappeared
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Then I bound it and cauterized within the neck:
ensi demora sens croistre;	Then let it rest and heal in peace;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I am gone from these parts, and only God knows what happens to him after me.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the limb hangs downwards, and it flees and becomes long, if it is called a "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is thick and round, it is called an "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the wound does not profit from it, you see that the wound is appeased and is subtle; therefore you must hold it together
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round is assembled and is not too long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	And it is bloody or of a reddish or black color, so beware the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril upon the patient.</start_of_turn>
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	So be it, when you see it, according to what I have said, of its color and length, that you make the patient sit in the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we mentioned before.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then put on the ointment in the eye, and draw out the foreign body, and hold at I two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And be sure that you do not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you cover more, if it cries out with its voice and its throat;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, use of that which we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then you must know that you must use something to restrain the patient at the cautery of the painful side.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is acute and hot
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And let the patient put his head in its right place, and then press the tongue to the instrument which we have said or the surgeon of cautery, and grasp with live charcoal, if it is neither too thick nor too thin.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And make use of the handle of this instrument, for it is like this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	Or has a beard or puts medicine, as with the nails of a nail, and put the instrument over the limb;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	And the patient should keep his side against his chest, so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth over the medicine, if it does not go down to the throat, and makes a hiss
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then keep your hand on the medicine and press on the limb for the quantity of half an hour, until you see it wrinkled and the bite of the medicine is appeased.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see it, take hold and cover it with no instrument, and moisten the cloth with the medicine, and press the instrument with all your might on the wound below, until the cloth sticks to the limb.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	Do it often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it dry, and cut after three days or five
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you have to renew the cautery of the medicine, if you renew it, and after the cautery wipe the limb thoroughly with cotton wool or lint, and bandage what is around the medicine
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the water rise from a cold source, and cure the hoarseness as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, for the cautery
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	she is cured by fumigation according to this method, takes charcoal and rue and chamomile and marjoram and ivy and rosemary and similar herbs, and brings them all together in a pot, and puts oil on it, and boils.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot has the instrument that bites according to this method
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And let it be of silver or gold, and let the one of the hands bite into the patient’s mouth until the vapor rises to the eyebrow through the hole, until the eyebrow is numb;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After the redness has ceased, it often recurs as long as the wound is dry; keep that in mind when you begin the treatment of the burn, for many things happen then.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	...and do not do this until the redness has subsided.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	If these instruments are not present, take a needle and put a piece of egg-shell in the patient’s mouth, so that the patient does not suffer too much from the heat
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	because the egg-shell does not make the vapor sting the mouth, and this is a good remedy for many things
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it has happened at the throat bone or fishbone, or nothing at all;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	Therefore, if you saw it, treat what you see, and press the tongue to the sunlight with all your might, until you see the object;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what does not open your mouth and is placed in the throat, you must make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	Otherwise if it is taken out by vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of gut, or a lettuce root, or a dry breadcrumb;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie it to the sponge, and then transfix it
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes back, if it is aired, and then draw out the foreign object.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out by this, take an instrument of pliers according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the beard be trimmed at the root if it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted up.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	Beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, for if you do, it will cause him no good, nor will you drive the bone out of place.</start_of_turn>
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	Let the patient grasp the instrument, for if he is strong or the thing is slippery.</start_of_turn
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the tongue swells or bites fiercely at the instrument evenly, as much as it can.</start_of_turn
de la sansue de la gorge	And let the curved instrument rest at the head if it can more easily enter through the throat, and keep the head raised; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, for this can cause them to choke, do not push the bone inwards; and move quickly that the patient may hold the instrument, for if it slips or the thing is loose, since it has slipped down, or if it is forced too far, it will be equally broken.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Medicine is never without its danger, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines.</start_of_turn
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And when it does not help, look in the throat of the patient at the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I told you.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the limb without its bone, if the fracture has penetrated all the way through, or if there are subtle cracks that are worth as much.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	If these are not the case, take a saw and place it in the throat of the patient; then cut either upwards or downwards with the saw as much as is necessary.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	If the patient groans with acute pain throughout
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take full notice that I see a cold sweat, and wet the mouth, and vomiting in the direction of swallowing, and the hand moves often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if the tongue swells with the heat, it swells up.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not swell as we have said, if you suffocate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, for it will have a sense of purpose.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot or there are charcoal pieces, and that the position be covered with a veil, and that which is pierced is the head of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then I order you to perform fumigation and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes out only through the nostrils.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the nostrils will now swell, and if they do not bleed, repeat the fumigation many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and if the patient feels thirsty, and swallows dirty and foul things, and does not drink water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	then you must know that it is necessary for her to vomit because of this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which we treat the bleeding is, if we can see it, like tenailles hooked in the throat to enter the gorge;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And it has the semblance of a vulture's beak, and it has the roughness of lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go.
et vez ci la forme:	And thus it appears:
li chapistres des apostemes	the physicians of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	The shape of these wounds is such as those of an abscess, as it is mentioned in this book many times, and they differ in perforation and size
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are two ways in which this occurs: one is like its own shape, and the other is due to moisture
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method if for the limbs or if they are stiff.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the swelling of the head is different from that of the root, and the swelling of the limb is different from that which comes at the joints, and the tendons have their judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	If there are abscesses, one must not pierce them until the swelling has subsided according to its degree;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	If there are such cases where it is necessary to pierce them when they are solid, and they do not subside according to their degree, like an abscess which is between joints
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	for when swelling comes from the joints, and it is left until it is relaxed, by chance if the bone and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, because of this there is contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or the incision is at the root of the principal limb; and if you delay the perforation until it is middling, it will reach the principal limb.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	Or it is at the root of the foundation, if the perforation is not done immediately when it is middling.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And I must only tell you that you must pierce the abscess in a straight line with digestion accompanying, except for the one at the root of the foundation, which must not be perforated, and be along, and there will be fistula
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot be cured in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you must know that you must wash the wound of the abscess which is dead according to the completion, when the pain is calmed, and the departure of fever, and the cessation of pain and redness, and doubt and the swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And you must know that you must make the perforation or more dependent on the abscess, and where it bursts out muscle.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	Or if the perforation is long in the bone, and if the abscess is grasped by hand or piece, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all these cases it is equal or there is no fat.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the location of the limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the wound is in flesh, if it is deep enough that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in digestion, as we have said
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce before this, if it comes out along the bone, and there is plenty of pus;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	And by chance it strengthens the bones and deepens it from him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no abscess that is perceived at the large end of the wound, according to what the limb has to bear.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must know that you must bring in small abscesses, small perforations;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and many wounds according to the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	And if there are such abscesses, or if it is necessary to shave close the hair near, cover.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When it is so swollen as a drape, and is softened, if necessary, one can do the same as with boils:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	And if there are such as are split into three angles, and such as require being grasped just like the berries of thyme, or like abscesses of carbuncles.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And if there are such that require making a round cut of a certain size, and others of various sizes and similar to cutting off
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	When there is no head, if it is a superficial wound, it is necessary to pierce straight through
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And when the abscess is large and there is a great swelling, and you pierce through, if you do not pull out all the swelling at that moment, but only a part
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then I press the abscess right up to the other jaw, and then do nothing more.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this repeatedly with great force, until the swelling is completely gone
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Indeed, if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman in childbirth, or a young child, or an old man decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Hence avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived the abscess, if the wound is small, look to see if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is of full size, if you attempt to pull out hair or old cotton
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there is much pus, you must know that you must bite together two attempts so that they meet each other
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have cauterized in the abscess a part of raw skin, and you have closed it round, then you must know that you must fill it with much cotton or lint of hemp in the direction of moisture, and keep it firm until the third part is over.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood should discharge from your work, if you order cold water and ease, and moisten the drape, and withdraw the draining limb many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the wound persists, if there is danger of infection and cure, and the powders that I have said are in the hands of the lord in this book, and if it is spring or summer, and the hands or the abscesses are covered with moisture, if you must put on bandages and wet cloths with vinegar and oil
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in this state, and the hand is fleshy, if you must put on wet cloths with water and oil, or with vinegar and oil, until the third part is over, as we have said
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then take away the abscess, wipe away the pus, and treat the wound, if it is possible, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	This action is useful for all kinds of abscesses.
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Or as you have said, before treating the abscess, one must prepare the patient properly.</start_of_turn>
des soros	And this thing is known throughout in the treatment of abscesses: or as I have said previously, before treating abscesses, you must be wary of the chapter.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or if the chief comes down with small abscesses, and they are like those which are in silk, as is the case with a goose, and there is in it something which resembles it.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some greasy or wet patients with moisture as with boils.</start_of_turn
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And if there are some that are hard and painful at the bone, and no doubt that the artery does not oppose it.</start_of_turn
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And as for the work of this size, if you expect with all the instruments which are called "instruments of introversion", from which the shape comes afterwards, what thing does it contain?
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, if it flows down long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	When the moisture is evacuated, if you leave the skin that contains that moisture, it returns to its place.</start_of_turn
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then plunge the cotton swab into the Egyptian ointment, if it is present.

et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And this will counteract what remains dormant at night

puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of ointment according to what is appropriate, until it is healed
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess persists without fat, if you cut it according to this form, for a long time
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	And evacuate your sponges, and the pus from all parts, and put all your care to drain for the coat or where it lies
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the artery opposes you, do as I have said afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	In the same way, do an incision if it is purulent, and cut and cure as I have said before
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the size of the purulent incision and the moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little consequence
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if there are any of these abscesses or heads [of wounds] or there is no moisture, and if these are the abscesses that I cauterize or heads of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	then find the abscess just like a stone, rough and pale, and cannot burst.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if it does not bleed, we must make an incision as with a stone.</start_of_turn>
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses that bleed or head, for these that come from the bowels and from the roots of the ears, it opens even on the most dependent day, for fear of bursting the belly.</start_of_turn
et les cure si com il covient.	And the treatment is as it is commanded.
des scrophules	And the size of the perforated abscess and the moisture, if they are lighter, because they are of little blood. And if some of these abscesses or heads or there is no moisture, and these are the ones I cauterize or head of an old woman; and I find the abscess as a solid stone, rough and white, and cannot break it; and if there is no blood in it, we must make just as good a wound as if it were a stone. In other abscesses coming or heads, forasmuch as these which come from the spleen and from the roots of the ears, it overtures if it is always dependent on the liquid, because of the swelling; and we must cure it as it should be.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess arises at the collarbone, and the armpits, and in the groin, and never comes from anywhere else or bone, and is bloody, and is joined to each other.</start_of_turn
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And every swelling is properly placed in its sheath, as we have said before;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And the signs of these swellings are many.</start_of_turn>
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some diseases that contain moisture, and if they have malignants that do not obey reason, they will not yield to treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	When you see a good colour in the touch, and that it is like the colour of bone, and soft from one side and not hollow as in the neck nor in the artery nor in the vein, nor deep.</start_of_turn
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	If you can grasp it by the root and the soft part, and if the two levers of the shoulder are as we have said in the apostemes of the head.</start_of_turn
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And so be it that you keep your hands away from the nerve and the vein, and do not touch or handle anything that may cause spasm or bleeding, only grasp firmly and do not speak too soon, lest you cause more harm than good.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you grasp the vein or the artery, and this does not allow you to work, if you put in the wound a bit of vitriol broth or any powder that remains bloodless, and strain the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And leave it until the swelling has subsided and the wound is softened, and then begin to move around.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	When the thing is washed clean, if you return to your work, until you have finished it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then your duty will be shown if there remain no small scabs, if you grasp and touch them
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large swelling at the root of the scrophula vein, I do not advise you to grasp only the swelling at its root; but rather to bind it with a strong double thread and leave it hanging freely, as needed.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the dressing of many layers of cotton, oiled in Egyptian fashion, and then treat the wound
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you have completely cauterized the boil, know that you must now join the two layers of the wound and suture them; and that there will be no remaining excess due to the size of the boil.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you understand to grasp the root of the thing and to pull out the pus, and to suture as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	The scrofula that persists in excess, pierce it or I fear it will die.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	And pierce it like the one before mentioned, depending on the situation, and mix it with oil and similar things, so that it may remove what remains of the corruption
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wound is well closed, if the oily dressing adheres firmly, as long as it is healthy.
de squinance	When the wound is well drained, cure it with ointment which will cause the wound to contract as long as it is healthy.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancient men spoke and told of the measurement of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen it in our land, and it is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	As for those who have a squint, it is necessary that the epiglottis, which is called the epiglottis, be turned away.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and this does no good, for all the veins and the blood of the patient are at those which are above the mouth, in the throat or in the two mandibles
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the chest of the abdomen, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from strangulation.</start_of_turn>
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we want to split the epiglottis, to split it from three circles or four, a small cut between the two circles or by the quantity of the split of the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And if the larynx is closed to the epiglottis, there is no meat there, and the blood vessels are long and thin.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, then you must stretch the skin of the throat to its furthest extent, and then cut the hair as far as the chin;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And hide the blood vessels, if you see nothing else, and then close the wound as we have said before.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	It is shown by the cutting of the windpipe that the cough will erupt from the broken bone, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	When the hour has passed and the strangulation is not seen, gather the two layers of the wound of the chin, and bind them all around the cartilage
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that cause the growth of hair, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim does not make this just until the throat is completely closed, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the default is that it has failed.</start_of_turn>
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore keep the epiglottis closed for this reason that the patient does not vomit, and he breathes through the wound; and thus death is averted.</start_of_turn>
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And for this reason the ancients command that the wound remain open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it is passed in three days or four. And when it is healed, they command that the wound be sutured and healed, until it is healed.</start_of_turn
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I tell you this, that I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I have seen that a lady took a knife and put it in her throat, and grasped parts of the windpipe that were hanging loose.</start_of_turn
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I fled called for the cure, and found her as dead.
