I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had escaped from it, and saw that it did not penetrate any vein or artery except for the throat, and that the blood came out through the wound itself.</start_of_turn
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and saw the wound, and cured it until it healed completely.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	There was no further complaint from her, except that her voice was hoarse, and she returned to her usual state
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis I did not feel fear
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	These abscesses are called "neck hernia," and are large abscesses the color of jaundice, and are very common in women
et est selonc II manieres:	And there are two methods for treating them:
naturez, et accidens;	Natural treatment and surgical treatment
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Or natural treatment has no effect.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the cause of the accident is two ways, for one is like grease to us, and the other way is like an abscess which comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is doubt, and one cannot do more work than in this small thing, and the evidence and the search is in everything that is inside:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it just like I do not know of grease, and cannot do anything to it, if it swells, as we swell the thumb, and take away from all around it, if there is no point;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and cover everything thoroughly, and treat it as if it could be saved, until it is perfectly healed
des nous	And encircle all around, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many things of this kind are with us, of which I will speak of all the similarities.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And thus it is proven that I shall tell you all the difference that exists between a nut and an issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that dislocation is a heat and fever that persists as long as the inflammation has not passed, and is accompanied by swelling;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Therefore rest the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Without a nut there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, but it contains the sap, which is its own bag and is like the color of blood, and begins like an abscess and becomes large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And are like wax, grease, or moisture, and moist of the color I have said in the division
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the knot, that you first examine and inquire about the instrument which is called the “entromissoire,” according to its form or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiry of abscesses of the head is that you take more moisture from the head than you find in the abscess, and twist your thumbs and fingers back and forth until you believe that the instruments have felt the pain, then that it is in proportion to the greatness of the abscess
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the entraumeater, and take care that the leap bound over it does not spring forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	When moisture covers the skin, making it slick, if it is like this with other incisions;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the removal of the entraumeater no moisture comes, greasy discharge, if it is like this with other incisions, grasp the surrounding area with tweezers and pinch slightly towards the bone, and keep the dressing in place with your hand or with a bandage.</start_of_turn>
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you do not handle it carefully, if you tear it piecemeal so that nothing remains.</start_of_turn>
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if nothing remains, it will return to us many times.</start_of_turn
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it lingers a little while, and without pain, if you employ a wound of some corrosive powders, hold the wound steady, and apply calming things above the wound, and it will heal of itself; and do other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it swells greatly, if cost two pounds of the wound, and treat it of that which engulfs flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	If the vein swells up against you or something similar forces you, and if you hurry and use the broth of vitriol ground fine, and leave it for two or three days, until the wound bursts, and rest the swelling of blood
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cover what is remaining that has lingered from now on.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the entrapped bones, and there are three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	Great, medium, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	There are three quarters which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three ways of doing it.
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Great, medium, and small, for to encompass the fistulas of the abscesses.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And are like nails which we sew up the wounds, and are of saffron, or iron, or silver, and must be thick enough to encompass the cortices of the fistulas
et sont de III manieres:	And there are three ways of doing it
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the perforation.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the needles are like those of wheat grains, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	Great, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	...and if there are those who have two curves of three ways also.
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	...and if there are those who have three curves, and are also of three ways
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	...and if there are those who have two curves, and one curve only, and are of three ways
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	...and all these things are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these shoulders feels is tense, and there are some that cut only from one side, from which we extract the nails, because of this we do not close the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	...and from these inward movements are the bones repositioned in sleeves, so that the patient does not lose them when opening the abscesses;

puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then repeat the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering from this, and take out a small amount of pain;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do not do this again, and take care not to do this until there remains only a little pain.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt the patient, and you put too much pain, if the surgeon of the burial or sand burn, and by putting out sweat or bath and sun, and drink plenty of liquid.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And the treatment of dry medicines until they are healed, and cauterize upon the stomach and upon the liver and upon the spleen after the extraction of the urine, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stomach of the thigh.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Never are children born without a mark on their belly, or the mark is small, or it is not properly in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If the coving [cautery] is too great, that it causes no perception at all in all the surrounding parts following this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	Then put or pierce I clo of ointment, and bind and hold it for III days or IV, and when he wants to urinate, if he keeps it closed, make him urinate, and then put it back
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance it cannot be, for the urine that comes out will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, if it is treated with oil of lead, as we have said, if it dilates.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the opening in their limb are blind, for none are born with the opening at the head of the penis, for they cannot urinate before they lift up their penis
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and cannot urinate because of that, for the matter cannot come down to the marrow, and that is a bad illness
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And thus the work proceeds if the patient lies somewhat bowed down on his back, so that the head of the arm and the elbow are as wide as a thumb, if indeed he has pierced through flesh in the middle, as he should.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus you must keep from bloodshed which often comes, and if it comes, if the stain of that which stains blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des pustules de la verge	Des pustules de la verge.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times this white spot appears in the arm, and is an omen of great suffering.</start_of_turn
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are malignant and non-malignant.</start_of_turn
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	if it is possible that you take hold of it and cut it superficially, and break all the bones and teeth, then put on Egyptian linen cloth.</start_of_turn
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment of ointment is applied until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the bath is bad, of dark colour and putrid, if you must bring cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have grasped it, and if the swelling is in the hip, and there is some in the belly and some outside, then you must stretch the swelling that is inside first

Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat it whole, if you do not keep the shoulder firmly in place, it will blacken and corrupt the limb and the bone.

Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery is of two sorts:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	It is to say, at the discharge of blood, and the corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	When the head of the arm is corrupted and retracted, if it is suspected that you have swallowed or passed a clot from the vein, and the patient urinates among them;

et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	If this matter is neglected, if it is suspected that the fracture of the bone is not displaced, that you must grasp the arm without moving its head or shoulder.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then sprinkle somewhat between two, and I put one subtle bandage of wet linen on the cold water, which does not move from its place.
de la circoncision	with circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not simply a continuation of other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	However, when we make this work of our will, and properly apply it, if it is necessary that we make it better, and the lighter for the health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision in their laws, because they did not use it in their customs, and we have only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and doctors who make circumcision endure for a long time, with force, and with all their skill;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	If they flee from fear because of two tiles, and by chance they break this one and leave the other one behind
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Or it is recovered covered, and the pain is doubled, and there is confusion that is not sure whether the point of the limb is fixed;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	And at the loosening of the ligament by chance escapes the iron, and corrects the work, and many times they are born anew that they do not need to be loosened again, and I desire it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Or the wound covers again, and the pain is doubled, and at the movement which is done with too much force at the point of the limb; and at the movement of the tendon by chance escapes the iron, and repairs the work, and many times the nails are born again without having to make another incision, and I want that.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if it is equally taut throughout,
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread is well stretched around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and that the manner of the first work makes you think of the child, if he understands, that you do not force him to bind the thread around the limb too tightly, but that you make him do it loosely in various ways as you wish
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then you make him grasp between your hands straight, and bring the forces between your hands or withdraw your pieces that the child does not see them, neither any of the instruments;
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then take your hand to the shoulder and breathe or groan, and pull it up as high as the head of the shoulder is bent;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then thoroughly cleanse the wound of the filth that is gathered there, then tie the limb with a double thread, and tie it firmly so that it does not slip away again.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	And hold it as two fists by the second loop to the pouch and the thumb, and pass between the two loops, then hold the thumb downwards tightly and pull the head of the shoulder forward
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	Then let the blood flow back slowly and steadily, because that is the medicine.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put powder on and over the powder I drape a cloth glued with an egg yolk smeared with rose oil and fresh, and leave it until the other side is healed, and cure it with other ointments until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The forces of form are multiplied when this is the case:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	when both shoulders are tense and firm, and the arms are as strong as the hands equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	the force of the world is great when the tendons are torn during an incision.
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	therefore you must extend your nails, even though it makes the wound burst open
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and keep it even, and if you do not wish to hold it with your nails, grasp it firmly, and then pull it out
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	and if it persists for three days, and what is below the edge is inflamed, if you leave it as long as the swelling subsides, and gently scorch it

cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it as we have said, until it is healed
dou retenement de l’urine	Dou retenement de l’urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	It holds back urine if there is an obstruction of a stone, or blood clot, or tumour, or worms, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that the obstruction is in the stone which is in the belly or the neck of the bladder, if you must, you must bend the patient over his knees

et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	Then constrain the collar of the bladder towards the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released easily
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	If it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instruments which are called a «syringe», for this is the form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	Or of fine silver wire, as thick as a sparrow’s quill;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And let the cauterization be of a long and a half palm, and of a finer sort at the head
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And thus the method of extracting urine is as follows: if you take two needles and bind one to the head of a wool or cotton swab, and pass the needle through the bladder.
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and keep the surplus of wool and pass the juice until it reaches the head of the syringe, then join the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a chair, and gently raise the bladder and the oily parts moist with oil and water
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	and put the syringe into the bladder until it reaches the root of the bladder, and double the bladder under the pubic bone
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	and pull the syringe out before it reaches the bladder, and the patient will feel the urine come out until it is empty, and this must not be done except in this order because it may cause damage;
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then the thread is at its greatest length, and the urine follows the thread, then the bladder is emptied, and the urine is corrected.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	The catheter is resumed until the bladder is empty, and the patient is aligned.</start_of_turn>
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are flank stones or blood in the bladder, or if there is swelling, and you see urine and medicines being distilled, if you have at your disposal the instrument called the «clepsedre», which is shaped like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if there are three holes:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two from one side, and one from the other, as you see.</start_of_turn>
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the head of the shoulder is held so that the medicine can be applied as well as possible to the bone, if we can remove the moisture, and push as much as necessary.</start_of_turn
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	And when you see the medicines dripping from the bladder, put the head of the physician over the moisture, and push the one who is behind.</start_of_turn
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you grasp moisture at the shoulder, and then quickly push back the hand that grasps it;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	If then moisture enters the hand, and comes to the belly now, if the patient feels it;

et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And do as if you had made a bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	Of the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said above the methods of cutting and the extraction of arrows, together with medicines.
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	And I have said the difference between a stone embedded as rain and all the signs, and in what case a stone must be opened of size.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	And in the bladder, and in the kidney;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	And I shall tell you openly and briefly
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder is often like rain, and this is a sign that the stone has burst from the bladder as if from its subtlety
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and opens the kidney, and grinds the patient's flank, and it can happen many times, and then it hardens;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	And from these bursts the foundation is loosened;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and is light the healing of the bursts until they are three years old, and is great grief in the elderly, and is like a young man between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	And it is the lighter cure of those who have the large stone, than of those who have the small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, first purify the patient by vomiting, to drive out all the bile that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hinders to inquire about the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the limbs, and loosen and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not rise up again high;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then make him sit between your hands, and his hands rest on his thighs, so that the bladder is completely emptied downwards
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then press and touch inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the stone in the space, then quickly pull up on the stone immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not come out with the touch, then take your left index finger, if the patient is old, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and robust;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	And the stone at its foundation, and ask the bone, and when you feel it at your elbow, if the marrow is at the neck of the bladder.
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press on your elbow, and the stone will be forced out or you will see your tailbone
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the ribs above, and with his left hand grasp the skin that is below the ribs in the part where we make the incision;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then pull out the clot covering, for that is the shape
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And enter between that which is between the ribs and the foundation, do not go inside but along the edge of the left armpit;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And either hold two fingers upon the stone, and the two must either stay or rest, and the size of the hole must be as great as the breadth of the stone, but not too large; according to the quantity of the stone, do not make it too wide.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	By chance the press if two must stay or rest, that it leap forth in the direction of work.
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and the nails that are on the edge of the stone or that are angled, and margins
si est griés a issir;	if they are gripped to split.
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is something soft that looks like a gland, round, from which there is a slight oozing
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Then make the hole larger where there are angles and margins
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	If it does not jump, know that you must draw above the nails which are as sharp as a file at the root, for the tooth must be drawn out if it escapes.
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you must hold the instrument curved at the root firmly.</start_of_turn>
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you do not hold it firmly, if it is too large, the vessel will burst, and if the vein is split open.</start_of_turn
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more than one tooth, first draw out the largest at the root of the vessel, then draw out the others in order.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If it is large, if it must be soothed, and make greater pain.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or he dies, or the urine comes together due to the heat that the leaves cannot withstand.</start_of_turn
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	But all the while you must exert yourself greatly to tear, or to remove, the teeth, until you have torn them out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	And when you have finished your work, if you apply the salve of incense, aloe, and dragon’s blood, and hold it tight, and put above it a wet cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the burn.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then restore the patient to his collar, and do not loosen the ligature until the third joint below
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have loosened it, if there arises much blood from the wound of oil and water, then treat with oily dynafinicon and oily basilicon, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if boils come to the wound and carbuncles, and swelling of blood in the bladder, or because of retention of urine, which is known in part as being like urine without its discharge:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Boutes donc ton Doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sang, car s’il y reste, si corront la vessie, et la porrit.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound of acute and easy and gentle aid, and support it in every way you know, until it is healed;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and that you cover that all the hours that you treat it, that you bind the two edges together, and assemble the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the wound is small, and it is an opening of the gut, and is plugged with silk, and the urine cannot pass;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if you are treating this as I have said above, that you must listen to me many times, for this cure is heard of in this size
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already heard of this in other cases
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form and make two angles fixed in one vessel:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take I thread and loop it around the root of the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder.
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then tighten the thread lightly in the root until it comes to the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the thread around the stone back and forth, until you can pierce the stone from the other side
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	When the urine comes, then press your hand on that which is remaining of the stone that is in the root.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is broken, and spurts with the urine, and is seen by the patient;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you are unable to do this for any reason, then take I thread from the root of the stone and I other from above, and push the root towards the stone between the two lines, and then pull it out forcefully, and release the thread, and congeal the blood in the wound
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep it steady until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	If you do not wish to do this by any means, take hold of the limb above the joint and support the limb below, then push the limb forward between the two tendons, and pull it out forcefully, remove the tendon, and congeal the blood that is in the wound; and cure as long as it is necessary.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that in such cases the woman is a virgin.
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is truly learned, even though she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	and the third is that one cannot find a woman who is truly learned in this work of hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth is that if the woman’s hand is more plump than the man’s, because it can therefore hold a deeper size, and great pain is at this point. And if you need some skill in this, if you take a mistress who is truly learned, and prick her with the needle, and if you do not find her to be chaste, there is no woman in the world who is as subtle as she.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And she presents a cunning dance in the life of women, or a woman who cuts off a part of her body, and she commands her to do what you command her with the inquiry of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look well if the woman is a virgin.
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then she must push her shoulder forward or downwards and inquire about the stone.
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, if she confines her shoulder socket, she recommends that she push her shoulder forward or with the patient, and she orders her to press her left hand on the bladder area
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	if she finds it, she must move it from its entrance on the bladder until it reaches the root of the thigh
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	Then put your hand on the thigh at the root of the knee and find the middle of the bone, where it is usually visible, and feel the bone in that part.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	Do not move the forearm under the bone or beside it, and let the size be small at first.</start_of_turn>
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	Then tighten the limb steadily, if you feel the bone growing in the wound as much as the bone can bear, and soak up the blood that has flowed many times before.</start_of_turn
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	This is to say, small and large, acute and blunt, long and round, and which have rained.</start_of_turn>
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if her discharge resembles stones, it is an issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if it does not go away, if put at the limb vitriol broth, and hold it for an hour until it is stained.</start_of_turn
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	Then return to your work, as long as the stone is firm, and have the instruments that I have told you about in the extraction of the stone, for they are useful to you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	If it does not go well, and it is the artery that is cut, put powder on the wound and hold tight with clamps and bandages, and do not attempt to move it again, but leave the stone alone and do not touch it, except in the event of an accident that causes the patient to die
puis cure la plaie.	Then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the bleeding has ceased and the limb is at rest, if you return to this work while the wound is still fresh, as long as the bone is firm.</start_of_turn>
de hernie carnouse	Of hernias of the intestines.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Warm water is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is like lukewarm urine from cows, that contains eggs.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	It is called "syfac," and never is it properly in the urine of a cow, if we take care that it is not something else
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	And this is the skin between the white surface that we mentioned before.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	And it does not swell further.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this membrane is from weakness that comes from the cheese, and it is spread throughout that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never if it comes from percussion on the bones, and this moisture is of many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it is pale yellow, or it is without red, or black, or pale blue, and this is more
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are signs of congestion in this assembly, because if it is like the white surface that we mentioned before, if the abscess is reddish, I do not see the bones, because there is moisture everywhere
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is reddish with a part of the yolk, and because of this it is believed that it is another bone;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	And if moisture is between the skin of the armpits and the white membrane, if he feels well;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	Then when you know the colour of the moisture, if it spreads throughout the entire inwardness where it appears, from that it is known that its form is as it is before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, which comes after the introductor, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we bind the limb with iron, if it is known that the patient is well according to the poor and the filling of his body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then we support him on his back, on something somewhat high, and put on him a little bandage
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and stretch the limb to the second rib below the armpits;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the sponge of lead, and grasp the skin of the armpits among the long hair as far as the ridge of the scapula, and make a complete incision straight across the armpits down to the white membrane, and burn it superficially as much as the poor allows
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the skin deeply with a large hole, drain all the liquid, and then place your thumbs on, extend the skin upwards.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	Do not touch the root of the bones, but only the skin should be grasped gently
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Cope either all at once or in pieces by itself the cost of it secretly, for if you do not cope it well, the liquid will return
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	If the limb leaps up to your work, keep it in its place until you have completed the work of the incision
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then assemble the two limbs of the bones at a joint, and then suture if like the other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the limb corrupted by another illness, then you must tie up the vessels that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then grasp the shoulder firmly with all the suspenders, and draw out the limb, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if it is assembled into two parts together, its roots are two branches.
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	if you have grasped the other part in the same way as the first, then press out the blood, and put lint in the wound soaked in rose oil
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another layer of gauze soaked in wine and oil on top, and put on the two shoulders, and put on under doubled cloths, and bind it up in the way that is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths and use coarse wool according to this shape and join them together at the armpits, and one hand grasps at the bottom just up to the back, and the other at the part of the armpit
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	And the other two heads above the two armpits, and so be altogether assembled the restriction in the loop of the braid.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never is this twig of cautery as large as iron, and take I cautery of the pointed kind, and burn the hair of the flanks, and so eschew if we have said, so that the white fat that contains the liquid is discovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery thus, and pierce that fat as we have said, and burn with this pointed cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And so burn in all ways that you will, until you have scraped all of it away.
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	And keep that the flame does not touch the egg;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and the wounds that this work is more helpful.
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and bloodletting for the removal of swellings, and medicines that mitigate the severity of the diseases;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if anything hinders you, or incisions of boils or discharges of blood or anything else, if you can, cure that which hinders you, as it is said above
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	and if the patient is pale and does not wish to stay with this work because of its horror, if you must perform an incision, as I have said, and when you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that the swelling has gone down, if you wish, you may seat the patient on a low chair
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then make the incision at the lower part of the limb with all the surrounding tissue, and put the perforation through to the bone's length
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	Or let the wound be large, so that all the pain will cease for certain.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and leave until the remaining pain ceases; then cure until the wound is healed completely.</start_of_turn>
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	If the white cloth does not hold back the pain at the edge of the wound, then you must drink a penny or the instrument with which the wound is treated for dropsy.</start_of_turn

And make the wound large, and soak it in water so that the pain returns, and bandage it together after six months or when the pain has passed, and when it is bandaged as before, the patient will recover his days.</start_of_turn
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the buttocks.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Soaking as in the section of this twig has many precautions, for I believe it is better to leave it alone.</start_of_turn
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I shall tell you of the work and the semblance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say therefore that the main cause of an abscess comes from suppuration or boils, and even cysts;
et c’est par mout de cas.	And it is through experience.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is to say by excessive rubbing and swelling, which is caused by boils or percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and it has the color of an abscess according to the color of boils;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and does not cause pain, but is a true abscess
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and sometimes it is a bloody abscess, purulent and painful, with a foul color, and never comes from a vein or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When there is no pulse from an artery, if it is known by the position of the cautery, when you press on it at your side;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you must not touch it there.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	The one that is made of swelling of a vein is known by its position at the expression of touching the sides, and can well do the size above this semblance, and above the others
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and that you hold it like nails, then the head will be high, and the thread for white silk, and deliver the suspension from all parts of the head.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the head of the limb is already swollen with these nails, if you can, then only treat the limb and hold it
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is near the surface of the skin, or in what is inside the blood vessels, you must deliver all the surrounding tissue, and the cavity must be rounded off.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the limb hangs loose from the socket or from behind, then you must grasp all that is taut, and pull out the root, as we have said.</start_of_turn>

When your work is finished, if you have used up the soft wool dressing in oil and rose wine, then cure it with other ointments until it is healed.</start_of_turn
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the buttocks.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess enclosed by a covering resembling two boards, with the softening of the bones, and the patient groans when he walks.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	The treatment for this disease is as dangerous as the disease itself, as we have often seen in the past.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	You must make the patient sit on a low seat, then support the bones below his shoulders to the armpits, all the veins that are around the edge, and hold them firmly, and stretch them out
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then grasp the spur of the tooth that is piercing wide through the blood vessels, until it is uncovered, and then pull it out from the root, as we said in the extraction of arteries in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then insert a needle or if there is double thread, and bind it to the first limb or the nail has gone, and bind it loosely at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then hold them (the teeth) in the middle upright, according to the length of the root, and remove the corrupted moisture
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then treat the wound as others or bathe, so that no blood vessel is cut except those that nourish one of the bones
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because by this there is no harm, and if all the blood vessels come loose, as it should be, if you can carry the bones over all the blood vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	If the oesophagus does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the veins, and if it is dried and does not swell, it will not need aid.
de la routure dou syfac	If the vessel does not lose its nourishment by the incision of the veins, and if it dries and does not yield assistance.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The outcome of this root is if it is by the section that comes or if it is extended on the belly in the part of the flanks, because the intestine descends from that passage to one of the buttocks.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	And this passage is either by section or by extension of the intestines, and these two methods arise from two causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or by percussion, or by jumping, or by pressure, or from the lifting of a burden, and by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is by section of the syfac are that there is both pain and swelling in length, and it does not come immediately
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the abscesses are equal in size until towards the belly, because the spleen presses the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the socket is inflamed, that it makes an immediate sharp pain, and the swelling is diverse, sometimes the skin is pale, and this is because of the escape of the intestine and the stiffness of the socket.</start_of_turn
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never is the bone moved with the intestine, and is retained when it is pressed, and makes great pain for the patient, even when it is pressed.</start_of_turn
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with fire and fear, for it is known that they must be cautious.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the way of this work is that if you command or patient that he bend the intestine to his hand in the wound, if it can return there again.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	Then hold his collar between your hands, and keep his legs still;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then stretch the limb upwards, and clench all the skin of the buttocks long
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then hold the bowels open to the size of a thumb according to what you must see to open the wound, and be like that which causes it not to move
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then uncover the spleen that is under the skin of the buttocks, until the white spleen is discovered throughout
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	Then take your thumb and index finger and place them on that which teaches you the position, between the white splint which is above the leather of the egg, and between the second splint, and withdraw that which is behind the egg, and between the second splint.
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And thus move the right hand from the knuckles of the fingers, and extend the white splint above your left hand, and hold the egg against all the splinting towards the belly;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	Command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and loosen that which is behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And look if there is any intestine or white splint hard involved, and if you find nothing, if the egg is soft against the belly;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	Then take a needle or if there is thick thread made of X threads, and pass it through the back part of the scapula, which is behind the skin of the armpits.
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	Then the size, then tie the head of the dislocation which appears from the threads, until there are three threads remaining.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	Then assemble the bones one over the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the scapula, as we have said which is behind the skin of the armpits, with a strong thread of two parts

et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	And put the thread straight according to the first thread which is two finger-widths long, and after these two fingers leave the scapula which is behind the skin of the armpits the greater part of a palm
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	And afterwards, according to the roundness of the egg, which is carried.
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	Then grasp in the part which is under the skin of the joints, as much as it hangs loose, and bow it, as we have said before
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then mix coarse wool with oil, and put it on the wound, and put in the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the flesh except as we have said, after the incision, in doubt of the discharge of blood.

puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound in another way, until it is completely healed
de hernie carnouse	Of hernias of the intestines.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this chapter, I have never seen anyone cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones say that it is made as the twig which is bound to the nut, in part as you bind the blood vessels, after the size above lightly on the outside.

Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Never comes rupture in anger, as we have said, and open the wounds
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not break any intestines as bones, and if there are any, that is bad, and repair them at all hours.

et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press upon the belly, then cut the two thighs appearing from the hip bone on the top of the right thigh, and cut both of them.

Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is confined, and has no apparent cause in the course of treatment, and the cautery is useless in this situation, and more proximate to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the nails
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times is the skin of the joints softened in baths of hot water, because the bones that are within are softened, and it is evident to see
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	And it is necessary, when one sees it cured, to make the patient sit up on his back, and to support the softened skin on the natural skin

dou chastrement	Dou chastrement.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	The wounds which are scraped in our laws, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of them in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and are only necessary for two methods:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one is that the patient looks at the wound when asked and that the cure is applied to the wound itself
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other is that often we have seen patients scratched by animals such as dogs and goats, cats and other animals
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say therefore that the cautery is performed in two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	or by traction, or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In that which we do it by traction, we must keep the part to be treated in hot water, until the skin is softened and limp.
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then grasp it with your hand, until it is firm and you can no longer feel it
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the size of the cautery:

des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphrodism is in two ways as at home:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one if between the two genitals appears as the nature of a woman, or there are hair, and sometimes in court it urinates.</start_of_turn

de la tentigene	Hermofrodie is according to two ways: one if between the two testicles opens as with the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in between they urinate. And the other way if in women, and has on the navel as a boy and two testicles. And the cure for the womb and fame if it is that you copulate the testicles all, and cure as other wounds; in the second way, men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tentigene est une chars ajostee sur la partie naturelle, tant qu’elle est trop lourde pour voir;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a weight hanging from the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have had as much as an arm, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary to hold the surplus of the weight at your hand or on the nails, and to support it lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	do not go too close to the wound, for blood will come out, and that is worse than the disease itself; then the cure of other cures when it is healed
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and another weight that comes from the mouth of the marrow, and the spleen, and by chance a jump upwards, and it is like a cow's jaw, and for this reason it is called the old "coward disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you perceive that it has slipped, as we have said, hold the limb steady until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Erratic if it is when the nature of the woman is not clearly known, or the opening is too small.
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	for it is natural by birth, or by accident from illness that it comes about;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is caused by a tight band, or a soft swelling or spasm, and is done by pressure in the marrow, or the ribs, or the bowels, or otherwise

des emorroides	des emorroides.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Emorrhages are bursting of veins which, without treatment, are almost always fatal; and when old, become thick and clotted.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	And as we have mentioned in the preceding sections the signs and symptoms, I will now speak of those which signify a cure.</start_of_turn>
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that in old emboli, when they are softened in the marrow, and cannot be felt, if they are not treated by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the root of the marrow can be felt, and these can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then keep the abscess closed with pins, and press on its roots, then sprinkle on restraining medicines like acaice and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things.</start_of_turn
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	Then bind her parts until an hour has passed, then immerse her in cold water.</start_of_turn
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	If blood flows away, if the patient sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel, of barley and other things, then take barley flour, and mix with honey and oil, and apply it on his back.
