des apostemes de la marris	Emorroids are tears in veins which without support are not usually seen; and when old become tough. And we have said concerning the marks and signs, I will say here those which are useful for cure. I say that emorroids and tough veins, when they are pressed in the marrow, and they are not felt, if not except by the cure by iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then extend the heel and press on its root, then sprinkle on medicines that restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then withdraw its pieces an hour later, and put it in cold water; and if there is blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix with honey and assails, and make one application on her back. And if it stops, that is good. If not, if there is an opening at the back, and there are clots that look like wounds; then take lint, and soak it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make an opening at the root. And when the wound is healed, if it is cured of swelling as long as it is healthy; and that which is called “albathir” is red, and is similar to a rough beard, if it is covered as I have said the tough veins; and then it is cured as long as it is healthy.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come into the marsh, such as carbuncles and perforated abscesses and herpes and swellings and fistulas and hemorrhoids and cautery abscesses, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the previous division.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	Therefore, I must say that I die in this treatment the abscess that comes up in the armpit, which is not just an abscess that collects pus;
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	And if you see the work of iron, if you see that the abscess is already coming to an end at its beginning, full of heat and fever, and if it turns red when you see it.</start_of_turn>
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Therefore do not hasten to pierce [the abscess], but make me wait until the pain is eased.</start_of_turn
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	Then make the patient sit on a chair, and give him two small stools or he will lean forward, and support him on his back and join his limbs so that they are aligned with the limb;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	And let his thighs be spread wide, and place his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a strong thread.
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	Then bend the knee towards his chest costing, and bring the instrument which we hold in our hand to cover the mouth of the mare, for after this comes the form
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	And you must know that when you bring this instrument to cover the mouth of the mare, that you must first test the depth of the wound, so that what enters between the instrument and the wound does not go deeper than it should, and does not harm the patient
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	And if the instrument is large, if you must cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause pain
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	And he must put the horn of the instrument at its base, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	When the abscess bursts open, and we make a hold of the hand below, if he covers the head with the thumb and index finger,
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	When the wound is cleaned out, if he covers the wound with a bandage, you must put in it some soft lint or cotton soaked in rose oil or dry green oil.
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	Put a little pressure on the wound at the bottom of the vein, and put a layer of lint over the vein and over the piece of cloth, and fill with water or mallow which has been boiled;
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then keep it bandaged for two days following this, until it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	And never lift the bruise and wound with a clustery of water and honey, and then with water or radish and chamomile long shall be cooked.
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Then return to the swelling.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the cavity, one must take care not to burn it, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	De l’enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	Master is first at play that he knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down and desire to smell the navel:
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	Then the child is born with force to be delivered

et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	And when you see these signs, if you must press lightly on his belly, so that the child is thrust out;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	For when he falls on his head, if he is accompanied by a second person, and the marrow of his superfluities is broken by violent impact.
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this which comes from elsewhere does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it never comes from its bones, but comes from force of bone or limb, hand or from the belly, or even from the throat, and is turned by chance from his collar and by other harmful postures.
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	if he is aware of the dance that it should be discreet in these matters, and he avoids error and deception, and I will show you all the postures in which one must aid him

et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	if there is a discharge or the belly is tied, if you see it, and if you pull it out or pierce it;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and if there is a hole in the rib or in the side; and in the one there are two holes, and in the other one there is one hole.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and if the belly or the owner puts medicines in a bladder of gut or parchment, or if you pierce all around the holes, and between each hole put one must of space, and then put in these holes one strong thread of strong thread twisted in the shape of the cross or in the shape of an anchor, and reassemble the belly as if it were a needle
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	And when the medicine is dense, if the thread has been placed in front of a strong wire, then clench.
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	It is like the shape of a circle
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine neither too hot nor too cold, and join the head of the clamp with oil or balm of egg, or something similar, and tighten it lightly
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	Then grasp the minister with both hands together, until it is well seen, then withdraw the clamp, and leave the patient’s legs in place, and if the medicine breaks through, if it can be helped;
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if it sleeps all night long, if it is more useful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he sees it in the disease of falling of the belly, and the physician hastens to go out, if he recommences as long as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if swelling appears on the surface or foundation, or abscess, if the clamp is as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And thus is the form of a subtle blister on which the skin is strained:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the previous section the treatment of wounds.
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or you may say the treatments of hands and surgery, according to their accomplishment
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on the way they are made, and depending on the parts of the body from which they are made, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things which are done for wounds are made with the bite of a stone, and the size of a nail or a staple, or of an arrow or a tube or a saw, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or they are made according to the conditions of the flesh, as for example a wound that bites on the chin, or on the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, or similar parts
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I shall tell you the treatment of a chest wound, and I shall begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come back to you in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes or an abscess bursts, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that it is not from a stone wound or similar things, and the skin is entirely ruptured and the wound is large, and you doubt the depth of the wound, do not hesitate to cauterize.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if you do so too soon after the wound, and there is still blood coming from the wound, or if the blood is flowing in the opposite direction to the part that is affected;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and listen to the patient's swelling from wine and meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	and if he does not recover, if he is vomiting his food, and does not drink wine, does not eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and take out the wound, if there is pus coming from it, cover it with soft cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in styptic wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	If there is no clot at the wound’s base, if you put a bandage on the wound when it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, dust, etc., I will tell you about it later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If blood has moved, put on some ointment until it has healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the size of a nail and similar, and the layers do not want to stick together by tension, if you join them together with stitches, as I will say for wounds on the belly, from the stitches.</start_of_turn>
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to bone, and pus, and only holds at a point, if it is grasped,
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hair that has fallen out in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat fatty foods, such as testicles and bread, as well as poultry, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find hair or decay on the bone, if it grasps the bone firmly, extract it forcefully, then cure it.</start_of_turn>
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	If there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without support, and it cannot be held by medicines, if the artery is displaced, if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If that does not help, if you must cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, suffice with a mild treatment:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And put on this powder that will harden as soon as it comes into contact with blood
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	The way of using the powder is as follows
pren encens une partie;	Take an incense and mix it with a part of the powder
sanc de dragon II parties;	With two parts of dragon's blood
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	chalk three parts, and the powder finely, and apply to the wound, and hold firmly until it has healed well and reunited with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	And then bind it well, and leave it loose, if it does not swell.
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not keep the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we make this charcoal burn only, when we have no incense or blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if it has moved the wound, even in this state, if one does not put on this powder immediately.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some astringents or poultices made of barley flour soaked in water and honey, until it stops bleeding
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	and if a bone breaks with the wound, and it is small, if you have grasped the wound carefully
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	I will tell you later about the breaks of the head
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the head.</start_of_turn>
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes with the head and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the neck or the artery is cut.</start_of_turn
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If that is the nerve, if there is nothing else to be done, let the cure alone, and do not put anything restrictive, for it does no good and makes the nerve shrink.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the nerve is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the most sensitive part of the limb
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But if the medicine is soft, like warm water with sweet oil, and mixed with rosemary oil, and vinegar washed in sweet water, and other stones of the earth, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, if the bone and the surrounding tissue are bent, then cure it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and closed and full of pus, if the opening or more downwards lies;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	If the artery is cut, and blood flows out, if swelling, and pus, and cautery must be mixed together is
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the bristles of the beard are cut, or the hair of the head, and the cord is held, by which the meat goes, if the hair on the edge of the beard is cut, do not touch the beard but return it to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then the pain will subside, and leave them for some days, and cure them with liberal applications until they are healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	If the wound has made an indentation in the bone, if the marrow;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, if the marrow is split, you must leave as much as possible of the wound open, and keep it clean and aligned
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, if powder is sprinkled on the wound as I have said
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, if the cure be as I have said in this chapter.</start_of_turn
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of from a wound of lance or knife</start_of_turn
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, if you see that the wound is spitting blood rapidly, the patient cannot remain still.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Then the wound is deadly;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	if it is not deep and is fresh throughout its extent, if you do not immediately put powder on it, do not bind it up with the blood until it has clotted, and renew the application of the powder, and comfort the patient
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but if there is an attractive dressing, and you tie it twice tightly;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	if there is no dressing, put in the wound a great deal of cotton to absorb the moisture, and make the patient rest on the wound for three days, or four, or more
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	If there is no spasm, do not tremble male of body, nor stretching of limbs;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see the bones set, if the wound is saved.</start_of_turn>
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Cure the wounds of sutures and others, as long as they are healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and there is an opening, then leave the wound open that there is fistula.</start_of_turn
si la cure si com on doit.	If the cure is as it should be.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision of sword or knife, and it is simple, or more so on the front or back, if the cure of what is in front.</start_of_turn
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	is great, of stitching.</start_of_turn
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	And if it is small, like dust, and is lodged in the bone, and breaks into pieces, if the wound is deep, and the surrounding tissues are severed if they are loosened.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loosened, if it leaves the wound open, if it aligns the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds, as for other members, the judge will determine as we have said
dou derrompement dou ventre	as other limbs are the judge of such things as we have said.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The breaking of the belly is great and mean and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	There is no greater wound than a wound of the intestine, or no less dangerous than the intestines themselves, because of the introduction of worms.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	And the suture is more painful, and no wound is better than a great one, because in this case we must return the intestines many times to close them;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	Forasmuch the intestines swell greatly that they feel the fruit, if they return to the point, it is worth little to make an incision; for in that case one should retain the intestines in their place rather than make another incision.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And the wounds of the intestine that are in the belly are in three ways:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common incisions are in the belly and the incision of other wounds from bone to bone and two other incisions are common with other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and all of them are more pure with the incision of the belly, and I will say one thing and leave it at that.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small and there is nothing wrong with the intestines, and there is something to be done, this is by one of the two methods
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	Or for the slightness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen by the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, swallow the cold in part slowly:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	wet a sponge or I make a towel wet in cold water only, or thou wilt burn with cold water stinging and pricking and spiking, and raise the intestines until the swelling is bony
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never do thou make this wine restraining, and it is mute that thou art sure to cure by swelling
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	and when thou seest the swelling depart, if moisten the intestine with water or elevate and twist and soften be cooked, for by this is aligned the entrance to everything.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	If it cannot enter, if one makes a hole in the wound with the instrument, we grasp the blood clots.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	The first treatment is to make the wound small, for we must not cut excessively without necessity; it should not be large.</start_of_turn>
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	This is the instrument for cutting.</start_of_turn
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If the cut is too deep in the curve and does not yield, and when this happens, take the form of this.</start_of_turn
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen and the intestines protrude, if you stop bleeding in accordance with the natural form in its own place, you will have done well, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large and is in the lower part of the belly, if you must manage the patient lying on their back, and raise their legs above their head.</start_of_turn
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	And if it is in the lower part of the belly, put the head and the heel higher than the lower parts, and in the same way if the swelling of the belly is in one of the two lower parts, put your hand under what is above so that the upper part is higher than the lower part.</start_of_turn
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And so it is necessary to administer what I have said in large and moist wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	And small wounds do this that you have noticed, then take hold of your hands I administer pity which holds all the way around with its hand, and gather the layers together.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	This is the common method of stitching, and take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the wound's size, then leave a little space at the edge of the wound, and pierce a needle or there put a strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	And pierce the two holes in the leather with the two holes in the sponge, which is to soak the leather through, until you make it pierce from that part, and gather the two heads of the sponge together the three together
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then the strain of a double thread around the needle of two parts, then unite the two ends of the wound immediately, and then leave one space of an inch, and insert another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the knot of the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease until you have made as many knots as you have seen fit for the needles, until the whole wound is secured.</start_of_turn>
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be neither too thick nor too thin, for the thick needles will hold all the hair, and the thin needles will not penetrate well.</start_of_turn
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore it is recommended that they be of moderate size.</start_of_turn>
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	And do not press the needles too far into the hair and skin, for they will hold and tear the wound before the suture is complete.</start_of_turn
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	And then grasp the head of the nails, so that they do not bleed the patient at night; and put a bandage or cloth over the head of the nails to hold them, and leave them until the wound has healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this method of stitching with nails is more convenient for small wounds, because there is a nail or two under the skin.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitching is common, and it is that you join the two nails of leather and the two nails of silk together with a nail or there is one thick middle thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you have pierced these three nails together, if you leave the nail at the start, in the manner in which you began to sew, it will hold the edges together
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	And put space between each stitch the thickness of a candle stub
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	These wounds are seen in the home, and I sewed a wound which had a horn or belly, which was injured by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm of great size, and there were intestines well two palms of great size, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will restore the gut when it has been outside for twenty-four hours, and it was closed for fifteen days, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the blood flowed so abundantly that it seemed he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not care for the ointment, because I was in a place where there was none, neither medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and put more oil on the wound two times a day, and poured honey on it until it healed
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or you will tell me two ways of sewing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and pass it through from the back of the part until it reaches the center;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the thumb on the right side, if the head of the thumb is swollen or bruised or if the needle has gone in too deep, withdraw the needle from the other side of the part until it reaches the base of the thumb.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And you must understand this suture as if you were making leather, and that you leave a space once the swelling has gone down, and you take it up again from the other side until the suture is complete
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of stitching is as Galiens does it properly, which is to join the two parts naturally together, and to press one head of the swelling against the other head, in a similar manner
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Burn an awl or thorn near the edge of the wound, and make the wound pierce only slightly, and leave the hair in place.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then withdraw the needle, and make it pierce from the back outwards until it reaches the center, leaving the hair in place
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	And make the wound pierce on both sides until it reaches the center, at two other awls that are on the other side
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	This is the usual method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	If anyone doubts this word, and no one testifies, we must suture the belly with two needles, or there is a thread in the gut
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who suture wounds
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And the stitches that when the rotation is inward of the belly, if the stitching is greater than others on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judge of the wound is like the judge of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even though it has moved, if you stop the bleeding and the swelling.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on absorbent powder around the wound, and if it has moved, do not put on any dressing that is present until the wound has healed;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and close the wound, and keep the dressing firm, and the bandage tight
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound like the others until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	If you have no medicine, put on a cloth, until it starts to bleed profusely, cotton wool, and move the limb twice as much as necessary until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For in many situations where wounds are simple, you need no other medicine.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	If you doubt that the wound will not heal, moisten the principal limb with warm oil of poppies or rosemary oil, and put on compresses; soak the wound and remove the discharge.</start_of_turn>
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	If there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, and it happens often, if you mix vinegar and black wine together, and do the same if the putrefaction reaches the intestines.</start_of_turn
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	The spleen and the large intestines are easier to heal than the small intestines.</start_of_turn
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot heal when they are swollen, because of the swelling of the veins, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the thread breaks from the wound, if it is returned backwards as with the intestines, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is black and has become towards or black, if you must know that you must bind the black part, for there are veins and arteries there.</start_of_turn>

Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, if you can restore it in small pieces, because I have seen that one bone has been fractured or belly of a spear;

je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put it to cure as much as I could, and did not cease to undermine until it was healed, and the pus was drained.

Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the head of the intestine is perforated and there is no further discomfort for the patient, and it can be tied up with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine itself, in part as before.</start_of_turn

Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds and abscesses, when they swell, if they are called universally "fistula", and even when they are closed and swollen.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	The fistula is, in truth, a necessary hardening and whitening of the nodes, or there is no pain, and it is as limp as a goose feather.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	never in clear water, and sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	never once, and sometimes rather;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not sanitized, and there is pus, must be caused by one of the seven causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of the blood or by pus;
ou por sa malice;	or for its malice;

Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	The wounds that fistula arise in all members are painful.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that arise from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the surface of the skin, or in the intestines, or the bladder, or in the ribs, or the scapula, or in any joint of the hands or feet.

et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if a fistula occurs, as when a worm attempts to plunge into it, for the worm will bend inwards towards the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the fistula has holes, and you do not manage it well with your attempts, if the worm bites through one of the holes, for moisture is short from one hole to another, and it fills the cavity.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then when its reason becomes evident to you, that there is bone or nerve involved, and the limb is bowed inward, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and the place or where he feels it
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	When you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein, or other bones that I have mentioned, if the limb is placed as I have said, and the bones are firm and the corrupted flesh is removed from it.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then the treatment must be complete when it is healed, and if the fistula is well formed from the right side, if you must break it, just do so; then put in ten soft compresses in medicine, and keep them until the medicine consumes the excess that is remaining at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then put in greasy ointments that are healing and safe until they are healed;

Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	And I tell you of a young man who was about thirty years of age, who had pain in his leg caused by something within his body, until the matter came out through a large abscess; and there was no other cause known to open it

dou feu	If you think of the instrument which you must employ in this case, according to what it is able to do.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, or by pressure, or by force
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated the inflammation with medicine, it does not help; if you cover that limb until the inflammation subsides, or if the inflammation returns, for the patient escapes by this means or by the greater malice of the defect of the limb
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if burnt by fire, and afterwards the blackness, for that inflammation of the limb spreads throughout the limb and takes hold of all the bones;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if you are in a hurry to cover it, and if it is from the bite of venomous creatures such as scorpions of the sea and vipers, and similar things, if the inflammation is at the root of the bone, if you touch it, and does not give you space to move your hand
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if the nail is at the joint, so that the cuticle does not reach the elbow;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes up to the forearm, if the nail is at the wrist, so that the cuticle does not reach the forearm.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the wrist, that is death, and there is no remedy but the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and all that you can do when the cuticle comes or is bent.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, if the nail follows the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the bone, if the nail goes through the whole bone.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it comes to the leg, if the nail is at the knee joint
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes from below the knee, if there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And if it comes from below the knee, if there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die; then grasp the limb with one hand below and above, and with one hand support the ligament below and the other support the ligament above, and cut the flesh between the two bones at the width of a nail, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then grasp the limb with one hand below and above, and with one hand support the ligament below and the other support the ligament above, and cut the flesh between the two bones at the width of a nail, until the bone is exposed; then pull out the bone or cut through the flesh, and put some lint on the wound so that the dressing does not touch the sound tissue, and make the patient another wound and incision around the wound
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if blood flows when you work, if you cauterize the wound immediately, or put on some restraining powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine as long as it is accompanied, and then bind the limb securely with a strong tie, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I will tell you that I have seen at home in this very place:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	there was a blackness that seemed to burn like fire, and that corrosion first appeared in the middle of the bone, so that it consumed the whole bone.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when we saw the corrosion, if we covered the bone, and it healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after the corrosion had gone away, it returned to me, and I put upon it things that rebounded after the removal of the callous, and it did not cease the corrosion
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	therefore I cut off the limb, and I did not dare to hope to save the matter
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	And I doubt also that if I cut off his hand, he will not die, for the strength of the man was feeble.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And he awoke completely, returned to his land, and took hold of his hand, and was healed
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	I have heard of nothing like this except in the case of necessity
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Blood often comes out of the vein in the bone, and it stays for such a long time that it makes great swelling
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then it returns and bursts, and in that jump there is a bursting of blood, and it stays in its place like vessels
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	The skin which is under is also as thin as draped cloth, and does not reach the bone, nor the nerve, and such diseases are called “sane”, and are not called “fistula”.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone in the marrow, it is called a fistula.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the wound if it is that you can embrace that skin all around, and even when it is subtle, like a drape.</start_of_turn>
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not remain because of its corruption.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have bound that the skin is split, and the corruption is not in the marrow, and the skin is thick like hair, so the surgeon must take care of the fistula.</start_of_turn
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	watch if the wound is great, and that the swelling is of foul odor, then apply Egyptian medicine which is made for this purpose.</start_of_turn
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take ease, and oil, and lard, equally, and put them on the wound over the vessel in the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	Then take what you need according to your need, and make it hot and sweet with honey, and clench your chest, and restrain the opening.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	Leave the medicine in for two hours, then remove it while squeezing out the excess.

Take vinegar from the root of the vine, and pour water over it, then let it drain, and clench, until you are sure that the wound is well healed

ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you bathe in some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken about the properties or treat with ointments.</start_of_turn>
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the opening of the wound is too small, and the cautery needle cannot enter, if the space has been enlarged by the point of a spear, put in an attempt of Egyptian or balsamic ointment, as much as it has been enlarged.

Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if it is found to be dislocated again after being adjusted, the limb remains stiff and does not yield.</start_of_turn>
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	If subtle drops appear after a long tension, do not fear for your life, for health is approaching.

et en use de simples ou de compostes:	And use simple or compound remedies.
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Grind them, and make powder, and sprinkle on honey that I mentioned above, and use it.</start_of_turn>
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	If the cure is prolonged, and has not healed from this treatment, then the abscess must be opened, for corruption has spread deep into the bone, or there is stiffness of the limb, or swelling.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If the cure for the fistula, as we said before.

Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	The swelling is an abscess that originates from the boil of the hand, or the heel, or by chance originates in other places;

Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints which arise in the hands of some men by chance are always fleshy, and in some there is bone, and never is there a nail, and never are any born in the root of the joint, or are they born in our hands from the two joints.

He who is born or must afterwards in no wound, if you must, first cover the rounded fat until the bone, then grasp the bone to a suitable width like that, and then cure until it is healed whole
