des vils	stink.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	These veins are large vessels covered with black mucus filled with sorrow, which comes to cause pain in many limbs
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often cause those who travel on foot and work and carry burdens than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not give any purgatives of colchicum, and then the rest of the balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure of fire is as follows: two methods.
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One method is with the forceps, and one treats the black blood by burning it.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The other method is to ligate the vein, and then burn it thoroughly.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size is as these two methods allow
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	The limb should be made hot with strong heat, until the great part without being split is soft, and then strain the limb of the patient from under the buttock down to the part below the knee
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then ligate the vein in one, two or three places, of a large size, and then burn from the head to the tail, as much as the patient can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	Then the leech is taken, and it is commanded that it should seize hold of flesh surrounding the black mole.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	Then the evacuation and bleeding recommences when the veins are full, and harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The nourishment of the limb is in this way:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	raises the limb of the patient, if there is any hair, then puts it in water or oil, and raises the limb of warm water until it turns red, and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no oil, if the limb is burnt by fire, then grasp the limb at the long bone at the shoulder or at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then apply leather to the burn, and loosen the vein from below, until it appears when it is felt
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And on the wound one sees red and black, and when it enters or leather seems just like a white thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then one should stretch the wound, until it reaches the leather, and then pin it with a lesser weight, and then put a weight on it in another place in the third degree;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then pull the leather over the wound until it appears, then tie it firmly, as you have done previously, and pin it with another weight as you did before
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then pin another weight, or several if you need them, and then tie it, and pin it at the root, and pull and tie until the second degree
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then pull out the weight degree by degree, until it is all gone, and then pin it
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you do not handle and lift it, if there is a nail at the end of all its might, hold it fast and pull it out, and there will be blood, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it is gone.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	Hold that it does not slip, for if it slips, it cannot be handled or lifted, and this brings harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	When you have finished treating it, put out the limb from the wound with vinegar and rose oil
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the limb is contracted and twisted and bound together, and it is not straight, as we have said, if you must force it open, but do not cover it up
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And thus it is with us that we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the fire from which we take hold of the bone is crooked, and does not tear me, except that it takes hold of the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	It is of great curvature, for if it were slight, it would tear the vein, but being thick as we have said, this is the shape
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is enclosed in the limb, in hot parts or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth or where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And sometimes it happens elsewhere except in the limb, and this comes from the rotting that comes from the decay of the skin, as it comes from the inside of the serpent's body and outwards, enclosed between the skin and flesh
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if there is a sign of the beginning of this vein, that is, if there comes into the limb a very great swelling, then it chains the blood, and the vein begins to swell like a plant root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the arm is dislocated, if you wish to cover it, take a piece of sponge from one and a half fingers’ breadth to two and a half, and hold it, and leave the sponge on the limb; every time that it points downwards, if you cover the sponge and the thumb, hold them.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	If it is too long, if in its course you cut off a part, and cover the remainder, do not cover it at its root until it is fully healed;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, if it returns to the bone, it brings about inflammation and pus or swelling, and makes the disease worse.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore it is necessary to treat it thoroughly and leave nothing or bone behind
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And never has this vein escaped me when treated with five palms of length, or with ten; and once it escapes from ten palms of length, when you grasp it, if there is even a hair or a wound, and the blood flows until it stops.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And either empty the contents that are within, and bring medicines to the place; without causing any swelling, then cure as with abscesses.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never has this vein been grasped by the hands, even when it bursts at the joint of the thumb or the little finger, and there comes blood from a wound; from which it leaps again.</start_of_turn
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure in this way as we have said before.</start_of_turn>
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never has this vein hands rained, even when it opens at the elbow, or at the wrist, and there comes moisture from the rupture; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "beef disease" because it often causes swelling of the buttocks, and is like a small wound between skin and bone, which rises throughout the body, upwards and downwards, and the patient feels it well in every limb, as long as it tears the skin or goes away, and leaps fiercely.</start_of_turn
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is said that from any humor, when it comes and bites like serpents and worms and beetles or belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and there is doubt of its malice, for when it goes through the body and ascends to the head, and comes to the surface, by chance it returns and destroys the substance.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and treated, if one cannot drive it out until it goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then you must certainly bind up the limb above and below with a strong and tight ligature, and then support above and support below, and when it is moved into the fire it will be consumed and will die
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm that it makes is when it contaminates the oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming or near the oil, immediately grasp its bristle and hold it above, and push it away forcefully
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And you must use the patient for the application of external medicines to dissolve bad humors caused by bodily humors, and feed him nourishing foods rich in protein
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	When you see it cured and treated, if it will not go away, then do this: bind the limb above and below with a strong thread, then put a cautery on the surface and burn it until it dies; for the greatest harm that it does is when it runs counter to the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, strain from it the hair that grows on the edge, then put a cautery on, and burn it. And use the patient of purgatives of corrosive medicines for the bad humors that are carried, and give him nourishing food.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This ailment is called in our land "Vakirir," and is a pain that comes in the joints, and which passes from one limb to another
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	I saw that which I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and saw her arm swollen, and discovered a small swelling in the belly of her arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And thus afterwards, the limb will rise up like a worm at the shoulder, more erect than anything else, like a living silver when it breaks from its root to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain departs from that root and rests in the shoulder, and then afterwards it is corrected throughout the limb, until it comes to the other arm
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then it was told to me that it twisted back towards the limb, as I saw it
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it twisted back inwards towards the body, for I had never seen such a disease in this way before.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I would advise that if you wish to move the limb from one place to another, you must not cause pain in the limb, but I do not wish you to move it, as I have seen it in women
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because of that that the women had dry limbs, and their veins uncovered, and because of that appeared that constraint of that stiffness.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not appear to me according to this reason to those who are fond of such things, and who have moist skin and veins filled with blood.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	When you see this disease cured, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, if the lymph below and above has become swollen, and then lies upon them as long as this constraint of the wind opposes;
et cauterize le leu;	and burn the flesh
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it at your eyes, if you cure it of that which evacuates the wind, as foul pills, and oily pills, and similar things
des saiettes	And when you see the healing of this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if the swelling above and below has persisted, and then press over until the wind pressure is overcome; and cauterize the limb. And if you do not see it in your eyes, if he is cured of that which causes the wind pressure, as foul pills, and pilules of serpin, and similar things.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The towels are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the wound or the pain they relieve.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is such that some have large points, and small, and hairs, and pus;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those in which there are pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And those which break in no limb break in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal bone breaks, as with the skull, forearm, heel, shoulder blade, ribs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it breaks in no place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, will teach you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if you know that you must extract this shard, for death comes afterwards in various positions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this sign is not present, do not teach me, for the shard does not go deep, if you follow, and cure the wound.</start_of_turn>
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of a fractured skull when a splinter pierces the bone, and leaps the blood that is above the skull, is when scraping and soiling and vomiting and nausea, and redness of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of senses, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and sometimes there is no wound, or no ear;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	or by chance it causes the speech and the voice to stammer
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from a white moist wound resembling a boil, and also like burnt barley.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears, if you hold back treatment, and withdraw the splinter if it has not penetrated
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the splinter when it breaks or curves is that it is close to the left breast, and it feels as if it were stuck in something hard, without emptying;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the eye turns just like the pouls, and in dark blood, and comes cold sweat and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The eyes then sense doubt that the death is coming.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a wound that never heals is that there is no scab on the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes heavily and sweats profusely.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the eye is struck in the corner of the eye, if it is taken out of the small bones.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	it spits greatly and suffers great pain and breath is suspended
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the limbs are moving around
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the arrow comes out or remains in the flesh, by chance there is no sign of indigestible meat in the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the arrow comes out or remains in the flesh, and there is no sign of feces in the intestine, if there is no hope of recovery, do not attempt to extract the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	and if the eye is struck in the bladder, and it urinates in leaps and comes out running, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	The wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	As for the other limb, if the face, the neck, the chest, the armpit, the groin, the buttock, the thigh, and the leg are affected, and the like, there are many possible causes.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the stone is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have mentioned before.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	And there is at home a woman who has a lash or mucus in the root of the eye:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I grasped it, and by force from the other side I drew out the fat of the ear, and it was cured without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I pulled out a splinter from the fat of the ear, at the root of the hair, and the splinter was restored, and did not reach beyond the tip towards the head, and the splinter was as large as a Turkish bow, all in all it was a perfect cure for the ear
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The pain was cured, and no bad effects followed
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from the throat to the chin, and the arrow was Arabic in the ear
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I soothed the barbs, and held it tight until I pulled it out, and the chin was cured
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I took out an arrow from his side, which was in the hip or belly, and I thought he was dying.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and when he had not passed three days, if he did not recover his health;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, and I pulled it out, and I pulled out the swelling, and there was no further harm done.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if I took out an arrow from his side or from his back, and the wound was deep, then;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	I left the arrow in, and I did not constrain his natural inclinations, and I found no discomfort in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And when another man had an arrow go into his face, and the wound was deep, then
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	And so it often happens that great pain accompanies this.
et mout d’autres semblans.	and that of other things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And to carry out an arrow at home of a prince the king, that it was stuck deeply among the bones, and was a weakening inclination to the lower part;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely withdrawn.</start_of_turn>
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to care after three days that it had been stuck.</start_of_turn
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very inflamed.

Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought that it was the tip of the arrow. I put on the therapeutic plaster plaster of digestion, so that it would not swell.</start_of_turn
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And there appeared to me the wound of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I held the hands above the wound, and closed the wound again, and held the patient firmly until the arrow was removed from his body;
et il le me dist.	And he told me.

adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore, I will persevere in subtle methods and contrivances of various instruments, until I have made the grasp truly firm, as is appropriate for this ailment, until I have finished this chapter and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or as you have said concerning the quality of the extraction of some clots, if you place your remedy on something that I do not know, for the books do not teach me everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but you know the masters compare well with great things, and with what is present and lacking, find nine works, and a new instrument, following the order of things that arise in this art
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that the arrows do not emerge from members or are fictiously bound for that matter.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by liquid discharge or they enter, or by another way.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which comes forth for liquid or enters, is an arrow broken within flesh, and never comes out again
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	and if it does not come out now, let it stay as long as the flesh is swollen, and rejoice in its issue
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is bound in bone and cannot be extracted, if you leave it alone for a while, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	then it will come out, and if it does not come out, if you prick through all the soft parts, as long as the flesh is swollen, and then take it out
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the splinter is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the things I have mentioned before to the patient.

And if the splinter is fixed only in the bone and does not reach the surface, and remains in the patient for some days without any other accident, if the limb is not treated properly.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	If it is firmly fixed and cannot be extracted, if you administer tarriers around it, as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the splinter is replaced in the bone so that it cannot be seen, if you have tried everything;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, if the pain has no palpable cause;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you do not perceive it from the wound, and from the depth of the wound, and there is neither bone, nerve, nor vein, if the pain persists as long as the wound is great.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And if you see blood in the wound, if there is a swelling in the wound, if there is an object caught in the wound, or if the limb is fractured, do not pull out the arrow until you have broken or softened the swelling of the wound as much as possible.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	Be cautious not to break the arrow, but grasp it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not succeed at once, if the limb remains bent over, then grasp it firmly, for the extraction will bring relief.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	If blood continues to flow from the wound, follow what is said in this chapter about treatment;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And take care not to cut into the nerve or the vein, and put in place as you wish to remove the arrow, either forward or backward, or firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	Put the patient in the position in which he was when the arrow went in, for this is the greatest help, and if you do not know how, follow what the signs tell you
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or if you see no wound, or the skin is swollen in that place if you see it or feel it.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Therefore, take hold of it until the nails can grasp, and then extract it
si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you round your hand around it until it enters the bone, expand the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be pulled out, if you leave it in, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if it is from an arrow, it is, if the wound is great;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	And if it is from an arrow, it is, if the wound is great; and if you see it administered immediately, if it is administered with a pointed instrument that grasps the tip of the arrow between the teeth of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	Then hold the wound firm, and if the arrow is grasped, hold the instrument pointed inwards so that the tip of the arrow is grasped by the teeth of the instrument.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, then you must take hold of all the surrounding flesh or the venom is there, if you believe so; then cure the wound as it seems right.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is torn or broken or in the belly or in the bladder or in the chest, and it is close, and you must cover over it, if you cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	Keep covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract the arrow, and then close the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment must be such that it is harmless.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers with which we treat the splinters is similar to the beak of an eel, and thus is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways to do it.
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, moderate, or small, according to the amount of blood
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the tip of the bone is like the quill of a bird, to push out the point of the wound, as in this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the nails to push and to grasp if it is like this:</start_of_turn
des voinnes dou cors communes	From common veins.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of veins from which one has bled for a long time, there are some which have had or will have sixteen inches, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two veins which are behind the ears, which are covered by hair
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and two arteries which are in the temples appearing;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And if two veins are two cubits long, which are called "aspires,
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is at the front of the eye;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the back of the eye.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two strings that are either yellow or white.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are under the chin, which are called "augeherich.
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are beside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The common veins are those that are in the armpits of the arms:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and is on the left side of the chest, and they call it the great vein
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	The hair is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalique and basilique; and they call it the people "belly of the head".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The basilique if it is thick or dull is called "belly of the belly"; and they call it the people "belly of the belly", and is above the navel, and is the one from which one sees, which manifests openly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saving is the vein which is between the auriculaire and the anulaire, and if it has two veins;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the limb and the foot are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one if it is thick the bulge of the pouch of the left costa, and the second is sophene which is at the ankle of the right costa
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and the vein which is called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other limb; and in the other limb are three veins similar to these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps as old purges and eliminates; and it causes emigration.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the healthy person, as I have told you, is that you raise the head of the patient and rub the body or the veins are rough;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tighten the patient's neck with a screw, as long as the two veins which appear behind the ears rest in two loops depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	when you have done this, and you feel the pulse from these veins, if it signifies an embolism
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet, and hold it by the edge of the vein until it reaches the bone, then keep your hand over the upper part of the vein, and press and squeeze the skin and the vein well; two should pierce through, and make blood flow as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then strain and hold it tight, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said concerning the incision and the cautery or the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration, sode, and obtalmia accustomed, and at the root of the tears there are blisters.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of the patient if it is like I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the patient strains his neck, so that the two veins open wide.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	he feels a tingling sensation in his teeth, and then he groans loudly.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then he takes hold of the vein in his upper arm with his index finger, grasps the lancet, grasps the vein in his upper arm and holds it, just as you would with the two lower veins, and makes blood flow according to your need
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then he releases the patient, and puts his hand on the vein for an hour, and then puts on a bandage
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then he binds it and leaves it until it is healed
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and as for the other things we have spoken of them in their place and their treatment and their extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as that from the cephalic vein has ancient diseases of the face, has emigration, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and if the patient turns his head violently, as when the vein bursts open.</start_of_turn>
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called the "forceps", which has this shape:</start_of_turn
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see.</start_of_turn
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient’s neck, and tie the vein until it is well healed and never do it with a wide flame.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not right for the flames to be too great;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the latter [hair] through, for the bones are near, and by chance break the flames when they are slight.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood of two veins that are two cubits long if they aid the abscess, and the swelling, and the redness, and the yellowing in the fat, and diseases of the face
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their blood is that if the patient strains his neck by turning from side to side, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the latter, and let the blood flow slowly, a long flame a wide base, because there is no fat
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	and if the flame is slight, by chance it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make the blood flow out freely, as much as you are able, and then hold it on a cloth, and bind it firmly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The blood from the vein does not flow if it is clotted, and if it is forced out, and in diseases of the face, such as measles and redness that comes on the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And if the patient is spitting blood, then strain his neck to your left hand, and take a piece of charcoal long, and put it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open very well indeed, and you must begin to correct it now
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	Do not go too quickly, and make the blood flow out according to your need, and then hold it for a night, because it is often restored by rest.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the form of the fire:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	And this is the form of the fire: the blood of the two armpits assists in the expansion of the spleen, and in the beginning of mixing, and in the mouth of diseases, and in spitting, and in corrosiveness, and in herpes, and in stone-like things.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the blood is that if the patient pulls out his collar with one hand and with the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Or let the master be above the patient’s head, and the patient sit on one seat, then open the vein widely, and take blood steadily, or as much as is necessary
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then do the other part in the other vein, and remove the ligature, and tighten loosely the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	And let him leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the livers.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the arms above helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and wounds of the arms, and toothache and pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And if you must make the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then open the eyelid, and look at two veins, one on the outer eyelid and the other on the inner, and know them by their darkness, and by the fact that there are small black veins running alongside them
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Therefore close both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, if the larger one is at the corner of the eye, and both of the lower and upper veins as well, for this is a mean method
de la sainie desoz la lengue	And of the blood of the veins the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of the lower veins flows after the blood of the cephalic vein, and this is at the widening of the throat, and it has diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And if the patient faces the sun with hands clasped before him, tongue lolling out, and looks at the ground beside each rib, there is a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then one must grasp both [arms] firmly, and do not move them too much, for these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The common veins which we commonly grasp are healthy in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or if you prick at their root with a blunt lancet like olive oil, which is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	They are wide and slippery according to the size and distance of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of the fire cautery is known to be round, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the superficial veins filled with thick blood which contain much blood and disorder;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for healthier veins, or there is citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	And this is the form of the olive flame: the blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps with ailments such as those that are in the throat, or the collar, or the teeth, or the belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the patient to keep his body still and to stop the artery that is near
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If he bites the artery, and blood flows out, if the bleeding continues, if you have said so;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	You must not be hasty with the flame, but must keep it at a distance as if it were an animal.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilisk does not clearly appear, if you must grasp it, and bind another one instead
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	Or you want no rain from it, or you keep in its place the vein filled with blood in the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens openly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the head of the shoulder is dislocated, as we have said
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	and if you see the blood spurting, if you must indeed take hold of the limb, touch the limb until you see the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the head of the dislocation, and then join the limb, and keep the vein filled with blood open
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and beware that you do not damage the artery when you see the limb swollen, for that is the artery
eschui la donques.	indeed.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it swell up like the urine of a child, and it is neither red nor pale, know that it is without an artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Quickly then, put your hand over its length, and hold it steady, for many times it has happened to me
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	so that the limb remains still and does not move the patient;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	or until it has healed properly.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	if it is not bleeding and you feel pain, and the medicine is not present, if the artery is opened, for the head of the shoulder is pulled out.
et estainche li sans.	stop the bleeding immediately.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	and take a piece of sponge, put it on, and take one of them and place it well until the other side is reached
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If he does not stain them, it is well.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If not, if the physician does so as we have said, with powders that stain blood
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stainings do not last long in various situations because of the little movement of the wound and the swelling.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The blood in the vein helps to heal it from the top downwards, and from the outside inwards, because it is composed of the fatty and bony parts, as we have said
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is important that the nerve that is outside should not be too deeply bruised, and if it is too deep, it will tear the nerve, and it will swell and the wound will either be scarred or will not heal at all
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some homes due to its subtlety, it is certain that you must use an anesthetic instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And hold the nerve still at its root.</start_of_turn>
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if the vein is long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The blood of the cephalic vein assists, for it pulls blood towards the head, and helps the eyes.</start_of_turn
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	It is certain to make the patient feel better by pricking with the olive or myrtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins, for it has neither nerve nor artery.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to inquire about the degree of pain beforehand, and grieve nothing if it is the first time, and we begin again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance the swelling goes up to some homes, which cannot be forced out the first time, but it matters not.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about health is that blood must not be forced out except for the preservation of health and to repel diseases to come.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	or be made in one of the three veins that are or should be seen to be well-formed;
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	namely the cephalic, facial, and basilar veins;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	it must be done at the beginning of the prayer before fasting, and after meals when the signs of fullness appear
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	it must be done the first or third hour, after two or three hours or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The blood which is administered for diseases has no definite measure, but when need arises for urine or stool, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not permitted to give blood to children under twelve years of age, nor to women who are pregnant for more than four months up to seven times.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Must not be given to those who have passed 60 years.</start_of_turn>
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	When anyone sees a bloodletting, in whatever way, if it is commanded to evacuate the intestines of a light fistula, if there is much mucus retained, so that the veins do not draw out the useful humors from the principal parts
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	and it is not right that he should be too fat with meat, or that he should be very drunk, as much as there may be force in him, or hydrops
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if he suffers from vomiting, pain in the belly, and swelling of the belly, and frequent urination, and sweating, and guarding, and lying in bed, and all his forces, either from the weapon or from the illness;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then conceal the humors, if they are not great, by meats and by drinks and by medicines, if you can find any good ones.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then give him a bath or a wash, if nothing else hinders, to conceal the blood, and keep him warm from the belly to the chest, as we have said before
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep him away from work, from worry, from luxury, and from similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	keep him bound and quiet, and let the patient be higher than his companions, and massage his arms two or three times, then gently pull out the thread below moderately, for if it is too tight or loose, it will not be able to correct itself without
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then he wipes the limb with his hands, until the veins swell up, and one can feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And then he wets the limb with a little oil, then puts his left hand on that vein below the limb a little above or below where he wants to make the incision, so that the vein does not burst and cause injury.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that run like strings to the patient, and if they are filled with wind, so that when one puts on the flame and takes it away, it cannot open the vein, and thus is this the result of that
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he severs the vein, if the wound is too wide, because of this one must be warned about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein bursts the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	otherwise, if it bursts again later, a little more than before, if the swelling has not subsided.</start_of_turn>
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the swelling has gone down, and the patient groans, if one leaves the arm hanging about for an hour or two, and does not bind it,
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	it will burst again.</start_of_turn
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter or bathe, and then burst the blood again.</start_of_turn
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small, or if it lacks a visible mark and you doubt that there is not as much blood as you saw, if you are confident in the wound itself with all your might.</start_of_turn
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And the work of a physician must be with great care, even if the illness is acute.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for often in such work, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb inflamed, do not immediately resume the bleeding, but apply a layer of oil over the wound, for it softens the flesh of blood, and hinders the pain in this limb that the oil covers
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and also administer oil to the wound to staunch the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this also causes a tingling and swelling of the limb when applied to the limb;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if it is applied too thickly and comes away when too large
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a large boil, which happens many times, even when it is not seriously infected except for this time or the opening of the vein is small, if you are hasty, put on the sponge soaked in water and in silk a little cloth, and hold for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And do it afterwards when the blood has stopped flowing from the vein, and if it remains fixed after a few days no black or green discoloration, if that does not happen to me.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, put on no other dressing or unguents made from beeswax, mastic, or the like.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times there comes a boil and the appearance of blood in the basilisk’s urine.
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Put your hand on it, and if you feel the limb soft under the compression of the hand, it is that bad appearance
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Listen then, do not put anything of what we have said upon the wound, for by chance in the court without an artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Listen then, do not put anything of what we have said upon the wound, for by chance in the court without an artery; but it makes it swell dry to harden the limb, then cure it with another cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And take out each piece of blood according to the amount of its virtue, and its color.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if it is without color, if you leave it festering as long as it is red,
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it black, if you leave it festering as long as it is subtle.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too thick, if you let it cool down.</start_of_turn>
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is appropriate for the one who is plain and strong, and has the skill of extracting blood, to make the wound larger, and the flame wider.</start_of_turn>
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the weakling, do the opposite, and bind it firmly so often, and must bind it firmly by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding saves the blood from decay and swelling, and is more effective than letting it drain for a long time.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for the one who has a swollen limb due to the bleeding, bind soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice around it
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if he is pale, if he has three or four bleedings, and if he is of a pale complexion, mix before the bleeding soft bread soaked in fragrant oil of poppy seeds, or in beeswax with aromatic spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant oil
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he drinks at the blood, after the issue of mouth blood, it is to be believed that he will vomit bile, an odorous liquid, and use other things which we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the belly.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he sees that his arm has turned pale, and he feels well again another time, if it is possible by great bleeding, let it rest still and still, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever has seen his arm swollen after the first bleeding, and has strong swelling, if he remains thus for thirteen hours after the first bleeding, or after the twelfth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever has seen himself well on one side, if he must remain well for the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood in the limb that is already pale, and it causes fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	If it is necessary to handle a great quantity, and to widen the opening as much as necessary;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	Then you must provide all the necessary precautions, and place your hand over the wound when it is healthy, so that the blood does not flow in place of the flesh, and this often happens when the patient is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	Do not attempt anything if you see the limb slip again, and do not open the wound a second time; the opening is closed, so press firmly on it
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is crooked, extend the limb as much as possible, because that is better;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	But leave it until it heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Or you apply the point of the flame until the blood vessel that is frozen at the opening of the vein bursts, and place over it a little piece of cloth wet with water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has escaped, if you leave it alone and do not restrain me, until the swelling subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to drain blood the second time, if the same in this limb or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is saved in place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And if the patient grasps his hand in warm water, until the flesh is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind it loosely, so that the vein opens well, and do not make it too wide or long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and if it does not open, keep the hand in warm water until the blood has clotted sufficiently; then withdraw the hand from the water and leave the blood to drain naturally until enough has drained out
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not put the hand back in the warm water, for it will swell more in the water than it did before.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The blood of this vein is more precious than all the others, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The saliva from the thumb of the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	The saliva from the thumb of the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver. Strain the hand and hold it in hot water, until the belly is emptied if you see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the side of the hand turns pale, and if you embrace it all the way round, if it does not grieve anything
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and does not swell too much, for the nerves are all loosened from their sheath, and then reset the hand in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not touch it
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, if you put oil and lint on the wound, it will help to hold it together, and put on a bandage.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth to the disease of the mice, and do the same as I have said concerning the right side.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the spleen is worth for all the diseases which are caused by the heat of the body, such as diseases of the marrow, retention of flowers, diseases of the rains, and of the cramps and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	and the quality of its saliva is that the patient should soak in hot water, and wipe over the belly until it is limp, and lie down under the joint of the thumb.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And if the vein is at the ankle, and below the heel bone there comes out a torrent of blood.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	pure or more copious rain, or at the ankle, that the limb is swollen.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	If you see blood dripping from the heel bone, beware of the nerves that are loosened, and the limb will recover as if you were grasping it
et soit li flaimes anesil.	or the fire is extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it does not recover, if you reset the limb in the water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	If the patient must be treated again the second time, because the first treatment did not work, because the pus is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and do the same on the opposite side evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The blood of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that is clotted.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	If the blood is thick and the patient groans or sweats, and pulls the limb away from the ankle twice, because otherwise the vein will burst;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if she opens, if he is sound in every way, as much as you can, and through and through.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	it is worth noting that you must hold her firmly, for her spirit is strong, and she is easily restored by hand alone.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	and if you do not find her, if she is sound neither head nor tail, nor in the least towards the little toe, and you guard against the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	then do as much to staunch the blood as you see, and then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton and bind it tightly
ele est maintenant sanee.	she is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of bloodletting
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Wounds are made of horn, or spider’s silk, or hair
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and the cautery is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	Or by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting. And this bleeding which is done by cutting is in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is at full heat, or by cutting.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	or bleeding which is done by cutting and by extraction of blood if it is done in twelve weeks of summer, when one is all swollen at the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is at the collarbone
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in two ribs of the collarbone;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the wound from the bleeding fills the mouth
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the wound from the bleeding fills the space between the ribs
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the sponge on the crupies.
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	And the sponges cover the two arms
et les ventouses des II jambes;	And the sponges cover the two legs
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	And the sponges cover the two ankles
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And the sponge does not touch blood, for there are many veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this one must not make any bleeding from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	One must only apply it [the sponge] when it is necessary, not with fire or sensation of fire, in no disease that comes from congestion, until all the swelling has gone down
