Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of a disease it is necessary to sponge, or for custom, if one administers it carelessly at the beginning or at the end, and over and over again, in every embrace;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they are blown about by the wind, bear a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who suffer swelling and redness in their face, and on their head, and at the collar, and they have swollen eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are those who spit blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and swallow blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who faint, and see stars and blood and mud and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is wet and moist, we command them to fast for two hours after dinner.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	Blood from the wound helps to relieve the pain of the head … which comes from the eyes, and it is not possible for me to know anything other than that after the evacuation of all the fat
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this vomiting is in place of the blood of the head, and it is not possible for me to know anything other than that it is from those who are of a cold complexion in use, or who are consumptive, for this causes them great discomfort
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason, I advise you to refrain from using it in cases where there are cold or chief fevers.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if the patient is conscious, if he becomes dizzy, it is necessary to place the suction tube one place further down the throat due to the doubt of dizziness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The winds of the head are in lieu of the blood of the chief and of the bile, and for this reason it is worth more for its stretching out of the spleen, and for the splitting of the channel of the marrow, and for all, and for distension;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	I must advise you not to force it, for if it is held too tightly, it causes disgust or swelling of the belly or the chest or the head.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The winds cause two costels of the head if it is worth as much as the pains of the chief, and oblation and vomiting, and strangulation, and toothache, and it is in lieu of the blood of the bile
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	You must command the patient to grasp his hand to put it in place, so that he does not obstruct the artery or blood vessels nearby.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The windings of the nose are like the cause of oral disease, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	This is related to the health of the two lower teeth
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds blow cold from the coast and cause disease that comes from heat and swelling.</start_of_turn
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The windings of the tonsils are as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these three veins
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Command the patient not to move too much, for the blood vessel is delicate, and knows that there are nerves and arteries nearby.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The swelling that is on the rump is like blood clots at the foundation, and there are diseases from this; you must make the swelling large and round, that it has mixed well together
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And by chance, if it were subtle, if it should break;
et i fai grans plaies.	And thus it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The veins of the leg swell open widely, because they draw blood from all over the body, and cause the ancient pains of rain, and of worms, and of the bladder, and cause swelling of the flowers;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are in the place of the two shoulders, and of the two knees, and all of them grow pale after a long time, and cause death in many cases
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of placing the vein is that you must put it on empty first, and then temperately, and put it on immediately, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the limb red and swollen, and when the blood appears red;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then be fierce, and reset the incisions, and take care in the arrangement of the limbs, for there are some who have twisted their thighs, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to wound once only, and make large incisions, and a deep wound;
et suce legierement.	and do so gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if it is not large, if you can wound twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to make the opening of the blood less painful.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	and if it is not very thick, if you can wound three times.</start_of_turn
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when our veins swell with blood once and twice, if we stop wounding only once.</start_of_turn>
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if our veins burst with blood, if we should often renew them;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if they are not immediately apparent, if they are fiercely inflamed, and if they are perceived to be clotted, it is prudent for those who have thick skin and brittle veins, and who have swollen pores, to administer purgatives of oil that are both aperitif and dissolving.</start_of_turn>
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If this is the case, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil.</start_of_turn
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if in wine, with rosemary oil, or lily oil, or chamomile, or something similar.</start_of_turn>
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is great and cold, if take oil of marigold, or balsam, or oil of ivy, and the like.</start_of_turn>
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one has stubborn pain and large pores, one must not put oil on, but it is necessary to wash after the evacuation of rose water, or cold water, or black bile, or pumpkin seed water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture in his mouth, if he rises easily, or from a surge of mint, and thyme, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	These who have large superabundances may rise from old wine, or water of hemlock, or decoction of ivy or chamomile, or other things of that kind.</start_of_turn
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it is not permitted for the physician to use the vacuum before the bath, neither during the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not sleep afterwards the venting, and must keep awake when it is necessary to vent and when it is vented.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And keep oneself from eating anything cold, and if it is too hot or inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it is possible that he grasp cold things, such as pomegranates and cucumbers and lettuce at ease, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And eat barley broth, and broth of barley, and soft meats
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine medium, which is between wheat and barley, and eat little, and eat barley broth and little oilseeds and herbs;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And when it is windy, if he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and must give to others homes no time a tickling or mustering before or after, for to comfort the principal limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	or be silent about it, but I must tell you that only those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The winds that cause wounds are those that are put on the liver, and on the wrist, and under the heel, and on the belly and the buttock and the groin and the hip, for these members do not suffer wounds above the joints, and they do not make them except to draw blood from one member to another, as we do when we put them on the armpits when we do not want to bleed
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to overcome the stiffness that is in the limb, as when we put winds on the belly and the buttock to soften the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And the bone causes pain, when there is an operation or a stone, for the bone, by its attractive virtue, attracts the operation, or deserts the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And it makes swell when it is placed on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained wind, and these swellings are administered empty so as to suck up only;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And never are they administered together with fire, and never completely filled with cold water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a manner we fill the swelling with hot water so that there are herbs covering it
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the compress administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And there are two palms and a half of barley, or cost the entrance between the mileu and I little hole, as to pierce an arrow, and be of marrow, if so that it does not grieve the patient when placing it on the limb
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And in the middle put a twig of flax or iron, to hold a tampon in place, and let it be great or small according to the ailments and the extent of those who take it.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the swellings of the limbs are different from intestines, and fats from bones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must be placed on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	holding the tampon of cloth or linen, and put it between the thumb and the ventouse, so that it sticks to the end of the ventouse without burning the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and put it on the limb, and must be put either on the wound that we have said, so that when it is seen, if it goes away, we will know that the ventouse is in the right place
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And hold it firmly in line as before, and repeat often, if you are skillful.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	And in the chest where it is administered for the disease of pleura, at all times, there is no swelling or perforation, and it is only administered when it is plain water, and is placed upon the limb only lightly.
et c’est li forme:	This sentence is incomplete and does not provide any meaningful translation.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	They are only administered in limbs or where we cannot put compresses because of their small size, such as the palms of the hands and the gums, and similar things
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the places where there is no hair, such as the nails or teeth, and other things of that kind.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the patient is that when you find blisters that are soft and clear without any sign of puncture, if you take hold of them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put on them a nut in warm water, until they are familiar, and they have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleansed of vein and vacuum, and then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the bandage.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	when they are full, and cheerful, if it is possible to put on a vacuum, put it on, for this is better afterwards
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, if you lift the limb easily, and then with water, moist well, and then press it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb is too red afterwards take off the bandage, and put on a cloth of linen in cold water, and put on until the bandage is loosened
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if it does not mend by itself, put upon a broken glass vial or scraps of glass, and similar things, until it is extended.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you take half of a clove of garlic and leave it on the limb until it blisters; then it will stop bleeding now.</start_of_turn>
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more pain, take other unguents.</start_of_turn>
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the unguents do not help, rub the limb with fresh blood, or put in an awl as long as it does not go in, and then put it back on, and as soon as it feels blood, it will heal.</start_of_turn
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that it is bleeding, put over it a little bit of aloe and a bit of burnt wool, or charcoal, if it will stop bleeding now.</start_of_turn
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This marks the beginning of the book of broken bones.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and displacement.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Saichiez, dear son, that in this chapter the fools gather, who do not see in any of the ancient books, neither in any letter, anything like it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason is it strange in our land, for I have never found anything like it before
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	I do not know anything about it, except by the science of the ancient books, or because I have studied so much that I have treated this science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	I have described it in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have summarized at the end, and I have made it clear the shapes of the instruments that are brought in, as I have done in the two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary, therefore, that our words or prologue of this book should be an image of the truth and the chapters or lessons should place their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are proved right learn and master this noble art, and learn it from others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that whenever a break or dislocation or twist or fracture occurs, if you must hasten the patient to safety, do not neglect the patient from either side, if nothing else hinders you, even if you are weak of limb or young or old.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the patient is tense or too cold or too hot;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold dishes, such as cold broth, mustard and chamomile, and do not drink wine, do not eat greasy foods or eat too much meat, until you are certain that there is no break or fracture of the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient recovers somewhat at first, use the first remedy that you find useful.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the fractured bone begins to heal, if you must restore the patient, do not nourish the patient with meats that cause great swelling, or that have viscosity, such as wheat germ in water, and pork, and testicles, and spleen, and veins, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For in part nourishment returns muscle and more quickly the fracture breaks.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	Know that bones that are broken in pieces and decrepit do not mend well by themselves, neither by soldering according to their nature because of the drying up of the limbs, nor because they are too brittle, as in the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no cure, rest on the broken bone and keep the great tension that is necessary to join the limb together, until it is firm as it was before
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not take away from it any of its substance, for because of this we must nourish it with great foods, as we have said
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.</start_of_turn
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by bending, as with the size of a pen to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a whole small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And with some measure, there is its own engine and its own instrument in restoring, according to what comes to mind in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the breaking of the bone is because its substance is twisted, and opens well by driving out, and some by pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	When there is no swelling or touch, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may well have swelling, or tear, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not possible to move the limb by hand, but medicines come after, then hold it firmly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And the blood that comes from the fracture, and is in the joint, it must now be put back in its place equally, even as if it were alive.</start_of_turn>
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if there are afterpains that come, if you leave them without treatment, until the afterpain is calmed.</start_of_turn
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it in its place gently and steadily, and the blood that restores it is less heavy than the restoring of those who have fragments.</start_of_turn
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then the stretching, as it should be after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken bones, if it extends from two parts, if it is hands or feet, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or at two strings, or at a string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb in its natural position, so that when the broken parts of the limb are relieved, if you maintain by all means the adjuncts to their places as much as possible, and keep that by your work there comes no further injury or pain to the patient
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel well the hand if you think that it is not well:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If the swelling subsides beautifully, and does not irritate me too much, do not press so much as those who make it come by their work of incision and contraction of the limb; for we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is fixed, if the patient is very painful that he does not move it, neither waking nor sleeping, neither turning nor doing anything else;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	Beware that the limb is well secured that he does not feel any pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it is not fixed, and you can put it in a position where he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And keep him straight, so that there is no twisting when you restore it.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of a broken limb is as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The limb is braced in various ways in small and large sizes and shapes.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as bones and thumbs and the like.
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	if it is possible to cover them with soft and subtle cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as bones and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	if it is possible to cover them with a wide and strong cloth, because large wounds embrace the whole limb and restrain it equally from all sides, so that there is no slackness
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then I will bind the limb lightly, three tours or four according to the limb, and I will restrain the hand one inch above the break, and I will loosen the break a little, so that the break moves a little
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the limb a little here and there, as much as you take a great part of the limb itself, then take hold of the limb once more, and turn the joint back into its socket.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then bring to the lower part of the fracture, and hold it moderately, not too strong or too weak, as we said earlier.</start_of_turn>
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the joints some strips of linen or bandages, so that they are all even, and then bind everything up above with a bandage, and then put on your splints well made, if there is no abscess or swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, put on something soothing to the abscess, which will stop the swelling, and leave it like that for a few days.</start_of_turn
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain upon your thumbs, and let them be half of a broad cane resting steadily, or of wire from which you make nails, or of round stones, and let them be in this fashion:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the thumb that you place on the fracture be thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it is necessary for the part of little or great size;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then hold the bones as before, just as you did at the first hour, and then bind them with a thread following the breeze, as before on the brimstone.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	The closer the binding is, the less;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And make sure the thread is medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the thread is thick, like those fools who make their wounds with linen cord, it is a great error, for the ligature will not be even if it is too taut.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is nauseated by the nails after stripping in the flesh, if you put down nails of linen or coarse cloth, it will not stain.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the nerve is fractured, I will speak of the cure later on.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	The wounds that it is not possible to restrain with the hands must be grasped from the toes of the limbs which break first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, one must not force the bones into place before five or seven days or more, according to the severity of the wound that has escaped.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And thus the manner of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion.
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And thus it is that you take flour that stays as by the walls of a mill, and mix it with egg yolks, and make this confection, not too fine nor too thick, and use it. And this is the common manner of plaster that restores fracture in various positions, and even for women and young children, for there is neither too much chalk nor too little.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of plaster that restores fracture and dislocation and torsion:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take pitch, lard, alum, saffron, gum arabic and mugwort, in the amount of ten to twelve parts.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	resin and aloe, in the amount of five to six parts
alechil VIIII З.;	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And make powder of them, and mix it with the yolk of an egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	And if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it restores broken bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plaster which is worth more than torsion:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mustard and vinegar, mix in the proportion of X to Z
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	and mix with myrrh and aloes, in the proportion of seven to nine
acaice VI З.;	cayenne six to nine
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	camphor ten to nine, and grind it well, and confit with water or the yolk of an egg, and administer it
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Other methods of treating dislocations and fractured bones consist of relaxing the pain, removing the swelling, and using an external support.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new linen, moisten it in oil and water, and put it on the limb.</start_of_turn>
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These treatments do not restore me, but it is good to appease the after-burning heat, and properly relieve the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of reduction which restores fractured bones.</start_of_turn>
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, mix them together, and make a poultice.</start_of_turn
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of reducing dislocations is to restore the break of the bone and mitigate the remaining heat
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take wormwood root, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, henbane seeds, one part of rue.</start_of_turn
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind them together, mix with wine, and if the limb is pale, mix with moist coriander water or wine.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of restoring the limb are more forceful than the first, when an abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take root of chamomile, and flaxseed, marshmallow, melilot, and gentian, and violets and chamomile flowers, of all an equal part.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Grind them together, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates in his book does not put anything on the broken limb to restore force except for some wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between soft and firm.</start_of_turn>
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says we must put something warm on the affected limb to restore it, such as mustard, aloe, incense and the like, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method of treatment that is useful for wounds and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	take mugwort and chopped onions, or fennel seeds, and chamomile, and mix them equally, and grind them, and make a poultice of it and apply it liberally
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then wash it away a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, and that the bones of the limb are not displaced
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	If they do not loosen with hands for days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	If pain comes to the limb, or swelling, sense rest or inflammation, if you hurry, loosen it and hold the bone in place now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a lighter bandage, and a sponge of sea salt, and immerse in water, and elevate the limb, until the swelling ceases and the pain is relieved
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then leave the limb rest for an hour, and put on dry cloth, soaked in water or oil of rose, and bind with a bandage, until you are certain that the wound has healed.</start_of_turn>
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and rest the inflamed limb, and relieve the pain, and then restart the bandage slowly, and a little displacement, and do not tighten too much.</start_of_turn
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And must be subtle so that it is harmless.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess is swollen, red, painful, and inflamed throughout, and that it persists despite initial treatment, you must repeat the procedure as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if no movement appears in the limb after what has been said, do not force it to be released until after three days or four, or five or seven;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And in no case leave it for twenty days, according to what is seen, until the bruise has disappeared, and approach the junction of the bone above
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Therefore more restraint must be used than before, and the swelling must be increased, as I said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see the limb become drier than usual, the swelling will not rise again;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then apply hot water every time you release it, and do this every third hour, and cut a little piece of lint every time.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	By this work, therefore, cut off the nourishment of the limb, and stay away from these fools who make it worse, and restore the limb promptly.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is bad, and if there is doubt and fear, I see nothing else but to leave it alone and treat it directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways to break bones, various figures, and the causes are diverse;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	because there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a spear, and the collar of bone all the way down to the syphus which is the socket of the bone, as in the case of a splinter or fistula;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this type of fracture is called a fracture of the bone
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	or the spear pierces the bone from below in a forward direction, and this type of fracture is called an absolute fracture
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And it is the wound of these two large or small breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or snap of a bone, or fracture of the bone above the joint, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a burst wound, which approaches the gut that is below the bone, or it is on the bone, and is this wound great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is sutured in the bone as finely as a thread, and the break is small, it is called a “capillary” break.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by a pierce or by stone, or by a fragment of something similar, and causes the bone to protrude, and the limb is askew like the cauldron when it boils over
si entre li piere dedens.	If there is a piece of bone between the pieces
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this is more with children who have soft bones;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	And there are many other ways of breaking bones that are described in small pieces like stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I shall speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all kinds of fractures due to the separation above them, the tension at the edges, and the corrupt marrow that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The blood vessels are recognized by this: when one discovers a bone, and wipes over it, if the black fracture is open
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, take care of the patient’s condition, and if you see no other mishap, like vomiting of bile, emission of urine, extension, and paleness, fever and swelling, and other similar things, if not, it is certain that the matter will not recover without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if no sudden accident befalls thee, and thou hopeth for health, if so, commence the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the swelling comes first to thee, and it be in the armpit, if so, know that it is necessary to remove the bone from the quadrant above the muscle which thou dost touch.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it be in this state, if thou hast haste to remove the bone from the seventh quadrant above the bone, thereby that the bone of the armpit be corrupted, and comes the accident which we have said.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if a break of a bone comes right up to the cloth covering the brain, if you must make an incision there
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and take hold of the patient's head and uncover the bone in every way you can, and on the figure of the wound more cruelly than you can, and if blood comes out from uncovering the bone, or from incisions, if you can, put on some cloth soaked in rose oil over the wound
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and rest the wound until the incisions are healed, and be sure to stop bleeding
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to reduce the bone, and that is done in two ways:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One way if it is that you grasp the narrow tail end forward, and that is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another tail that is larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second way if it is that you have many different sized nails, some narrow and others wide, and be pointed, and be made of iron indeed.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And gently work, that you do not break the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is thick and hard, if you must pierce through, even though you administer nails with washers, do not make them go through the bone more than necessary, and must have under the head of the nail a margin or a circle, that does not allow the point to pass through the bone
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	And you must have several of them, so that bones do not come in place of the thickness of the bone, if you have washers for all tests
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three ways of cautery.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	And the one who wishes to pierce around the bone is that you put one cautery on the bone and turn around twice until you know that the bone is pierced
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put the other cautery elsewhere a little later, and do this all around; then cut the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you did before, and lightly, as we have said, until you have brought the bone to your hand, or to any instruments that you have like nails, pins or the like
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And keep that you do not touch the brain or the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and treated, if it is possible, reset the fragment which is displaced from the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it must be more tense and subtle than the other incisor
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if it lingers nothing of the small bones, no nails, if the bones are lightly struck by a foreign object.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with sutures and bandages as we have said
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of work is like that of the Galenicians, which is more certain
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the load is very strong, and that is its word
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either the fracture that appears swollen, so that when you have uncovered that part, put on gloves and grasp the handle of this incisor lens, for this is its form.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	Do not split it from one side, and is the part most affected by two coasts, if it is split towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then hold it with a small mallet above, so that you can easily compress the bone all around, and take care of the dressing that is below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If the socket is loose with the bone, slightly move the bone because one must well position it firmly, and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks but does not pierce the skin, cut the bone only slightly above; there are small pieces remaining. If you can repair the fracture, remove the sharp fragments with blunt instruments of various sizes, in order to close as many cavities as possible, according to the work and the appearance of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there are large fragments remaining, and after further bluntness, and it does not stop, continue to do so until it is well done.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	Concerning other minor capillary ruptures and superficial breaks, it is necessary that you provide the cause in accordance with its location.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that is not easily understood by one who has not studied this art
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the surface is discovered, it is necessary that you take a drape of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and put it on the wound
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another drape doubled in two or three, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first drape
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Leave the hair longer and even; do not pinch it at the root. Hold the eyes steady until they grow.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	Leave the hair longer and even; do not pinch it at the root. Hold the eyes steady until the abscess is calmed, then remove it, and give medicines such as root of iris, alum, incense powder, and arnica, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	Make a powder of these things and apply it to the wound, and give more medicines that are bitter tasting.</start_of_turn>
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	Keep the wound clean and dry, do not let it become infected, do not let it swell up, for when it swells on the head of the brain, if it is pressed and twisted, it brings great harm to the patient.</start_of_turn
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when one places upon the face something biting, if it does not desist from below.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Beware then, if no other misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, if there is any doubt or suspicion.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	When one puts upon the face something biting, if it does not desist from below, except for the medicine that has been placed upon it, so be it that one takes one part honey, three parts rose oil and one part beeswax, and put it upon the face.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it in the manner of healing that is appropriate, as long as it is safe.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Never break the two parts of the nail together, or only one at a time, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	These bones are cartilaginous and do not break easily, except when forced to bend or twist, and then they are healed
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	If one of the two parts is broken, if you swallow your thumb or pulp of the index finger or push it into the palm, as long as it does not return to its natural position.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	Do it gently, and take care that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is on the upper part of the limb, and it cannot be reached from below, it is proper that you place it even with the head of a splint as wide as a thumb.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	If the break is of two parts, if you do it again, and hurry to restore the first part if you are able to do so;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	otherwise, after the seventh or tenth day, when the inflammation of the wound has subsided, then bind up the thumb tightly with linen thread if the break is on one side
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you swallow the other side if the break is there.</start_of_turn>
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let the tents be so large that they fill the holes where need be.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer shall move the bandages from the wound, and must die each one for himself.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It seems to me that this is good, but it is fitting that they be soft in the making of eggshell and wheat flour
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilages hardened
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	Never put goose feathers in place of the tents, and if there is too much cloth, roll it up tightly, hold the brim steady, and blow on the patient among them
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do as you see fit
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if someone’s clothes come to the neck while you are working, if you put some butter or cotton soaked in rose oil, or some potage of alum.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	If the abscess does not come out, if you touch it with your hand, put plaster on it with linen, wheat flour and incense powder, confirmed with eggshell, then put on light pressure, do not bind it too tightly
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the bone is small and it is broken into many pieces, if the extraction has suitable instruments for this, then close the wound, and treat the surrounding tissues with char, soldering, if like plasters and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no displacement of the bone, if you cure the wound, and put on bandages, as long as it is healthy.</start_of_turn>
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the route of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without injury to the surrounding tissues, and the fracture is slight, and not deeply fractured, except for the teeth which must be loosened gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the upper part, to bite your thumb of the affected hand in the mouth of the patient.</start_of_turn
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you hold your right thumb of the right hand, and hold the fracture slightly, and support it with the other hand forward, and make it even.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in .ij., if it is recommended that you administer extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movement of the teeth arises, or looseness, if strained by a gold or silver or silk thread, then put on a broken jaw cerate and put on a double drape.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put on a great cushion of felt or a piece of leather equal in size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it on to the tooth that you put in, and command the patient to rest, and chew soft food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure changes, if it comes loose at the third joint, and then reset it in place again;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put on a plaster on, with powder of cloves with plenty of egg or breadcrumbs, after that you have oiled the cerate.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And put on the shoulder a soft lining, and if it is displaced again, let the patient know that it is not changing; leave it as long as it remains healthy.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Often it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a wound comes out, if it threatens what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, repair it so that no piece of the bone is left as bone;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If the bone is slightly bent, it has coved things together with it
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, if it has flared up as you need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have sutured all these pieces, and there is no more bleeding, if the wound is wide, and put on some covering materials that cover the wound, to absorb moisture, until it is healed
de la forcele	and strong.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The force breaks many times before, over the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Or it is broken and detached in two pieces, and there are fragments, and it is the most delicate to restore
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is fracture with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	Or if there is fracture with wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the limb that feels the force of the fracture;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the limb towards the part.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then put the fracture in its place, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor swelling
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	and if you have to extend more, put around the patient’s limb a round ball of wax, or cloth, as large as you need;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	extend and hold the fracture steady, and strain the sphere in your hand, so that you put the fracture in its place as it should be.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you are unable to manage the head of the shoulder when it comes out of its place, because it will slip downwards, you must know that the patient lies groaning on his heel, and put the shoulder in its place, that is, the middle ear, and hold the minister in the lower part of the shoulder until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then address the fracture to your shoulder, and if you find debris there, if you must, make an incision above.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	then pull out the pieces slightly, and if the bone cannot be reunited by any means, if it is at one of the incisions you have made;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but hold the forceps steady, for this instrument is used to prevent infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and appears like a spoon, and is not at all curved, and be as wide as it seems necessary, according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and has two holes, as you see, and one is large and the other is small, as is the fracture of the wound you made when you treated the bone
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of the depth of the wound, if the wound is small, or if you are uncertain of the depth, if necessary use a dressing and bandage, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the wound has become infected, if there is moisture, let draping with oil of roses, and balsam, and wine, and put on it.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The hardening of the bone, when it has wounds and is in pain, is that you put on the bone the plaster of pounded powder and egg yolk, and put on soft stamps above, and put a sponge below the shoulder if you need it.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very broad bandage of a palm width, then put on a double drape on the stamps, and plaster it on
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a slender rod about three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the head of the bandage remains in place;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the cushion on the shoulder, and roll the bandage around the neck, and drain the sore assissle, and drain the painful assissle.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And hold the shoulder steady, and when you see that the ligature holds the shoulder firmly, and you clearly understand that the cushion does not move from the bone socket, if you return the limb once, and when you release the restraint.</start_of_turn>
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And make the patient turn on his back, and put as little pressure on the assissle as possible to raise the limb up.</start_of_turn
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If you align the forcele of the shoulder with the displacement of the scapula, or you bind the arm to the neck, and do not release it until it is well mended, for up to twenty days.</start_of_turn
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it must be done, and hold it tight and leave it thus, until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in eight days, and in less time to anyone.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then restart the dislocation, if you see that there is need for it, and hold and leave it alone until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time than most men.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	There is no other way for the shoulder to break or widen than by touch
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the limb appears according to the figure of the fracture, and it is reset according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put out the limb powder with mill with abundance of egg, and bandage it lightly, and put on a double drape;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put on a broad and soft splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is crooked in any part of the shoulder, if you use that braid of linen, so that the splint rests evenly
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then the stretch with a great firm bend, so that the limb does not move from its place, and look at the mark of each joint.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time that it moves, if the stretch is held, and makes the limb equal to its place if it is forced from its place, and lies the patient on his chest
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or in twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When these numbers are completed, if the dislocation has been reduced, and the limb is painless, because it is not a bone that is easily displaced
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks forward, and does not yield at all, if it remains in place, and the bone, do as we have said concerning the breaking of the forcele to appease the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone sticks forward, and does not yield at all, if it remains in place, and the bone, do as we have said concerning the breaking of the forcele to appease the abscess.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The weight is never broken in the middle, but this often happens;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks outwards.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in two, if it declines with pain, and feels great pain, and is pale, and vomiting blood, and the jaw is split open in the broken bone, and one feels very well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And if the patient lies down and rests his back, put a cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae and unite the costae of the second ribs with your hands, and slightly force them into place until the bone is set as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then put on bandages and support the area under the ribcage, or with another soft cushion, and cover with a bandage, and bind it to the fractured bone, so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And turn the limb round at the back, and hold it steadily, and wait a whole hour before releasing it, and if it has healed, keep the strain on it
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	or if it comes loose, by corrosion or by swelling that comes from within, or pain or abscess, if you hurry and take it out, scrape the wound and address the cause of the cure.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then maintain the displacement, and hold it steady until it is healed.
