de la brisure des costes	And if the patient lies still on his back, put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades and unite the edges of the ribs with your hands, and subtly make them even in all positions until the limb is restored to its normal shape; then put on splints and bandage with fine salt or other soft material, and cover with a cloth, and bind firmly over the broken bone, if it does not move; and turn the limb around the back and strain it gently, and award some time the limb, and if it relaxes, strain it again; and if it comes loose again, because of corrosion or inflammation that comes from the bone, or pain or swelling, if you are hasty, loosen it and remove the splint, and address the cause of the fracture; then restore the splint and strain it until it is healed.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	When the bones break through the skin, it does not come forth but at the greatest distance from the back, and at the head downwards, and it does not bend forth except because they are greasy;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and the scent of it is well known at the inquiry as two should do.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is that you must put the fracture back in its place as it should be
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on a bandage, and bind it with a staple, if you have need of it
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the bones break through the skin is declining downwards, if the patient feels great pain, and points, like from the pleura, because the bone points the cloth
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and vomiting profusely, great quantity of blood, which is a grief of health, and the ancient ones have put great care into it
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if these things are said, it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push out the fracture outwards.</start_of_turn>
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except in the case of ulcers that do not heal, when they have not appeared.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have appeared, if they are healthy.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they say that no one has ever placed a bandage outside the limb to relieve pain, because it is similar to the reason
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Whatever, doubt arises that the vacuum does not suck up the superabundances at the root by the arrangement of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that no one should cover the limb with coarse cloth soaked in oil, but put on bandages between the ribs to keep the wound even, then either cure with a pleurisin dressing, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points the loin, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is necessary to cut on the root of the fractured rib, and it is necessary to put in the instruments to stay the inflammation.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then one must cut the bone further, and treat more gently, and then stitch together the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with sponges, until it is healed
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if pus comes out, if put on moist cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the limb;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure until the limb is healed from the opening of the wound, and be careful above the rib or it must be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	If the rib is fractured,
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Never comes a sudden break of bone from the collar, and then it comes to pass.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	When this is finished and you know if it is healed or not, if you see his hands softened and limp and dead, and that you cannot move or extend them, and if you prick them with a needle, if there is no sensation there
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	The wound is mortal in many situations, and if you move them and feel well when you strain and prick them, the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient is cured, if you put on cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if anything like this comes to the spine of the back, and you see well whether there is blood or not, if you take care that the pieces are softened, and that the accident which is in the hands and on the back is open with violence and vomiting at will
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it has been softened on the belly, if you vomit violently at will.</start_of_turn>
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and sees the ass, if he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	These wounds are mortal.</start_of_turn>
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if you do not work diligently on their cure.</start_of_turn
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen, if the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that if there is abscess of the caul, if you put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk, until it is calmed down.</start_of_turn
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a thread, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, even if he is well.</start_of_turn>

et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then break the bone, then assemble the two limbs of the wound, if it is large, with a staple, and then cure with ointment that will stick to the wound, while he is well.</start_of_turn
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the shoulder is broken, which is called the “fracture of the shoulder”, if you see your pouch of your left hand hanging down, and put it equal to the other hand at your side, then put on the plaster and the bandage if you need to.</start_of_turn

de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	and the fracture of the thigh bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	When the thigh bone is fractured, and if there is swelling, do not have fear of that, for there must be some degree of pain at the head;

Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and the cloth which is the fracture and the figure of the limb.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The adjuncts are those between the shoulder blade and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored in one of two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	When one has taken one fist full of my groin, thus: take two fingers and put them in the top, and place the patient above one seat.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then grasp the limb with your arms beside the fist, until it reaches the elbow, and has in the middle a fist-sized bulge, then place it on no heavy thing or the assistant should extend it backwards
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then put the palm of your hand together, as much as the hand can reach each other, until the bulge returns as it should
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is if you support the patient on his shoulder, and bind the arm to his collar, and order the attendants that one holds what is above the dislocation at his hands, and the other holds the shoulder bones apart, and stretch the skin outwards.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, if you strain I lift the spleen, on the spleen, and extend thumbs of the ministers at his side
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	If the bulge is close to the head of the shoulder, if you must put one half of the fist below the elbow and the other towards the shoulder, below the bulge
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And if the fracture is toward the shoulder, if you can put it in place easily, cautiously, as long as the fracture is even on the shoulder and on the bone.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then set the fracture firmly if possible, and hold it in place, for if it moves again, the bruise will not heal.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if there is a bruise, if it does not move, hold it still for seven days, and put on soft linen and rose oil, until the bruise is healed.</start_of_turn
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then hold it still, and the way to hold it if you place the support on the fracture, then assemble the limb on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest.</start_of_turn
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the swelling persists, as we have said.

si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if the disease proceeds by the virtue of medicine, and you do the meat that we have in front of us, in part as much as the meat is at the first moment;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to recover, let it be greatly.</start_of_turn>
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and limb should be taken back in XL days of every month.

de la brisure du bras	... of the breaking of the arm.
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm consists of two bones, which are called the "femur" and the "humerus," of which one is small and the other which supports the pouch
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and is the socket, towards the small head
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	By chance the large bone of the shoulder is fractured only, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bone is fractured, the restoration is easy, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the great bone is fractured, if the healing is poor, it is more painful than when it is fractured whole.

Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the great bone, if the cure must be forced, it is stronger to break it whole

Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then he puts the eye steady, according to its best form.

et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and the stitches that must be in six stars or arms in various positions.</start_of_turn>
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the iris is in one of the bones or in two.</start_of_turn

If you take care that the swelling does not return to the limb, because it is too tight, then you must soften it, indeed, and leave it alone for a while, until the swelling goes down, and then restrain it.</start_of_turn>

de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	From the breaking of the hand
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the hand is broken or dislocated, if you must know that the patient walks crookedly, and stands directly before him equally.

et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	Then the stretching of a long hair, and let the staple of the beard be as great as the palm of the hand; and hold, if it be necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the wrist, if you must know, put a splint above and one below in the palm, so that the thumb is over and straight, then bind it all around the wrist, and seal the loop between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if it breaks out to neither of us from the two, if it is the pouch, if you put it even, if it be necessary.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	And the stretching with the palm, and if you see that you must put a right little staple to lift the break, and it does not move
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the break is as the other two, if like in the index or one of the others, if you put it even, and bind it with the good side which is after
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	Or you bind them together holding, that the muscle is worth, or you put on a staple, as if it were a pouch
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	Leave the hair long and even, and if you prick them at their root, fix your eyes so they do not move until they grow.
de la cuixe brisie	And if the break comes to neither of us, if it is at the elbow, if you must know; put it even, if it is necessary; and strain it with the palm, and if you see that you must put a right-angle splint to lift the break, and it does not move; and if the break is in another place, if like in the index or one of the others, if you must put it even, and bind it with the two fingers that follow; or you bind them all together, holding firmly, as much as is useful, or you put on a splint, as for a pouch; and take care in the restoration and in the arrangement of the burn, and cure what comes with it, as I have said.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the hip is often broken, and it is well seen when it turns forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	When it is restored, it is held in place by the ligament beneath the fracture, and another one from above
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	The patient lies on his face, and extends his limbs so that his limbs rest equally on both sides
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	When the fracture is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the fracture is close to the root of the thigh bone, if either of the ligaments around the knee joint is ruptured, and the other is stretched by the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And in the same way if it is close to the knee, then either the ligament of the knee must be cut, or the lower extension must be made
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then put the eye back into the socket with both hands, until it is according to its natural figure; and then put in the patch, and hold it, so that it does not come out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is pain in the eye, if you leave it quiet, return to your work and your treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	It is made in a partial manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap around the wound with a bandage two or three fingers wide, and keep the surplus taut, then draw up the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail, and put in a thread long between the bone and the limb, above the joint, and under the head; and keep the thread taut.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then draw up on the limb and on the bone the bandage, and put on the outer bandage, and put a bandage on the bone of the limb
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then use the eighth finger between the leg and the hip of coarse hair to make them even, and start to tie three or four threads over the bristle;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And the more you go up the bristle, and the less you strain;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then take two threads of the kind you have between the leg and the hip, and tie three knots that are beneath, and then release the thread from the grasp of the thumb as long as you see the thread going down;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And the strain, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, and do not cause any swelling or any other sign.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if there is swelling, if the dislocation has been addressed, and if it is necessary to do so as we have said many times before
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	If there are pieces of bone that are pricked, if you can cover them, do not attempt it.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	If you cannot cover them, if you must, cut open the limb and drain the pus.</start_of_turn>
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	Treat it as we have said, so that it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never break the limb while these bones are set, as in the shoulder and arm.</start_of_turn
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	However, in the restoration of the limb when it is done, do not mislead the patient.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And so, if the bone is reset in one day, or less or more, according to the diversity of temperaments.</start_of_turn>
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin street.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Hair that is in the groin has often burst, but it falls many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	If it breaks, if not a mere split or opening, and if there is pain, wound or sensation of pain, this is very well indeed.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is that which brings together what is rounded to its sides, as long as it is put together firmly.</start_of_turn
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then place the support, and I put a round peg, if you are in need of it, and tighten it as it should be, then restore all the arrangements that we have said before, if as an abscess cautery and other similar things.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you put a check on every accident that may occur, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if the restoration is done, if you put everything round back in its place, as long as it is put together firmly, put the bandage on, and put on a round cushion, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the instructions that we have said before, as in incision and other things; if you put into each accident what it should be put in, as long as it is sound. And finish the fracture of the limb.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	As for the bones in the limb, there are two, of which one is called the "muscle" and the other is called the "fleshy bone".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And there is often a fracture in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is as for a broken arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, if the limb is twisted from all sides
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a bone is fractured in two, the limb is twisted from the front.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if a large bone is fractured, if one feels great pain, and it is well seen;
et torne desoz.	and it breaks out loud.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then bring extension, and set it even, and bind the edges evenly.
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but in this case, if the fracture is severe, and there are many pieces, that the extension is less severe and lighter
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and let it be as you are skilled.

puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap around two layers of bandage below and above, and bind it firmly in the middle, so that the limb does not deviate to the right or left, and that is good
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	And no one administers me elsewhere for a long time on the limb, and it is of no avail, and one sets on the limb to prevent movement, and it is done quickly in the case of fracture or wound.

si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the wound is complete, that is to say sane.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of bone fractures which are painful.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but in the bones of the limb there is no fracture at all, and two must suffice; and there is no other reason except for fear of death.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a break in the bone, and you see these bones crowding each other, if you put the limb so that it touches the ground as if it were falling, and then put your limb back in place, where the bones were raised, and press until they return to their place.</start_of_turn>
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then put the dressing and stamp on, and put some gauze on the limb a little above two inches wide, and press the limb steadily, and that you have wrapped the limb with cloth and other things as needed.</start_of_turn
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if you loosen the dressing, because you will find the bones equal, whether they are fractured or displaced.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are two breaks, if you restore them, as we have said, you must have two hands.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put at each break a staple according to the length of the two, and be it a little wider; then put the pieces together as I have said, and strain evenly
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three, or more, breaks, break each one; then put on each break a staple according to its quantity, wrapped in one layer of linen, and strain the pieces together.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And be firm on the head of the bone against the belly of the piece, so that it will hold well.

et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And treat each accident as it comes.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the thumb bone.</start_of_turn>
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bones of the female have been broken, if you make her sit with her back arched, and support her behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the belly with the nature of the patient's discomfort, and put as much in as I stop;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then loosen the woman, and hold her back and forth, and then pull out the cotton, until it comes out of the nature, and bring back the bones with the stop;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she has urinated, if the bone is pulled out by the cotton, and when she has urinated, she will recover, and do this for seven days or until it heals
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	if it is restored the fracture, and if you see it, take a bladder of Berber, and bind it to the part with a bandage, and put all the bladder in the nature;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow into the cannula until the bladder is evacuated completely.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	When the nature returns, the bursting will be finished

de brisure avec plaie	From the break with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, as if it were the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that it be set now, as the pain that we have mentioned testifies.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is well healed, if there is only a stain of vitriol, if you have nothing else, then resume the fracture in this way, or in that way, as soon as possible, for if there is no further displacement, the fracture will heal on its own.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there is displacement of the bone, if you leave the fracture undisturbed until the swelling subsides, as long as the displacement is not too great, and do not touch the bone or the surrounding tissue, for you will risk causing further damage.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks are apparent on the surface like a discovered wound, then you must know that you must press them lightly with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	If swelling does not appear to you to put your hands even, if the ravine has this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and its breadth is in accordance with the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary at the root that it grasp three or four inches, according to what is necessary in the wound cure for breakage;

Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	It is called "palainche", because it must be placed over the visible head of the bone.

Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, it is likely that the marrow is not in its natural position.

et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put anything on the wound except butter or anything else that may cause putrefaction and corruption;

et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	And often have they done this thing to fools, and have made the patient mad, or caused his death, or corroded him never.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Or let them be softer and more flexible than the other breaks.

mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	then cover the wound with a thick cloth instead of stakes, and bind tightly.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after one or two days that the wound is swelling, if the bone that you put on top has remained there for a long time, and if you put on healing dressings, like with tetracycline and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the limb three times a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be immobilized in part as much as is possible so that it does not bend excessively easily.</start_of_turn>
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the limb persists in its displacement, and it cannot be reduced but returns to its place spontaneously, with small pieces of bone, because it is necessary that you reduce the wound with care, and pull out all these broken pieces that cause this pain.</start_of_turn

par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	By chance, after twenty days or thirty, the wound will have healed; then cure the wound if you wish.

des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	From the beard which comes out from the beard hair.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often come after the safety of the armpit, even near the joint, and it is useful to see the position of the limb.</start_of_turn

si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if he has administered astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and ochre, acaice, and similar things, so that you take none of these things, or all together, and mix them with a stiptic wine or with abundant egg or with oil.</start_of_turn
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	And put it on the knot firmly, and strain it well, and do not release it from the hands until it stays.

dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after the bandage
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture has been restored, and rests after the limb is weak and limp, if there is any cause for it,
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	if there is anything causing it, it is because it was too tightly bound and was not properly bound as it should have been.

ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because there is much blood in its substance, if it is weak

dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the disease.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the limb is deformed, although it does not lose its natural work
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	although those fools say that the limb must be broken anew, and many have held this opinion in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	it is blamed, and there comes great harm, and by chance the patient dies.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	Toutefois, si les nodulations et la torture sont frais, si vous peut leur faire renaître d’eau chaude, ou herbes mollélifiantes soient cuites, comme feuille de vismalve, et racine, et mellilote, et cetera.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	However, if the swellings and the torture are fresh, if you can make them arise from warm water, or cooked softening herbs such as balm leaves, and roots, and melilot, and so on; and apply a liberal plaster, as with aquaintance well made, take the nourishment of balm, and confirm with butter of gelatine or oil of poppy seed, and apply the plaster on top.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	Or take fat figs, and grind them with poppy seeds, and similar medicines which appease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone loosened by continuous rubbing and length of time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And provide movement to the limb at the shoulder hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the swelling is tough and hardened, like stone, and need iron, if you cover it just until the bone, with a slight incision;
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And put cushions and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And thus begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no more, if you can now restore its normal position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if we delay, if it swells up in the limb, and by chance we reset it, we will have pricked the limb on the way.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	For in this case we must not move it while it is swollen
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	often brings vomiting and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	however, when this has happened, if you make the patient comfortable, then leave him, until the swelling has subsided
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the limb with warmth and oil, and support it lightly, and treat each limb as it comes to its place
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint to the end of the foot.
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	When the mandibles are loosened and the dislocations of both are in two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	Or they are a little stiff in their limbs, and soften a little.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Or they are entirely loosened, and hang towards the ear, and keep their saliva in their mouth so that they cannot hold it, cannot close their mouths, and wrap their tongues with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it will often spontaneously reduce on its own.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if they are whole and complete, if you must force them, then you must do it instantly, and do not linger;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the attendants hold the patient’s head firmly, and hold your gaze somewhat below the pocket of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands are loosened, to make them even
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And instruct the patient to soften his teeth, jaw, and move them all around.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And his eye should be level, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if they are crooked, even if both jaws are together, if they are raised with sharp heat and oil, until they are gently softened;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not force the return, as we have said before.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	When they are returned equally, and the patient’s mouth is closed with good sense, put on soft cloths soaked in rose oil and beeswax, then bind them lightly with threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on his back, and his arms resting between two cushions, so that they do not move forward or backward, do not attempt to force anything, but gently seize meat, until the pain is gone, and keep the jaws still
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Then he must swallow what he wants lightly, and do not work himself to open his mouth to swallow or drink, until the jaw is well numb and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws do not manage to be returned to their point at an hour, and are not otherwise converted at their leisure, if thereby fever and customary sickness arise, and by chance solution of the belly, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	When you see that, then know that it is a loss of blood;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and often death occurs from it in nine days
de la forcelle	of the forceps.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot remove from the bone without causing damage, and is useless every time it is attempted, and one can well tell.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is when the patient lies groaning on his back, and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	then press the limb firmly towards your palm, and it will return
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then place the bandage and bind it well, and strain it
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the one who is beside the knife cannot unbind it
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	Se poc non, et si il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then put on the support and the bandage, and strain it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and in this way the head of the shoulder is brought back into its place when it has been dislocated from its bone
de la dislocation de l’espaule	From the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	The shoulder is not dislocated except in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one that it dislocates at the shoulder blade at the armpit
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second at the top of the arm;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	And by chance it becomes loosened at the upper part, and this happens often.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and does not loosen behind for the scapula, and does not loosen from the inside for the nerves.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and often loosens downwards towards the buttocks, even among those who have plenty of flesh, because of these jumps they suffer greatly
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	because of those who have enough flesh, these jumps cause pain and return with pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens that there is a fracture or dislocation, and it inflates the shoulder with a hot abscess, and care must be taken that it is not displaced by this.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is therefore necessary that you expect it, until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocation is when it is pulled towards the buttocks, and distinguishes between the sick scapula and the healthy one, and you will find between them their diversity manifested
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and loosen the shoulder blade at the touch of the head of the shoulder, as if it were a bone.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you cannot make the patient move their hand back to its place, or move in any way
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	Also, if it is displaced upwards, if not hidden, for you will find it clearly at the touch
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this way of dislocation is not strong enough to restore it, when it is new, or if the patient is suffering
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	The way is that the physician holds the patient’s hand up above, then puts his thumbs under the shoulder blade, and holds the joint firmly up at the shoulder
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	And the minister holds the hand, and extends it upwards, because he puts it down.
si venra hastanment.	if it comes to harm.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said before, if it is known that the patient is in pain; then it must be that the patient be bathed in warm water
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the minister brings comfort that is soothing and calming, such as decoction of alum and fenugreek and honey in water, and the like.</start_of_turn>
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then put the patient on his back, and put under the seat a cushion of linen even, not too soft or too hard, and put the thumb of the hand over the cushion, and hold the shoulder joint firmly, and treat the hand of the patient.</start_of_turn>
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	And one other attendant grasps the head of the patient, so that it does not move backwards.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	Then the dislocation returns immediately, and if you see that it remains fixed in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that you make the patient groan in pain more than he suffers;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	then you must stretch the shoulder downwards towards the costal margin, and hold the shoulder away from the patient’s side, and keep the shoulder high up so that the patient’s shoulder hangs down vertically.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another attendant treats the patient’s arm behind the belly
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too light, if he can carry nothing heavy, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And so it is also remedied in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and by keeping the head of the shoulder long and tense in the earth, so that the head of the humerus is as resonant as the pestle, and is neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	Then let the patient lie down, but that he should have a soft blanket over, and that the patient should be quiet for a long time.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then extend his arm from the other side and the joint will return to its place firmly
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not return with all these things that we have said, if you do this cure:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take two thumbs and three fingers wide, which has the head resting on the bone to enter under the armpit, as in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then place over the head of the arm a soft blanket, so that the arm does not bleed the patient, and then put it under the armpit of the patient
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend the arms above the arm for a long time, and hold the shoulder against the arm, and the hand on the head of the arm, and put the arm over one inch of a fingerbreadth, and let the forearm hang down, and leave the shoulder hanging down on the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The jointure remains firm now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is corrected, in whatever way it is, if you command that you put behind the shoulder a ball of wool as long as it is even, then put on the shoulder pad with a sprinkle of wheat flour, with incense and alum on the whole shoulder and around, then strain out behind the shoulder immediately, and turn the limb on the shoulder pad, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands still.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that it move slightly, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	Then move it more after five or seven days, and move it regularly
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And if it is stiff and cannot be softened, if it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	If the joint is forced out of place by moisture or any other cause, then you must administer cautery three times over, as it is placed before or alongside the cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all of this, and it comes loose after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot lift your arm up, then the nerves at the head of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened.</start_of_turn
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and the joint will never be stable in its place.</start_of_turn>
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation which is towards the elbow, and the upper arm, or behind, if it is made by impulse, and extension of the hands, and it is administered with another binder.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heals as long as it is whole.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb complains by remaining stiff, if the patient uses it many times, while the stiffness gradually subsides, it returns to its former state.
de la dislocation dou coute	And if after healing the limb complains by remaining stiff, if the patient uses it many times, while the stiffness gradually subsides, it returns to its former state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	When the joint of the shoulder is loosened at the points, and comes back at the points;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and is loosened all around, both front and back, and the dislocation is not properly restored, for it is seen and felt well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and is loosened like a deformed limb
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the patient with the limb, if he wishes to see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is tight, and cannot bend the arm, touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	and you must immediately re-establish it even if it comes out again, for if it comes out again, if it is repeated, it will cause great suffering to bring it back
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	And by chance it cannot be returned all at once, even if it is at the back.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	If it is more serious than the others, and causes greater pain, and by chance death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	When it is restored, if it is like this that we can bring it back, you stretch your hand with both hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the arms are spread out, and the hands down towards the navel, up and down, and keep the joint together with its bones joined, or at the root of the bone, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and hold it from the root of the limb that is relaxed.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, give strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and two assistants extend the limb and hold it for extension, so that it does not move during extension.</start_of_turn
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	Then twist the arm from the shoulder outwards, and when you have enveloped a double-layered bandage long and wide around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when you look at the joint of the limb, if there is any oil on the joint to soften it, then stretch the joint until it snaps back into place.</start_of_turn>
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is fixed, if you put on dry packing with an egg-shaped weight, and the strain is complete, and you support the limb at the collarbone of the patient, and leave it for a while, then remove it.</start_of_turn>
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firmly in its place, leave it alone and leave it alone.</start_of_turn
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	And if you see that the joint does not settle well, repeat the packing and the weight, and leave it like that until it is firmly set.</start_of_turn
puis le deslie.	Then he lets go.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	Then if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, if you bathe him and wipe him thoroughly, and press until it is relieved;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you put on the joint a fat mutton nail, then leave it in place for a day and a night, and then remove the nail, and wash it;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, wipe the joint gently, and then put the nail back, and then enter or bathe.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this two or three times until he is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see, put on a wet poultice soaked in urine with chaff, and strain it on;
si revenra a sa disposition.	If it returns to its place.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	If the shoulder joint is loosened and the return is easy, more than the others.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to restore it to its place immediately, while it is loosened, even if the limb is swollen or there is an abscess

And restore it if you place the affected limb on a table, extend the limb, and look at its position, so that it places its palm on the surface of the joint and holds it until it returns to its place
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, take note that you must watch to see if it is truly in its place
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the patient’s hand behind their back on a table during extension and reduction

And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and I look put his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it comes back now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the strain of the relaxed post-treatment hair causes the wound to reopen, and you leave it in its original position, it must recommence.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if you cannot bear it, and you do not put it back after a few days, the joint will become stiff.</start_of_turn
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and do not cause any pain to the patient except when the hand is softened, and cannot move anything at all.</start_of_turn
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	therefore, when the nerves are cut or the arteries are clipped.</start_of_turn
