Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at rest, if you put on the bandage that we have mentioned, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove it and leave it be.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no pain, if there is hot swelling, and you rub it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulder of the arm</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Never are the thumbs desoiled at the wrist, never at the back of the palm or the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Therefore, hold the thumb steady, and support the dislocation until it returns, then keep the head of the thumb towards the part where it is joined.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	Leave it for two days, and then put it even again.
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	And do not bind it, as we have said, and do not move it, and bind it tightly
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Do it often, until it is firm, and do the same if it is desoiled at the belly of the thumb, and do as you did before, until it is healed
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do the same if it is desoiled from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Due to the loosening of the scapula from the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the scapula of the back or the neck is loosened, or if there are several loosenings, if there is no remedy, for the patient’s life is in jeopardy.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And if the patient egests spur or urine contrary to their usual course, they will not be able to hold it, and often their limbs will be softened, or both thighs or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the limb will slip at three parts.
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	The one that slips at the back is called "gilbosite".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The cure is that if the "gilbosite" comes from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no cure or healing in all
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	and that which comes from sitting or from blows or from similar things, say the old methods of treatment with great words, or there is no great benefit in them;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have abridged it according to my intention, and I have composed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes before the bite, there is no remedy;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And just as much as that which comes directly on two coasts, one cannot cure fire only for what comes from behind, as I have said
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And it is that the patient should extend his face on one side and suffer from his eyes, without blinking.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then I take a fist and put it at the head of the sufferer’s arm, and I take another and put it by the elbow, and I bind the upper part of the patient’s arm with a bandage, and I take another and put it on the thigh, and I take another and put it on the calf, and another on the ankle
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	And two ministers know the limits, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two thumbs.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And be well closed, the thumb as we have said, and the eye looks put its palms on the spine, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this cure, take a handbreadth long, and hold the thumb down, and the patient lies on the side, and put the thumb of the handbreadth down by the side, then put the middle of the handbreadth on the spine
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put the eye of the thumb on the other thumb of the handbreadth, and press well, until it returns to its place
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see that it breaks the nail that breaks at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you pinch two times at the head of the patient of an arm of great size, and over the pieces two others, and between each pinch, a sow and an ounce, a palm of space of length.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and between each pinch, I make a hole, or the knot turns right, and let the pin be firmly in the ground so that it does not move.</start_of_turn>
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between two pins there is one pin that returns, so that the thread returns, and there are two small pins of a palm in length to secure the knot.</start_of_turn>
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then the thread that is among the pins at the knot over the head, and the other thread over the pieces at the other knot, and between these two pins turn their knot to the whole thread, and the master puts in the pin even as we have said.</start_of_turn
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put upon an absorbent plaster with much yolk, and then press, and then support with a tablet of three fingers' length, that it may encompass the belly of the rib and the part of the spine that is sensitive; then bind with a thread, as we have said, and use the patient with subtle nourishment until he is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if nothing comes to an end of the sickness, if it is necessary, it is to administer soothing and relaxing medicines, with the support that we have mentioned before.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And never give a piece of lead, and never does the appearance come from behind the spin of the back, and take care that this is not a dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	it is the bone that is opened, for we must not presume otherwise.
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	By chance death comes to pass.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the shoulder.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	The joints of the thigh and the shoulder only come loose by dislocation, and do not come loose like the others;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	The thigh joint is loosened in three parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	front and back, and front and back
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	the more inward it is, the more it is loosened front and back
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of dislocation inwards is that when one joins the painful limb with the flesh, if it is longer, and opens more the patient's belly than before, and cannot double his knee over the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the lord who is taken away by excessive heat, for in this case the head of the shoulder comes loose
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that this accident is contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the sign of the one who has it in front, if he has it well his limb according to the accomplishment.
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	However, do not double the knee joint because of pain, and if you see him making a fart, if he cannot hold it back, he will urinate, and swell his belly, and when he walks, he will pass over his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that he cannot expand his knee, cannot double it, and is that his limb is shorter than the other, and his ankle is softened, and that his shoulder joint is dislocated at the root of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	You must bring back this semblance of dislocation if it is an old one, and it will remain according to its disposition, if there is no remedy;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and do not presume anything.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is a matter of three dislocations, if you hurry that you turn the joint, and stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it to the front and the back;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	By chance, if it returns, and there is no need for another remedy.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	If it does not return in this manner, if you must seize it firmly, with two hands or one that is sufficient, that it be bound upon the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	And another minister extends his hand downwards in part as much as he can stretch out his hands downwards as far as his elbows, then grasp it with a thread that is sufficient for the hip bone
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And another holds the head of the limb.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And stretch up and down all at once, until the patient is lifted from the earth at once, and remains suspended
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is often used in this case, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this does not work, it is necessary to apply another remedy.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the shoulder, if it is convenient, command the patient to lie on his side, then put the limb on the root of the humerus, and the limb which is below the elbow, then stretch the limb upwards towards the elbow and towards the forcele.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then take hold of his arms again, embrace the great limb of the painful shoulder, and extend it towards the front:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you do not manage to hold it in this manner as we have said, if it is convenient, tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong thread above the two nails, and above the two knees, and let the painful limb be extended twice as much as the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	Then let it hang from the top of a pole, or on the ground two arms’ length.
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then command the minister to grasp the head of the limb, and let another minister hang beside the patient, who graspes the limb, for the joint now returns firmly.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is out of place, if the patient lies down, as we have said in the case of hiccuping, grasp the limb properly above and below the painful area.</start_of_turn
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two cushions, one at the head and one at the foot, and put one cushion between the thighs of the patient in the form of a cross.</start_of_turn
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And put moist towels around the area, so that it does not bleed the patient, then extend the thumbs of the ministers towards him, and the one who has the dislocation put it equal in his hand.</start_of_turn
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on the table. Press on it as we said in the previous case, and keep the patient lying on the right side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is forward, if it is necessary to extend the affected limb immediately, do as I have said.
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and place the eye of the pain over the painful limb, then press on the other hand, and extend it towards the navel.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is backward, if it is not possible to extend the limb forward, do not lift it up from the ground, but rather that it be as if it had been dislocated backward, as we have said above concerning the two fingers;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	be on its face, and the limb is extended as we have said before, and must be pressed on the joint at the table
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and will be at rest when the limb is straightened, and will be even.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	Therefore, grasp the thighs and place the support, and strain with a bandage, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rest for three days or four, then remove it, and place the support upon it
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, if strained as before, and leave them for three days
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then remove it, and make it swell gently, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of dislocation from the shoulder-blade.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	namely, forward and backward, and downward;
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not damage it in front
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	and the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not move to his thigh, the dislocation has not been reduced;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his limb if he can, and place your hand on his back, and place his foot on your knees.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	Then take his shoulder joint in your palms, and pull inwards between your thumbs, then bend his two ribs forming the shoulder joint.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	And another minister extends his foot, until the shoulder joint returns to its place, and the sign is that his limb is properly aligned with his hip slightly bent
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	And place the bandage on, and make the limb breathe freely at the hip, and keep it bound firmly for three days or four, and then remove it
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And do not move the patient too much, until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at its proper place, if an extension is administered strongly, as we said in the treatment of the hernia, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of dislocation.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The talons never is measured, and never is fully evacuated, and always is swollen and painful.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign is if the ankle is swollen, and it inclines toward the part where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	If it is slight, one must gently hold it out with the hands when it is only slightly swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely drained, if you must make the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly by the leg under the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then pull the limb towards your right hand, then to the left twice, and then stretch it upwards, and keep the limb well stretched out
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	And do this twice as we have said, while pulling and stretching the limb
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, that is good.
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	If not, if you begin the work again, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	If it cannot return at once, if you make the patient lie face down on the earth, and place your foot firmly on the ground between his thighs, and spread out the blankets around him, that he does not groan;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then hold the limb firmly, and another assistant should extend the limb at his hands or at the elbow, which is placed on the collarbone of the limb.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend the shoulders of the assistants equally, and hold the dressing either beside the thighs of the patient to hold the patient when it is extended
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then place the eyes equally on the dislocation at his hands, and another assistant grasps the limb firmly at the shoulder, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	When she reaches a point, put on the dressing and stamp above, and strain forms, and lie the thumb to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that they are not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then leave it for two or three days, and if the strain subsides, if the tension is released
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then take it off at a third or a fourth, and tell the patient to wait for three days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if it goes before this time, it is not certain that it will not damage again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it persists, it is necessary to know that it must be appeased, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des dois	otherwise
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When they are dislocated, if they are properly repositioned without resistance, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is not in any knot of the bone, it is to be known that you must make the patient sit on one leg or on the table straight, and put your thumb on what is open of these joints, and press your thumb until it returns
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when they are even, and nothing is open, if you put some salt on the plant of the foot and put it on a table for two fingers, then the swelling will form, and leave it for three days, then take it off.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and rest it until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	It is from wound and dislocation together.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When the wound comes with the dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times it has been that the patient died:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you do not know the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and late, do not be bold;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at first soothing things about the abscess, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, if you now restore the limb to its place, even if the incisions remain open;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is in its place, if you administer calming things around the incision, and cure the wound, as it should be, with dried oil;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if there is a fracture of the dislocation, and minor bones are fractured, if the bones are displaced, do as we have said in simple ailments;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	And take care not to enter the way of fear, as I have said, for this will bring you harm according to your Creator, and for the preservation of your soul and body.
